The Ruling on Game Falling into Water
Ruling on prey falling into water after being shot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that falls into water after being shot and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Game that falls into water is not halal because the cause of death is uncertain.

This lesson addresses a specific case in hunting: what happens when the prey falls into water after being shot. The Hanafi school, based on an explicit hadith, rules that such game is not permissible to eat. The key principle is certainty — we must be sure the arrow, not the water, caused death.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
State that game falling into water after being shot is not halal to eat.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim, which explicitly makes an exception for game falling into water.
The hadith is found in Muslim and Bukhari.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning
The prohibition is based on uncertainty (shakk) about the cause of death. The arrow must be the direct cause.
The hadith says: 'You do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.'
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may allow if the arrow wound is clear and the water is shallow, but the Hanafi school insists on certainty.
This is a legitimate difference of opinion (ikhtilaf sahih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان رمى صيدا فوقع في الماء لم يوكل [۲۵۸۹] (۱۰) اگر شکار کو تیر مارا اور وہ پانی میں گر گیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ تیر سے نہ مرا ہو بلکہ پانی سے شکار مرا ہو اس لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ حدیث: عن عدی بن حاتم قال سألت رسول الله عن الصيد قال اذا رميت بسهمک فاذكر اسم الله فان وجدته قد قتل فكل الا ان تجده قد وقع في ماء فانك لا تدرى الماء قتله او سهمک (مسلم شریف، باب الصید بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۲۹۸۲/۱۹۲۹ / بخاری شریف، باب الصید اذا غاب عنه یو مین او ثلاثی ص ۸۲۴ نمبر ۵۴۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شکار پانی میں گر گیا ہو اور وہاں سے مردہ نکالا تو نہ کھائے کیونکہ کیا معلوم کہ پانی سے ہی مرا ہو تیر سے نہیں۔
And if he shoots at game and it falls into water, it is not eaten. [2589] (10) If a hunter shoots an arrow at game and it falls into water, then it will not be eaten. Because it is very possible that it died not from the arrow but from the water, therefore it is not halal. Hadith: From Adi ibn Hatim: I asked the Messenger of Allah about hunting. He said: 'When you shoot your arrow, mention the name of Allah. If you find it killed, eat it, unless you find it has fallen into water, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.' (Muslim, Bukhari) This hadith shows that if the game fell into water and was taken out dead, do not eat it, because it is not known whether it died from the water or the arrow.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) from the Hanafi school regarding the permissibility of eating game that falls into water after being shot. The ruling is that such game is not halal, due to uncertainty about the cause of death: it could be the water rather than the arrow. The proof (dalil) is the explicit hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding the hunter to eat only if he is certain that the arrow killed the game. If the game falls into water, this certainty is lost. The Hanafi school holds this prohibition as a general rule, and it applies regardless of whether the water is a river, lake, or even a small puddle. The underlying rationale is that the weapon must be the direct cause of death; any intervening factor that could have caused death renders the meat unlawful.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animal hunted for food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hunter shoots a deer, and it falls into a river. He finds it dead with an obvious arrow wound. According to the Hanafi school, is it halal to eat?
A) Yes, because the arrow wound proves the arrow caused death.
B) No, because the fall into water creates uncertainty about the cause of death.
C) Yes, because the water is pure and does not make the meat haram.
D) No, because the hunter did not recite Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
Game that falls into water after being shot is not halal due to uncertainty about the cause of death, based on an explicit hadith.

Ruling on Game That Falls from a Height
Ruling on game that falls from a height after being shot.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that falls from a height after being shot, identify the dalil (Quran and athar), and explain the principle of certainty applied.

Core Idea
If the cause of death is uncertain between the arrow and the fall, the game is not halal.

This lesson extends the previous ruling on water to a new scenario: game that falls from a height after being shot. The Hanafi school holds that such game is not halal because the fall introduces doubt about the cause of death. We will examine the proofs from the Quran and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage deals with game (e.g., a bird or deer) that is shot, then falls from a roof or mountain and dies. The ruling is that it is not halal to eat.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites Quran 5:3, which prohibits al-mutaraddiyah (animals that die from falling). This verse is used as evidence that death from falling is unlawful.
The verse is qat'i in transmission (thubut) but zanni in dalala because it does not explicitly address the combination of shooting and falling.
3
Understand the application of the principle
The key principle is certainty (yaqin). Since it is unknown whether the arrow or the fall caused death, the game remains haram. Doubt (shubha) invalidates the halal status.
This mirrors the earlier case of water where doubt about purity leads to impurity.
4
Examine the supporting athar
An athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is quoted: if an animal falls from a mountain after being shot, do not eat it because the fall may have killed it. This reinforces the ruling.
The athar is from Sunan Sa'id ibn Mansur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك ان وقع على سطح او جبل ثم تردَّى منه الى الارض لم يوكل [۲۵۹۰] (۱۱) ایسے ہی اگر چھت پر یا پہاڑ پر گر ا پھر وہاں سے زمیں تک لڑھکا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ شکار کو مارا جس کی وجہ سے شکار چھت پر یا پہاڑ پر گرا اور وہاں سے لڑھکتے ہوئے زمین پر گرا تو وہ شکار حلال نہیں ہے۔ یہ معلوم نہیں ہے کہ تیر سے مرا ہے یا پہاڑ یا چھت سے لڑھکنے کی وجہ سے مرا ہے۔ آیت میں ہے والمنخنقة والموقوذة والمتردية (آيت ٣ سورة المائدة) اور چونکہ یہاں تیر اور لڑھکنے میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اس لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے قال عبد الله اذا رمى احدكم صيدا فتردى من جبل فمات فلا تأكلوا فاني اخاف ان يكون التردى قتله (سنن سعید بن منصور) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہاڑ سے لڑھکا ہو تو حلال نہیں ہے۔
And likewise, if it falls on a roof or a mountain, then rolls from there to the ground, it is not eaten. [2590] (11) Similarly, if it falls on a roof or mountain, then rolls from there to the ground, it will not be eaten. The game is shot, and as a result it falls on a roof or mountain, and then rolls to the ground, that game is not halal. It is not known whether it died from the arrow or from rolling from the mountain or roof. The Quranic verse says: 'and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen from a height' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3). And because here there is doubt between the arrow and the fall, so it is not halal. There is an athar: Abdullah said: 'When one of you shoots game and it falls from a mountain and dies, do not eat it, for I fear that the fall killed it.' This shows that if it rolls from a mountain, it is not halal.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to a similar scenario: game that falls from a height (roof or mountain) after being shot. The ruling is that it is not halal because the cause of death is uncertain between the arrow and the fall. The proof includes the Quranic verse that prohibits animals that die from falling (al-mutaraddiyah), and an athar (report) from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The Hanafi school applies the same principle of certainty: since there is a possibility that the fall caused death, the meat is unlawful. This covers cases where the game falls onto a roof and then rolls off, or falls directly onto a mountain slope and rolls down. The key is that the fall is an additional factor that could have caused death.

Key Terms
متردية (mutaraddiyah): An animal that dies from falling from a height.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hunter shoots a bird that lands on a rooftop, then falls off and dies. According to the Hanafi school, is the bird halal?
A) Yes, because the hunter shot it first.
B) No, because the fall could have caused death, creating uncertainty.
C) Yes, because the bird was shot and then fell, which is natural.
D) No, because the hunter did not recite Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
If there is any doubt about the cause of death—whether from the shot or from the fall—the game is not halal.

Initial Fall to Ground: A Permissible Scenario in Hunting
Ruling on game that initially falls to ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that initially falls to the ground after being shot and explain why the doubt about death from impact is disregarded.

Core Idea
If the game first hits the ground, it is halal—the inevitable fall eliminates doubt.

In hunting, the manner of the animal’s death matters. If it falls into water or onto a height, the ruling is different. Here we examine a specific case: when the game falls directly to the ground. This passage clarifies that the initial point of contact determines the ruling, not any subsequent movement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The game falls to the ground after being shot. The ruling: it is halal to eat.
2
Understand the Doubt
The doubt: did the animal die from the arrow or from the impact with the ground? If from impact, it would be carrion and haram.
Other cases (water, height) exist where this doubt is considered.
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle
The Hanafi school disregards this doubt because every shot game will eventually fall to the ground. The fall is inevitable, so the doubt is not valid.
This is based on the idea that the natural course of events is part of the hunting process.
4
Distinguish Initial vs. Subsequent Fall
The key is the initial fall (ibtida’an). If the game first hits the ground, the ruling applies. If it first lands on a roof or mountain, the doubt remains.
Even if later moved to a different location, the initial fall governs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲) وان وقع على الارض ابتداء أكل [۲۵۹۱] (۱۲) اور اگر ابتدا میں زمین پر گرا تو کھایا جائے گا۔ شکار تیر کھا کر زمین پر گرا اور مرگیا پھر کسی طرح ہو اوغیرہ کے ذریعہ پہاڑ پر یا چھت پر پہنچ گیا تو کھایا جائے گا۔ اس میں بھی اگر چہ شک ہے کہ تیر سے نہ مرا ہو بلکہ زمین پر گرنے کی وجہ سے مرا ہو۔ لیکن چونکہ شکار آخر زمین پر ہی گرے گا اس لئے یہاں اس شک کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا اور شکار حلال رہے گا۔
(12) And if it falls initially on the ground, it is eaten. [2591] (12) And if it initially falls on the ground, it will be eaten. The game is hit by the arrow and falls to the ground and dies; then if it somehow reaches a mountain or roof, it will be eaten. In this case, even though there is doubt that it might have died not from the arrow but from hitting the ground, but since the game will ultimately fall to the ground in any case, this doubt is not considered, and the game remains halal.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage clarifies an exception: when the game falls directly to the ground after being shot, it is halal. The doubt that the impact with the ground could have caused death is disregarded because every shot game will inevitably fall to the ground. The Hanafi school considers this a natural consequence, unlike the cases of water or a height where the fall is not a normal part of the hunting process. Therefore, even if the game later rolls to a roof or mountain, as long as the initial fall was to the ground, it is halal. The key distinction is the initial fall: if it first falls to the ground, the doubt is waived; if it first falls on a roof or mountain, the doubt remains.

Key Terms
ابتداء (ibtida'an): Initially, at the beginning. Here it means the first contact after being shot is with the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a hunted animal initially falls to the ground after being shot, what is the ruling?
A) It is haram because of possible death from impact.
B) It is halal because the doubt is disregarded.
C) It is makruh because of the uncertainty.
D) It is only halal if the animal dies instantly from the arrow.

Key Takeaway
When a hunted animal first falls to the ground after being shot, it is halal—the inevitability of the fall negates any doubt about the cause of death.

Hunting with Mi'rad: The Ruling on Blunt Force vs. Cutting
Ruling on hunting with mi'rad: distinction between cutting and blunt force

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between halal and haram hunting with a mi'rad based on whether the arrow cuts or strikes with blunt force, and cite the Quranic and Hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A mi'rad that kills by blunt force is haram (mawqudhah); only a cutting wound makes it halal.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on hunting with a mi'rad, a type of arrow used in pre-Islamic and early Islamic times. The key distinction is whether the arrow cuts the animal, causing bloodshed, or strikes with its broadside, killing by blunt force without blood. The ruling is derived from the Quranic prohibition of mawqudhah (beaten to death) and the explicit hadith of Adi ibn Hatim. Understanding this helps apply the principle that emergency slaughter requires a wound that lets blood flow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the weapon and its two modes
The mi'rad has a sharp edge (had) and a broad side (ard). The mode of impact determines the ruling.
2
Distinguish between cutting and blunt force
Cutting causes blood loss and is akin to slaughter; blunt force kills by crushing without blood flow.
3
Apply the Quranic prohibition of mawqudhah
Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3 explicitly forbids al-mawqudhah (beaten to death). Blunt-force killing falls under this.
4
Apply the Hadith of Adi ibn Hatim
The hadith directly states: 'If you hit with its sharp edge, eat; if you hit with its broadside and it kills, it is waqidh, so do not eat.'
5
State the Hanafi ruling
Halal if cut; haram if killed by broadside. This is the mufta bihi position based on explicit texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳) وما اصاب المعراض بعرضه لم يوكل وان جرحه أكل [۲۵۹۲] (۱۳) کسی شکار کو لگے۔ بھال کا تیر چوڑائی کی جانب سے تو نہ کھایا جائے گا۔ تیر کا دھار دار حصہ شکار کو نہیں لگا بلکہ لکڑی کا حصہ لگا اور شکار گویا کہ لکڑی کے دباؤ سے مر گیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ شکار زخمی نہیں ہوا اس لئے ذبح اضطراری نہیں ہوا۔ وہ آیت کے مطابق موقوذہ ہو گیا یعنی دبوچ کر مارا گیا ہوا اس لئے یہ حلال نہیں ہے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ حرمت عليكم الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير وما اهل لغير الله به والمنخنقة والموقوذة والمترديه و النطيحة وما اكل السبع الا ما ذكيتم وما ذبح على النصب (آیت ۳ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں موقوفہ یعنی دباؤ سے مرے ہوئے کو حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ حدیث میں کئی مرتبہ صراحت گزری۔ عن عدی بن حاتم ... وسألته عن صيد المعراض فقال اذا اصبت بحده فكل واذا اصبت بعرضه فقتل فانه وقيذ فلا تأكل (بخاری شریف، مسلم شریف) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تیر کی چوڑائی کا حصہ لگا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا کیونکہ وہ وقیذ ہو گیا یعنی دباؤ سے مرا ہوا ہو گیا۔ اور دھار دار حصہ لگے تو کھایا جائے گا کیونکہ وہ ذبح اضطراری ہو گیا۔
(13) And what the mi'rad hits with its breadth is not eaten, and if it wounds it, it is eaten. [2592] (13) If it hits the game with the broadside of a spear-arrow, it will not be eaten. The sharp part of the arrow did not hit, but the wooden part hit, and the game died from the pressure of the wood, so it will not be eaten. The game was not wounded, so no emergency slaughter occurred. It becomes mawqudhah (beaten to death) according to the verse, and therefore not halal. The verse: 'Forbidden to you are carrion, blood, the flesh of swine, and what has been dedicated to other than Allah, and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen, and the gored, and what has been eaten by predators except what you slaughter properly, and what is sacrificed on altars' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3). In this verse, mawqudhah (beaten to death) is declared haram. The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim is clear: 'If you hit with its sharp edge, eat; if you hit with its broadside and it kills, then it is waqidh, so do not eat.' This shows that if the broadside hits, it is not eaten because it becomes waqidh (beaten to death), and if the sharp edge hits, it is eaten because it becomes emergency slaughter.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage deals with hunting using a mi'rad, a type of arrow that can have a sharp edge or a blunt broadside. The ruling distinguishes based on how the arrow strikes the prey. If the sharp edge (had) cuts and wounds the animal, causing bloodshed, it is considered an emergency slaughter (dhabh idtirari) and the meat is halal. If the broadside (ard) hits without cutting, the animal dies from blunt force, which falls under the Quranic prohibition of al-mawqudhah (beaten to death). The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim directly supports this. The Hanafi school applies this by examining the arrow: if it is a standard hunting arrow with a sharp blade, it is halal; if it is a blunt tool like a club or a stone, it is not. However, if the blunt tool cuts the skin and draws blood, it may be considered as emergency slaughter.

Key Terms
المعراض (al-mi'rad): A hunting arrow or spear that may have a sharp edge and a broad side.
موقوذة (mawqudhah): An animal killed by blunt force without bloodshed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hunter uses a mi'rad (hunting arrow) and hits a deer with the broadside, killing it without cutting. According to the Hanafi school, is it halal?
A) Yes, because it is a hunting weapon.
B) No, because it died from blunt force, which is not halal.
C) Yes, because the hunter intended to hunt.
D) No, because the hunter did not recite Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits eating meat from an animal killed by blunt force without cutting, even if the weapon is a permitted hunting tool.

Hunting with a Stone Pellet (Bunduqah): The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on prey killed by a stone pellet from a slingshot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating game killed by a stone pellet (bunduqah) and explain the legal analogy to mawqudhah.

Core Idea
A bunduqah kills by crushing, not cutting, so the game is mawqudhah and haram to eat.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on hunting with a stone pellet (bunduqah) fired from a slingshot. The central question is whether the meat of such game is halal. The Hanafi school holds that for meat to be halal, the animal must be killed by cutting or stabbing that draws blood; a crushing blow without bloodshed renders the meat unlawful. This ruling is derived from an athar of Ibn Umar and the Quranic verse on mawqudhah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is hunting with a bunduqah (stone pellet). The ruling: the meat is not halal if the animal dies from the strike.
The pellet is typically made of clay or stone and kills by crushing.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites the athar of Ibn Umar who classifies the kill as 'mawqudhah' (beaten to death). This is supported by Quran 5:3 which prohibits mawqudhah.
The dalil is a companion's statement, which is considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The bunduqah kill is analogous to mawqudhah because both involve death by blunt force without cutting. Since the Quran explicitly prohibits mawqudhah, this kill is also haram.
The 'illa (effective cause) is killing by crushing without bloodshed.
4
Note the difference from other weapons
This ruling applies specifically to bunduqah that does not cut. If the projectile is sharp and cuts the animal, the ruling may differ.
Some later Hanafis allowed it if the pellet causes injury, but the relied-upon position is prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴) ولايوكل ما اصابه البندقة اذا مات [۲۵۹۳] (۱۴) نہیں کھایا جائے گا جس کو غلیل کی گولی لگے اگر وہ اس سے مرجائے۔ پچھلے زمانے میں گول گول مٹی کی گولی بناتے تھے اور غلیل پر رکھ کر شکار کرتے تھے وہ چونکہ مٹی کا ہوتا تھا اور گول ہوتا تھا اس لئے وہ شکار کو زخمی نہیں کرتا تھا بلکہ اس کے لگنے سے موقوف کی شکل بنتی یعنی گوشت ہڈی چور کر دیتا اور شکار مر جاتا۔ چونکہ اس صورت میں ذبح اضطراری کی شکل نہیں بنی اس لئے شکار حلال نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے عن ابن عمر انه كان يقول في المقتولة بالبندقية تلك الموقوذة (بخاری شریف) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلیل کا مقتول چور کر کے مارا ہوا ہے۔
(14) And what the bunduqah (pellet) hits is not eaten when it dies. [2593] (14) That which is hit by a slingshot pellet will not be eaten if it dies from it. In earlier times, they made round clay pellets and used them for hunting with a slingshot. Since it was made of clay and round, it would not wound the animal but would crush the flesh and bones, causing death. In this case, since the form of emergency slaughter was not achieved, the game is not halal. There is an athar: Ibn Umar used to say about an animal killed by the bunduqah: 'That is al-mawqudhah.' This shows that the slingshot kill is crushed to death.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses hunting with a bunduqah, which is a clay or stone pellet shot from a slingshot. The ruling: if the pellet kills the game by crushing and not by cutting, it is not halal because it falls under al-mawqudhah (beaten to death). The Hanafi school considers that for the meat to be halal, the killing must be by a sharp instrument that causes bloodshed (as in emergency slaughter). The bunduqah does not cut; it crushes. This is similar to the earlier ruling on the mi'rad's broadside. The athar from Ibn Umar explicitly classifies such a kill as mawqudhah. Therefore, hunting with slingshots is generally not permissible according to the Hanafi school, unless the pellet is sharp enough to cut the animal's skin and draw blood.

Key Terms
البندقة (al-bunduqah): A pellet, typically made of clay, used in a slingshot for hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A boy kills a bird with a slingshot using a clay pellet. The bird dies without any cut. According to the Hanafi school, is it halal to eat?
A) Yes, because it was killed by a weapon.
B) No, because it is mawqudhah (beaten to death).
C) Yes, because the boy intended to eat it.
D) No, because the boy did not recite Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
Game killed by a stone pellet (bunduqah) is haram because it dies by crushing, analogous to mawqudhah, unless the pellet cuts and draws blood.

Hanafi Ruling on Hunting with Sling Shots and Modern Guns
Ruling with proof: prohibition of khadhf and condition for halal hunting with guns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting with sling shots, identify the condition for a projectile to be halal, and apply the distinction between mawqudha and dhabh idtirari.

Core Idea
Hunting is halal only if the projectile wounds; killing by blunt force makes the animal mawqudha and haram.

This passage addresses a common modern question: can you hunt with a sling shot or a gun? The Hanafi school rules based on a hadith prohibiting khadhf (sling shots) and the principle that an animal must be wounded to be properly slaughtered. We will examine the proof and derive conditions for halal hunting with modern firearms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is hunting (sayd) using a sling shot (khadhf) or gun. The ruling: haram if killed by blunt force, halal if the projectile wounds.
The hadith explicitly says 'no game is caught by it'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal in Sahih Bukhari: prohibition of khadhf because it cannot be used for hunting.
The hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا يصاد به صيد' shows that khadhf is ineffective for hunting, implying it is prohibited because it kills by blunt force (mawqudha).
Mawqudha is forbidden by Quran 5:3.
4
Apply the distinction to modern guns
The author extends the ruling: a gun bullet that wounds like an arrow is akin to dhabh idtirari and thus halal. If it crushes flesh without wounding, it remains haram.
The condition is that the tool must cut/wound, not just crush.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Hunting is halal only if the projectile wounds; otherwise it falls under mawqudha (haram). This applies to sling shots, stones, and modern bullets.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i who may permit killing by any means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصيد
منها ۲۵۹۴) (۱۵) واذا رمى صيدا فقطع عضوا منه أكل الصيد ولم يوكل العضو ۲۵۹۵] (۱۶) واذا قطعه اثلاثا والاكثر مما يلى العجز أكل الجميع وان كان الاكثر مما ا معراض ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۶ر سفن للبیہقی ، باب الصید بیرمی نجر او بند قیه ج تاسع ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۸۹۴۶ر مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۲۱ فی البندقية والحجر برمی به فیقتل ما قالوا فی ذلک ج رابع ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۱۹۷۲۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلیل کی گولی سے شکار شدہ موقوذہ ہے اس لئے حرام ہے۔ بخاری شریف میں اس کا ثبوت ہے اس لئے کہ وہاں خذف کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے جو غلیل کے معنی میں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن عبد الله بن مغفل انه رأى رجلا يخذف فقال له لا تخذف فان رسول الله الا الله [؟] نهى عن الخذف او كان يكره الخذف وقال انه لا يصاد به صيد ولا ينكاء به عدو ولكنها قد تكسر السن وتفقاء العين (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الخذف
والبند قیتی ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۹) اس حدیث کے اشارہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ گولی سے شکار نہیں کیا جا سکتا یعنی اس کا شکار حلال نہیں ہے۔ ون اگر آج کل کے زمانے میں بندوق کی گولی نوکدار ہو جس سے زخمی اور گھائل ہو جاتا ہو جس طرح تیر زخمی اور گھائل کرتا ہے تو اس سے شکار کرنے سے حلال ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ موقوفہ نہیں ہے ذبیح اضطراری کے درجے میں ہے۔ انمول ہر وہ گولی ، پتھر، لکڑی، لوہا جو دھاردار ہو اور زخمی اور گھائل کرتا ہو ان سے مار کر گھائل کر دیا تو حلال ہے اور زخمی اور گھائل نہ کرتا ہو بلکہ گوشت چور کرتا ہو تو حلال نہیں ہے۔
Book of Hunting. From them: 2594 (15): And if he shoots at game and cuts a limb from it, the game is eaten and the limb is not eaten. 2595 (16): And if he cuts it into three parts, and the majority is towards the rump, he eats all, and if the majority is towards the head, he eats the majority. (Reference to Bayhaqi and Ibn Abi Shayba) From this athar it is known that game killed by a sling shot is mawqudha (killed by a blow), therefore it is haram. The proof is in Sahih Bukhari because the word khadhf is used, which means sling shot. The hadith is: 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal saw a man throwing pebbles and said: Do not throw pebbles, for the Messenger of Allah (?) forbade or disliked throwing pebbles, and said: No game is caught by it, nor is an enemy wounded, but it may break a tooth or gouge an eye.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Khadhf). From the indication of this hadith, it is known that game cannot be caught with a bullet, i.e., its game is not halal. But if in modern times the gun bullet is pointed and wounds like an arrow, then hunting with it becomes halal, because it is not mawqudha but is in the category of dhabh idtirari (emergency slaughter). Any bullet, stone, wood, or iron that is sharp and wounds, if it wounds and kills, it is halal; if it does not wound but crushes flesh, it is not halal.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of hunting with sling shots (khadhf) and the condition for modern guns. The author first cites two rulings (15-16) from the matn, then provides a footnote discussing the hadith of khadhf. The key point: according to Hanafi fiqh, any projectile that kills by blunt force (mawqudha) is haram because it lacks the wounding action required for proper slaughter. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Mughaffal clearly prohibits throwing pebbles (khadhf) and states it cannot be used for hunting. Therefore, sling shots and similar non-wounding projectiles are prohibited. However, if a gun bullet is pointed and wounds like an arrow, creating a wound channel, it becomes analogous to dhabh idtirari (emergency slaughter) and the game is halal. The condition is that the projectile must be sharp and cut or wound, not merely crush by weight. This is a Hanafi position distinguishing between mawqudha (killed by blow) and mudhbah (slaughtered).

Key Terms
خذف (khadhf): Throwing pebbles or small stones with a sling shot or similar.
موقوذة (mawqudha): Animal killed by a blow without wounding, i.e., by blunt force.
ذبيح اضطراري (dhabh idtirari): Emergency slaughter where the animal is killed by a wound that is equivalent to throat-cutting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what makes a gun bullet halal for hunting?
A) The bullet must be made of iron.
B) The bullet must be pointed and wound like an arrow.
C) The bullet must be fired from a modern gun.
D) The bullet must kill by blunt force.

Key Takeaway
For hunting to be halal in Hanafi fiqh, the projectile must wound (cause a bleeding cut) like an arrow; killing by blunt force renders the animal mawqudha and haram.

Ruling on Eating Game Cut into Two Parts: Majority-Based Determination
Ruling with proof: determining halal status based on majority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on eating game cut into two parts by determining which part constitutes a majority and whether the head portion is included.

Core Idea
The head portion is always halal as slaughter; the rump portion's halal status depends on whether it is the majority.

When an arrow cuts a hunted animal into two parts, a key question arises: which part is permissible to eat? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer based on the principle of majority and the concept of slaughter (dhabh). This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri explains the ruling, supported by the athar of al-Thawri and the statement of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him). We will unpack the conditions and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognise that the game is cut into two parts by an arrow: one part contains the head and some body, the other contains the rump and some body. The ruling applies only when the animal is killed by the cut.
If the cut is not fatal, the ruling differs.
2
Determine the status of the head portion
The head portion is always halal because cutting the head constitutes slaughter (dhabh), regardless of the size of the attached body.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle.
3
Evaluate the rump portion based on majority
If the rump portion is more than half of the total animal, it is halal. If it is less than half, it is considered a limb cut from a living animal and is haram. If it is exactly half, both parts are halal.
The majority is determined by weight or volume.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
The athar from al-Thawri and 'Ali explicitly state the rule: if the thighs (rump) are less than half, do not eat them; if equal or more, eat them. This is the basis for the Hanafi position.
These athar are found in Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any limb cut from a living animal is carrion, so the rump portion is haram regardless of majority. The practical difference occurs when the rump is the majority: Hanafis permit it, Shafi'is do not.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different methodological approaches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اور سر کی طرف کا حلال ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شکار کا عضو اس طرح کٹ کر الگ ہوا کہ شکار زندہ تھا اور اس کا ہاتھ پاؤں یا سرین کٹ کر الگ ہو گیا تو اس کو اوپر کی حدیث کی بنا پر نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ he eats the majority next to the head. It is a part, meaning the game's limbs were not cut but the body was cut into two pieces. Here the principle is that the head is attached to the body, and cutting the head constitutes slaughter. If the head separates from the body, both the body and head are halal. Therefore, if two-thirds of the body is towards the rump and one-third towards the head, then both the rump portion and head portion are halal. Because the head was slaughtered, and along with the head some part of the body was cut, so both are halal. (2) There is an athar proving this: al-Thawri reported: If both thighs are cut off, then he does not eat the thighs but eats what contains the head. If with the thighs there is less than half of the wild animal, he does not eat it and eats what is next to the head. If the two halves are equal, he eats both, and whatever exceeds from the head side (he eats). This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. (Mussannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq). In this hadith the full detail: if the rump side is more, both rump and head are eaten. If the head side is more and the rump side is less, then the head part is halal and the rump part is not halal. (2) Another athar: from 'Ali: He said: Leave what is separated and eat what remains; if he cuts it into two equal halves, let him eat. (Mussannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Mussannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq). In this athar, 'jazlahu jazlan' means if the game is cut into two equal halves, both are halal. Therefore, if the rump side is more than half, that portion is eaten a fortiori, and the head portion is eaten because it is as slaughter. If the head side is more than half and the rump side is less than half, then it is considered that a limb was cut from a living animal, and according to the previous hadith, it is not halal. So the rump portion is not halal. In the previous athar, al-Thawri said: If with the thighs there is less than half of the wild animal, he does not eat it and eats what is next to the head. (Mussannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq). In this athar, if the rump side is less and the head side is more, then the rump side is not halal and the head side is halal. Imam al-Shafi'i says: If a limb of the game is cut off while the game is alive, like a hand, foot, or rump, then it is not eaten based on the previous hadith. But if the game falls dead as soon as the limb is cut, then the game is halal and the cut limb is also halal? Actually the text says: 'but if the hand or foot is cut and the game falls dead, then the game is halal and the cut hand or foot...' (cut off). Footnotes: (a) al-Thawri said: If both thighs are cut off and separated, the thighs are not eaten, and the part containing the head is eaten. If with the thighs there is less than half of the wild animal, he does not eat it and eats what is next to the head. If both halves are equal, he eats both, and if more is from the head side, he eats it. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. (b) From 'Ali: He said: Leave what is separated and eat what remains; if he cuts it into two equal halves, let him eat. (c) So if with the thighs there is less than half of the wild animal, do not eat it and eat what is next to the head.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a scenario where an arrow cuts the game into two parts, one larger and one smaller. The ruling distinguishes based on which part is larger. The principle: the head-related part is considered as if slaughtered (dhabh), so it is always halal. The rump-related part is considered a limb cut from a living animal if it is less than half; but if it is more than half, it is also considered halal because the majority indicates that the animal was killed by the cut. The Hanafi position, based on the athar from al-Thawri and the statement of 'Ali, is: if the rump part is more than half, both parts are halal. If the head part is more, only the head part is halal; the rump part is haram as a cut limb. If equal, both are halal. The text also records the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that any limb cut from a living animal is haram regardless of majority. The Hanafi response, implied by the athar, is that when the cut occurs as part of the fatal blow, the head part constitutes slaughter and the rest follows. The dispute (thamarah al-khilaf) is practical: Hanafis can eat both parts if rump is majority; Shafi'is would only eat the head part strictly.

Key Terms
اثلاث (athlāth): Cutting into three parts; but here used for two parts where one is a third and the other two-thirds.
جزلة جزلة (jazlahu jazlan): Cutting into two equal halves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if an arrow cuts a deer into two unequal parts where the rump part is one-third and the head part is two-thirds, what is the ruling?
A) Both parts are halal.
B) Only the head part is halal.
C) Only the rump part is halal.
D) Neither part is halal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on game cut into two parts determines halal status by majority: the head part is always halal, and the rump part is halal only if it constitutes more than half of the animal.

Two Hunters, One Game: Ownership and Halal Status
Ruling with proof on two scenarios of multiple hunters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario when two hunters shoot the same game and explain the legal basis for ownership and permissibility.

Core Idea
Ownership follows incapacitation, not final killing; halal requires proper slaughter.

This passage from the Book of Hunting presents two scenarios where two hunters shoot the same game. The key distinction is whether the first shot incapacitates the game or not. This determines both ownership and whether the game is halal to eat. The text also provides proofs from hadith and athar, illustrating how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from general principles and specific evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between (1) the first shot does not incapacitate the game (it remains able to flee), and (2) the first shot incapacitates the game (it cannot flee).
Incapacitation means the game cannot resist or flee; the first hunter could easily capture it.
2
Derive the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1: the game belongs to the second hunter and is halal. For scenario 2: the game belongs to the first hunter but is not halal.
Ownership vests with the one who incapacitates; halal requires slaughter if the animal is alive when obtained.
3
Locate the proofs
The hadith 'Whoever precedes to something that no Muslim has preceded to, it is his' (Abu Dawud) establishes ownership through prior possession. The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim (Muslim) commands slaughter if the game is found alive, and the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i prohibits eating if the animal dies with life remaining.
The hadith about land is used by qiyas to include any mubah thing like game.
4
Understand the underlying principles
Incapacitation = effective possession (milk). Killing a captured live animal without dhabh renders it haram, as the animal should have been slaughtered.
This shows that ownership and permissibility are separate legal categories.

پہلے کی مارسے شکار صحتمند شکار ہی رہا وہ پالتو کی طرح مجبور نہیں ہو گیا اس لئے وہ پہلے والے کا شکار نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شکار اس کی ملکیت ہے جس نے مار کر نڈھال کر دیا کہ اب آسانی سے اس کو پکڑ سکتا ہے۔ اور دوسرے آدمی نے گویا کہ صحتمند شکار کو تیر سے قتل کیا اس لئے یہ شکار دوسرے آدمی کا ہے۔ اور شکار کی حالت میں مرگیا اس لئے حلال ہے (۲) دوسرے آدمی کے شکار ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابيها اسمر ابن مضرس قال اتيت النبي الله الله فبايعته فقال من سبق الى ما لم يسبقه اليه مسلم فهو له (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اقطاع الارضین ص ۷۸ نمبر ۳۰۷) یہ حدیث اگر چہ مردہ اور بنجر زمین کے بارے میں ہے لیکن عام جملہ سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ عام مسلمانوں کے لئے مباح چیز جو لے لے اس کی ہوگی۔ اس لئے شکار کو جو مار کر نڈھال کرے گا اسی کا ہوگا۔ [۲۵۹۸)] (۱۹) اور اگر پہلے نے اس کو نڈھال کر دیا پھر دوسرے آدمی نے مارا اورقتل کر دیا تو شکر پہلے کا ہو گا لیکن کھایا نہیں جائے گا۔ پہلے آدمی نے شکار کو اتنا مارا کہ وہ نڈھال ہو گیا اور بھاگنے کے قابل نہیں رہا اس لئے یہ شکار حقیقت میں اسی کا ہو گیا۔ بعد میں دوسرے آدمی نے تیر مار کر ہلاک کیا تو اس کا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ پہلے نے نڈھال کیا ہے اور شکار اسی کا ہو گیا ہے۔
حدیث اوپر گزرگئی۔
اور کھایا اس لئے نہیں جائے گا کہ وہ زندہ ہاتھ آ گیا تھا اس لئے اس کو ذبح کر کے کھانا چاہئے تھا لیکن ذبح حقیقی کرنے کی بجائے تیر سے ہلاک کر دیا اس لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن عدی بن حاتم قال قال لي رسول الله الله اذا ارسلت کلبک فاذکر اسم الله فان امسک علیک فادر کته حیا فاذبحه (ب) (مسلم شریف ، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمۃ والرمی ص ۱۴۵نمبر ۴۹۸۱/۱۹۲۹)(۲) اور اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال اذا اخذت الصيد و به رمق فمات في يدك فلا تأكله ( ج ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۸ الرجل یا خذ الصيد و به رمق ج رابع ص ۲۴۳ نمبر ۱۹۲۲۵)
Book of Hunting: A game that was hit and not incapacitated and not taken out of the state of resistance, then another shot it and killed it: it belongs to the second and is eaten. [2598] (19) And if the first incapacitated it, then the second shot and killed it: it belongs to the first and is not eaten. [The game] was killed? then the game belongs to the second and will be eaten. A man shot an arrow at the game, it hit but still the game continued fleeing and was not incapacitated, just as a healthy game flees. Therefore it is like normal game and did not become the catch of the first. Now the second man shot and killed it, so the game belongs to the second. And since the second recited Bismillah and killed it, it will be eaten; it is halal. The game remained healthy from the first's shot, it did not become helpless like a domesticated animal, so it is not the first's catch. Because the game is the property of the one who kills and incapacitates it so that he can easily catch it. And the second man essentially killed a healthy game with an arrow, so this game belongs to the second man. And it died in the state of being game, so it is halal. (2) The proof that it belongs to the second is this hadith: From Abihayya al-Asmar ibn Mudarris: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and gave allegiance, and he said: Whoever precedes to something that no Muslim has preceded to, it is his. (a) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Land Grants, p. 78, no. 307). This hadith, although about dead and barren land, can be used by general inference: a permissible thing that a Muslim takes becomes his. Therefore, the one who kills and incapacitates the game becomes its owner. [2598)] (19) And if the first incapacitated it, then the second shot and killed it, the game belongs to the first but is not eaten. The first man hit the game so much that it became incapacitated and unable to flee, so in reality this game became his. Later, the second man killed it with an arrow, so it will not be his because the first incapacitated it and the game had become his. The hadith has already passed. And it will not be eaten because it came into hand alive, so it should have been slaughtered; but instead of proper slaughter, it was killed by an arrow, so it is not halal. The hadith has passed: From Adi ibn Hatim: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me: When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah; if it catches for you and you find it alive, then slaughter it. (b) (Muslim, Chapter on Hunting with Trained Dogs and Shooting, p. 145, no. 4981/1929) (2) And in the athar: From Ibrahim: When you catch a game that has some life remaining and it dies in your hand, do not eat it. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 8, hadith no. 19225).
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios in a hunting situation where two hunters shoot the same game. The first scenario: The first hunter's arrow hits the game but does not incapacitate it—the game remains capable of fleeing. Then the second hunter shoots and kills it. In this case, the game belongs to the second hunter and is halal to eat. The reasoning is that the game was not possessed by the first because it was not incapacitated; it remained in its original state of wildness. The second hunter effectively captured it by killing it with a proper hunting method (with tasmiyah). The proof cited is a hadith from Abu Dawud: 'Whoever precedes to something that no Muslim has preceded to, it is his.' Although the hadith is about land, the general principle applies to any mubah (permissible) thing, including game. The second scenario: The first hunter's arrow incapacitates the game—it is unable to flee. Then the second hunter's arrow kills it. In this case, the game belongs to the first hunter, but it is not halal to eat. The ownership is established because the first incapacitated it, making it as if it were in his possession. However, because the game was alive when it came into the first hunter's effective control, it must be properly slaughtered (dhabh) to be halal. Since the second hunter killed it with an arrow, it is considered as having died without proper slaughter, so it is not permissible to eat. The proof comes from a hadith in Muslim commanding slaughter when the animal is found alive, and from an athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stating that if a game with life remaining dies in your hand, do not eat it.

Key Terms
اثخنه (athkhanahu): Incapacitated the game by wounding it so that it cannot flee or resist.
رمق (ramq): The remaining life or vitality in an animal that has been injured but is still alive.
ذبح (dhabh): Islamic ritual slaughter by cutting the throat, the only method that renders a captured game halal if found alive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if the first hunter's arrow incapacitates the game so it cannot flee, then the second hunter's arrow kills it, what is the ruling?
A) The game belongs to the first hunter and is halal to eat.
B) The game belongs to the second hunter and is halal to eat.
C) The game belongs to the first hunter but is not halal to eat.
D) The game belongs to the second hunter but is not halal to eat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, ownership of hunted game is established by incapacitation, but permissibility to eat depends on the animal dying during the hunt or being properly slaughtered if found alive.

Permissibility of Hunting Both Edible and Non-Edible Animals
Ruling on permissibility of hunting both edible and non-edible animals with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting non-edible animals and cite the Quranic evidence and reasoning.

Core Idea
Hunting is permissible for all animals — the Quranic command is general, and non-edible animals may be hunted for skin, bones, or hair.

This passage addresses a common question: does Islamic law permit hunting only edible animals, or does it extend to non-edible ones? The Hanafi school, relying on the general command in Surah al-Ma'idah, allows hunting any animal for legitimate benefits beyond meat, such as skin, hair, or bones. The ruling is supported by the principle that the imperative in the verse indicates permissibility (ibahah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the legal classification (hukm) for hunting each category of animal: edible and non-edible. The passage states both are permissible.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) for both, regardless of edibility.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the exact verse cited: Surah al-Ma'idah 5:2, 'And when you become halal, then hunt.' Note that this verse was revealed after leaving ihram, but its application is general.
The verse is quoted as 'وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَاصْطَادُوا'.
3
Understand the dalala (indication)
Analyze how the imperative form 'اصطادوا' yields permissibility. In Hanafi usul, the bare imperative indicates ibahah (permissibility) unless there is a qarina (context) shifting it to obligation or prohibition.
The verse is general ('amm), including all animals.
4
Note the reasoning beyond meat
Recognize that the passage explicitly states hunting is not only for meat but also for skin, hair, and bones. This justifies including non-edible animals.
This reasoning is crucial for the inclusion of non-edible animals.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Acknowledge that some other schools may restrict hunting to edible animals only. The Hanafi school differs based on the general text and utilitarian benefits.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (scholarly difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز اصطياد ما يوكل لحمه من الحيوان وما لايوكل.
اور جائز ہے شکار کرنا گوشت کھائے جانے والے جانور کا اور جس کا گوشت نہ کھایا جاتا ہو۔ جن جانوروں کے گوشت کھائے جاتے ہیں ان کو بھی شکار کرسکتا ہے اور جن جانوروں کے گوشت نہیں کھائے جاتے ان کو بھی شکار کر سکتے ہیں۔ آیت میں ہے۔ واذا حللتم فالصطادوا (الف) ( آیت ۲ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں شکار کرنیکا حکم عام ہے چاہے وہ جانور ہو جس کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہے اور وہ جانور بھی شامل ہے جس کا گوشت نہیں کھایا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کا شکار حلال ہے (۲) صرف گوشت کھانے کے لئے ہی شکار نہیں کرتے بلکہ کھال ، بال اور ہڈی کے لئے بھی شکار کرتے ہیں اس لئے غیر ماکول اللھم کا شکار بھی حلال ہے کوئی ممانعت نہیں۔
اصطاد : صید سے مشتق ہے یہاں افتعال سے آیا ہے شکار کرنا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) جب تم حلال ہو جاؤ تو تم شکار کر سکتے ہو۔
And it is permissible to hunt animals whose meat is eaten and those whose meat is not eaten. And it is permissible to hunt animals whose meat is eaten and those whose meat is not eaten. The verse says: 'And when you become halal, then hunt' (a) (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:2). In this verse, the command to hunt is general, whether it is an animal whose meat is eaten or an animal whose meat is not eaten. Therefore, hunting both is halal. (2) People do not hunt only for eating meat but also for skin, hair, and bones, so hunting non-edible animals is also halal; there is no prohibition. 'Istitad' is derived from 'sayd'; here it comes from the form 'ifti'al', meaning to hunt. Footnote: (a) 'When you become halal, you may hunt.'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage rules on the permissibility of hunting animals, extending beyond those whose meat is consumed. The author states that it is permissible to hunt both edible and non-edible animals. The proof is from the Quranic verse in Surah al-Ma'idah: 'And when you become halal, then hunt.' The word 'hunt' (istiyad) is general in Arabic, covering all animals. The verse was revealed in the context of leaving the state of ihram, but its application is general. Additionally, the passage notes that hunting is not solely for meat; there are other benefits such as skin, hair, and bones. Therefore, hunting non-edible animals (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm) is also permissible. The linguistic note explains that 'istitad' is derived from 'sayd' (game) and is in the ifti'al form meaning to hunt.

Key Terms
اصطاد (istada): To hunt; derived from sayd (game), in the ifti'al form meaning to engage in hunting.
ما يؤكل لحمه / ما لا يؤكل (ma yu'kalu lahmuhu / ma la yu'kalu): Animals whose meat is eaten (halal) and animals whose meat is not eaten (non-edible).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hunting is permissible for all animals in the Hanafi school because the Quranic command is general and animals provide multiple benefits beyond meat.

Ruling on Slaughter by Muslims and People of the Book
States the ruling with Quranic and Companion proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of slaughter by Ahl al-Kitab and identify the conditions required for it to be halal.

Core Idea
Slaughter by a Muslim or true Person of the Book is halal only if they say Bismillah.

In this passage, the author establishes the foundational Hanafi ruling on the slaughtered meat (dhabihah) of Muslims and People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab). Using the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah and statements from the Companions, he clarifies that permissibility is contingent upon saying Bismillah during slaughter. The passage also addresses modern concerns about European Christians who do not meet this condition.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its conditions
The ruling: slaughter by a Muslim or Ahl al-Kitab (Jew or Christian) is halal provided they say Bismillah during slaughter. Identify this condition as central.
The condition of saying Bismillah is emphasized through later proofs.
2
Locate the primary dalil (Quran)
The author cites Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5, which declares the food of Ahl al-Kitab lawful for Muslims. Recognize this as the primary textual evidence.
The verse uses the word 'طعام' (food), which requires interpretation.
3
Interpret the key term 'طعام' (food)
Ibn Abbas explains that 'food' here means slaughtered meat. This connects the verse directly to the issue of dhabihah.
This interpretation is from a Companion, giving it strong authority.
4
Examine the condition of saying Bismillah
The athar of al-Zuhri states that if the slaughterer invokes other than Allah, do not eat. This implies that if Bismillah is not said (or a false name is invoked), the meat is not halal. The author applies this to European Christians who do not say Bismillah.
The condition applies to both Muslims and Ahl al-Kitab equally.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the slaughter of Ahl al-Kitab unconditionally halal, without requiring Bismillah. The Hanafi position is based on the need for the slaughterer to be a believer in Allah, evidenced by the condition.
This ikhtilaf affects fatwa in multicultural contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۰۱] (۲۲) مسلمان اور کتابی کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے۔
ہے۔
مسلمان بسم اللہ پڑھ کر ذبح کرے تو جانور حلال ہے اسی طرح اہل کتاب یعنی یہودی اور نصرانی بسم اللہ پڑھ کر ذبح کرے تو ذبیحہ حلال
آیت میں ہے۔ الیوم احل لكم الطيبات وطعام الذين اوتو الكتاب حل لكم وطعامكم حل لهم (الف)( آیت۵ سورۃ المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جن لوگوں کو کتاب دی گئی یعنی یہود اور نصاری ان کا کھانا جس سے مراد ذبیحہ ہے تمہارے لئے حلال ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال طعامهم ذبائحهم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ذبائح اہل الکتاب و محو مها من اهل العرب و غیر هم ص ۸۲۸ نمبر ۵۵۰۸ سفن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء فی طعام اہل الکتاب ج تاسع ص ۴۷۴ نمبر ۱۹۱۵۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آیت میں اہل کتاب کے طعام سے مرادان کا ذبیحہ ہے۔
یورپ کے عیسائی عموما ہر یے ہوتے ہیں وہ نام کے عیسائی ہوتے ہیں اور بسم اللہ پڑھ کر بھی ذبیح نہیں کرتے جومسلمان کے لئے بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے ان کے ذبیحے سے احتیاط ضروری ہے۔
اثر میں ہے۔ وقال الزهرى لا بأس بذبيحة نصارى العرب وان سمعته يسمى لغير الله فلا تأكل (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب ذبائح اہل الكتاب وشحومها من اهل الحرب وغيرهم ص ۸۲۸ نمبر ۵۵۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اللہ کے علاوہ کا نام لے تو نہ کھائے اور اسی سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ نہ پڑھے تو حلال نہیں ہے، اور یورپ کے عیسائی بسم اللہ پڑھتے ہی نہیں ہیں اس لئے ان کا ذبیحہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب قال ما نصارى العرب باهل الكتاب وما تحل لنا ذبائحهم وما انا بتاركهم حتى يسلموا او اضرب اعناقهم (و) (سن للبیہقی ، باب ذبائح نصاری العرب ج تاسع ص ۴۷۸ نمبر ۹ ۱۹۱۶) جب عرب کے نصاری صحابہ کے زمانہ میں اہل کتاب نہیں تھے تو اس زمانے میں یورپ کے عیسائی کیسے مسلمان ہو گئے۔
[2601] (22) The slaughter of a Muslim and a Person of the Book is halal. If a Muslim says Bismillah and slaughters, the animal is halal. Similarly, if a Person of the Book, i.e., a Jew or Christian, says Bismillah and slaughters, the slaughtered animal is halal. The verse says: 'This day [all] good foods have been made lawful, and the food of those who were given the Scripture is lawful for you and your food is lawful for them' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5). In this verse, the food of those given the Scripture, i.e., Jews and Christians, meaning their slaughtered meat, is halal for you. (2) Ibn Abbas said: 'Their food means their slaughtered meat' (Bukhari, Book of Slaughter of Ahl al-Kitab...; Bayhaqi). From this athar, it is understood that what is meant by 'food of Ahl al-Kitab' in the verse is their slaughtered meat. European Christians are generally heretics; they are Christians in name only and do not say Bismillah when slaughtering, which is also necessary for Muslims. Therefore, caution regarding their slaughter is necessary. An athar: Al-Zuhri said: 'There is no harm in the slaughter of Arab Christians, but if you hear him invoking the name of other than Allah, do not eat' (Bukhari). From this athar, it is understood that if he invokes the name of other than Allah, do not eat, and similarly, if he does not say Bismillah, it is not halal. And European Christians do not say Bismillah at all, so their slaughtered meat is also not halal. (3) An athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'The Arab Christians are not People of the Book, and their slaughtered meat is not halal for us, and I will not leave them until they accept Islam or I strike their necks' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). When the Arab Christians at the time of the Companions were not People of the Book, how then could European Christians be considered Muslims?
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that the slaughtered animal of a Muslim and a Person of the Book (Jew or Christian) is halal, provided they say Bismillah during slaughter. The author first presents the ruling, then provides Quranic evidence from Surah al-Ma'idah verse 5, which explicitly declares the food of Ahl al-Kitab (interpreted as their slaughtered meat) lawful for Muslims. This interpretation is supported by a narration from Ibn Abbas. The author then adds a practical note about European Christians today, who do not say Bismillah and are not considered true Christians; therefore, their slaughter is not halal. He further supports this with the statement of Al-Zuhri that if the slaughterer invokes other than Allah, the meat is not to be eaten. Finally, he cites Umar ibn al-Khattab's declaration that Arab Christians were not considered People of the Book in his time, implying a stricter criterion for who qualifies as Ahl al-Kitab. The overall ruling is that the slaughter of a Muslim or a true Person of the Book who says Bismillah is halal.

Key Terms
ذبيحة (dhabihah): An animal slaughtered according to Islamic law.
أهل الكتاب (ahl al-kitab): Jews and Christians, the people who received revealed scriptures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required from a Person of the Book for their slaughtered animal to be halal according to this passage?
A) They must be a true Christian or Jew.
B) They must say 'Bismillah' during slaughter.
C) They must be from the Arab Christians.
D) Their slaughter is always haram.

Key Takeaway
The halal status of meat from Ahl al-Kitab depends on them saying Bismillah during slaughter; without it, the meat is not halal in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Slaughter by Apostate, Magian, Idolater, and Muhrim
States rulings and proofs for four prohibited slaughters, with a dispute on the muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the slaughter of an apostate, Magian, idolater, and muhrim, identify the proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i disagreement regarding the muhrim.

Core Idea
Slaughter by non-Muslims (except Ahl al-Kitab) and by a muhrim's game is haram — even for others.

The permissibility of eating meat from slaughtered animals depends on who performs the slaughter. In this passage, we examine four categories whose slaughter is not acceptable: an apostate (murtadd), a Magian (majusi), an idolater (wathani), and a person in the state of ihram (muhrim). The author presents textual evidence and also engages with the Shafi'i school's differing view concerning the muhrim. By the end, you will understand the reasoning behind each ruling and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited categories
Explicitly name each type: apostate, Magian, idolater, and muhrim. Understand why each is problematic — the first three are not Muslim nor Ahl al-Kitab; the muhrim is forbidden to hunt.
The ruling on the apostate and idolater is derived by analogy (qiyas) from the Magian.
2
Locate the primary proof for each
For the Magian: the mursal hadith from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad. For the muhrim: Quranic verses (5:95-96), the hadith of Abu Qatadah, and the athar from al-Thawri and 'Ata.
The athar from al-Thawri and 'Ata is the key direct evidence for the muhrim's game being impermissible for all.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas) for apostate and idolater
Since the hadith explicitly forbids the Magian's slaughter, and the apostate and idolater share the same underlying cause (they are not Muslim or Ahl al-Kitab and do not properly invoke Allah), the same ruling applies by qiyas.
This is an example of qiyas jali (clear analogy) based on the effective cause (illah) of disbelief and lack of proper tasmiyah.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counterargument on the muhrim
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the muhrim's slaughter is valid because he is a Muslim, citing an athar from al-Hakam ibn 'Utaybah. Compare this with the Hanafi evidence.
The Hanafi school prefers the athar of al-Thawri and 'Ata over al-Hakam's, as it directly addresses the question of permissibility for others.
5
Determine the practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis do not eat game slaughtered by a muhrim; Shafi'is consider it permissible for non-muhrims. This difference matters for travelers or guests in mixed-madhhab settings.
The dispute is legitimate; both schools rely on transmitted reports. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi madhhab.

[2602] (23) The slaughtered animal of an apostate, Magian, idolater, and muhrim will not be eaten. These people are neither Muslims nor People of the Book; they are disbelievers, so their slaughtered animal is not halal. They do not rely on saying Bismillah, nor is their Bismillah considered valid, and saying Bismillah is necessary, so it will not be halal. (2) Hadith: Footnote: (a) 'This day good foods have been made lawful for you, and the food of the People of the Book is lawful for you, and your food is lawful for them.' (b) Ibn Abbas said: 'Their food means their slaughtered meat.' (c) Al-Zuhri said: 'There is no harm in the slaughter of Arab Christians, but if you hear him invoking other than Allah, do not eat.' (d) Umar said: 'The Arab Christians are not People of the Book, and their slaughtered meat is not halal for us, and I will not leave them until they accept Islam or I strike their necks.'

[PAGE_026]
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4
'...and the Magian, the idolater, and the muhrim.'
19
Kitab al-Sayd
Al-Bayhaqi, Chapter
There is a mursal hadith: From al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: 'The Messenger of Allah wrote to the Magians of Hajar inviting them to Islam. Whoever accepted was accepted, and whoever refused was to be imposed the jizyah on condition that their slaughtered animal would not be eaten and their women would not be married.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Dar Qutni) From this athar, it is understood that the slaughtered animal of a Magian is not permissible, and by analogy, the slaughtered animal of an apostate and idolater is also not halal.
And for a muhrim, it is not permissible to catch game, therefore slaughtering it is also not permissible. The verse says: 'The game of the land is forbidden to you as long as you are in ihram' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96). And another verse: 'O you who have believed, do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95). These two verses indicate that a muhrim should not hunt, because hunting is forbidden for him. And he should not help the hunters. The long hadith of Abu Qatadah has passed that the muhrims did not help him. A part of the hadith: 'From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah: I sought their help, but they refused to help me' (Bukhari). This hadith shows that a muhrim should not even help a hunter. The game of a muhrim is not halal; the proof is this athar: 'I asked al-Thawri about a muhrim who slaughters game: is its eating permissible for others? He said: Layth informed me from 'Ata that he said: It is not permissible for anyone to eat it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that the game slaughtered by a muhrim is not halal for anyone.
Imam al-Shafi'i says: For a muhrim, hunting although not permissible, but if he slaughters the game, it is halal for others; they can eat it. The muhrim is a Muslim, so his slaughter is valid. (2) An athar: 'Ash'ath informed me from al-Hakam ibn 'Utaybah that he said: There is no harm in eating it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar indicates that one can eat the slaughtered animal of a muhrim.
Footnotes: (a) The Prophet wrote concerning the Magians of Hajar: 'They will be invited to Islam. Whoever accepts is accepted, and whoever refuses will be imposed the jizyah on condition that their slaughtered animal will not be eaten and their women will not be married.' (b) 'The game of the land is forbidden to you as long as you are in ihram.' Another verse: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in ihram.' (c) Abu Qatadah said: 'I sought help from the Companions for hunting, but they refused to help me.' (d) He asked al-Thawri about a muhrim slaughtering game: 'Can he slaughter and is it halal for others?' He said: 'Layth informed me from 'Ata that its eating is not halal for anyone.' (e) Al-Hakam ibn 'Utaybah said: 'If a muhrim slaughters game, there is no harm for others in eating it.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage presents rulings and proofs regarding the slaughter of apostates, Magians, idolaters, and those in ihram (muhrim). It begins with the ruling that the slaughtered animal of these individuals is not to be eaten. The reason given is that they are not Muslims nor Ahl al-Kitab; they are disbelievers and do not properly say Bismillah. The author then provides a mursal hadith about the Magians of Hajar, which establishes that their slaughter is not permissible and that by analogy (qiyas), the same applies to apostates and idolaters. Regarding the muhrim, the author cites Quranic verses (5:95-96) that forbid hunting while in ihram, and a hadith where the Companions refused to help a non-muhrim hunter. The key evidence for the Hanafi position is a narration from al-Thawri and 'Ata stating that the game slaughtered by a muhrim is not halal for anyone. Then the author presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that since the muhrim is a Muslim, his slaughter is valid and the meat is halal for others. Al-Shafi'i cites an athar from al-Hakam ibn 'Utaybah. The author does not explicitly prefer one view over the other, but by presenting the Hanafi evidence first and the Shafi'i evidence as a counter, the context suggests the Hanafi position is the operative ruling.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate, a Muslim who has left Islam.
مجوسي (majusi): A Magian, follower of Zoroastrianism.
محرِم (muhrim): A person in a state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, for whom hunting is forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is only halal for the muhrim himself.
D) It is halal if the muhrim says Bismillah.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter by an apostate, Magian, idolater, or muhrim (for game) is haram to consume; the Hanafi school relies on specific traditions that override general principles.

The Valid Location for Dhabh Slaughter
Defines the specific location for valid dhabh slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for the location of dhabh (slaughter) and identify the proof from the Companion Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Slaughter must be between the throat and the upper chest – this is a defined legal location, not arbitrary.

This passage defines the precise anatomical location for valid Islamic slaughter according to the Hanafi school. It is not enough to simply cut the neck; the cut must occur in a specific zone between the throat (halq) and the upper chest (labbah). The author supports this ruling with an athar (narration) from Ibn Abbas, a Companion known for his expertise in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is dhabh (ritual slaughter). The ruling specifies a required location: between the throat and the upper chest.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar (narration) from Ibn Abbas in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
The athar is: 'Al-dhakaat fi al-halq wa al-labbah' (Slaughter is in the throat and upper chest).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of 'halq wa al-labbah' specifies the location as a requirement. The Hanafi school takes this as binding because it is a direct statement from a Companion.
The dalal is qati' (clear) even though thubut is zanni (through a companion narration).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Maliki) may allow a cut anywhere on the neck as long as the main veins are severed. The Hanafi school differs by requiring this specific zone.
This difference has practical implications for halal meat certification.
5
Evaluate the practical effect
The requirement ensures proper cutting of the windpipe, esophagus, and two jugular veins in the correct area, leading to effective blood drainage and a valid slaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذبح بين الحلق واللبة (٢٥) ذبح کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ حلق اور سینہ کی ہڈی جو ہوتی ہے اس کے درمیان میں چھری سے ذبح کرتے ہیں۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال الذكاة في الحلق واللبة (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب ما يقطع من الذبيحة ج رابع ص ٤٩٥ نمبر ٨٦١٥ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ٣٢ من قال اذا انهر الدم فکل ماسنا او عظماج رابع ص ٢٦٠ نمبر ١٩٨٢٢) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حلق اور لیہ کے درمیان ذبح کرے۔ لافتا البتہ : سینہ کے اوپر کی ہڈی۔
And the slaughter is between the throat and the upper chest (labbah). (25) The method of slaughter is that one slaughters with a knife between the throat and the bone of the chest that is there. There is an athar: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The slaughter is in the throat and the upper chest.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on what is cut from the slaughtered animal, vol. 4, p. 495, no. 8615; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 32: from those who said: if it causes blood to flow, then eat, except a tooth or bone, vol. 4, p. 260, no. 19822) From this athar it is understood that one should slaughter between the throat and the labbah. Note: labbah is the bone above the chest.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, establishing the correct location for dhabh (Islamic slaughter). It begins by defining the place: between the halq (throat) and the labbah (the depression at the base of the neck, above the chest). The author then explains the method: using a knife to cut in that area. The proof is an athar (narration) from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that slaughter is to be performed in the throat and labbah. The Hanafi school relies on this to specify that the cut must be made in the lower neck area, not higher or lower. The Arabic term 'labbah' is clarified as the bone above the chest (the upper sternum). This ruling ensures proper blood drainage and humane slaughter.

Key Terms
الذبح (al-dhabh): The ritual slaughter of an animal by cutting the throat, specific to the method prescribed in Islamic law.
الحلق (al-halq): The throat; the front part of the neck where the windpipe and esophagus are located.
اللبة (al-labbah): The depression at the base of the neck above the chest; the upper sternum area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the slaughter of an animal be performed?
A) At the very top of the neck, below the head
B) Between the throat (halq) and the upper chest (labbah)
C) At the base of the neck near the shoulders
D) Anywhere on the neck as long as blood flows

Key Takeaway
The valid location for dhabh in the Hanafi school is exclusively between the throat (halq) and the upper chest (labbah), as established by the Companion Ibn Abbas.

Four Veins in Slaughter: The Ruling and Its Proof
Lists the four essential veins and ruling if all are cut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four veins that must be cut in Hanafi slaughter and explain why each is required based on the Prophetic hadith and scholarly athar.

Core Idea
Four veins must be cut; cutting all ensures complete blood drainage required for halal meat.

Islamic slaughter (dhabh) has specific requirements to ensure the meat is halal. The Hanafi school details four veins that must be severed. Understanding these veins and their proof from the Sunnah is essential for anyone performing slaughter or issuing fatwas on meat consumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the slaughter of an animal. The ruling is that cutting the four specified veins makes the meat halal (permissible to eat).
2
List the four veins
Memorize the four veins: al-ḥalqūm (trachea), al-marī' (esophagus), and the two wadajān (jugular veins).
The two jugulars are considered as one unit but are distinct veins.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that all blood must flow out of the animal's body for the meat to be halal. These four veins are the channels through which blood drains.
Complete blood removal prevents the accumulation of stagnant blood, which is prohibited.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Eat what makes the blood flow, except tooth and nail.' This indicates any method that causes blood to flow is acceptable. Cutting these veins is the established method to achieve that flow.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud, reported by Rafi' ibn Khadij.
5
Note the athar evidence
Ibn Jurayj from 'Ata reported: 'Slaughter is the cutting of the jugulars.' And Ibn Abbas said: 'The slaughter is in the throat and the upper chest.' These narrations specify the location and confirm that cutting the jugulars and trachea is required.
The 'throat' (ḥalq) implies the trachea and esophagus area.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعروق التي تقطع في الذكاة اربعة الحلقوم والمرئ والودجان فان قطعها حل الاكل (٢٦) اصل تو یہ ہے کہ جسم سے پورا خون نکل جائے۔ اور پورا خون ان رگوں کے کاٹنے سے نکلتا ہے۔ اس لئے حلقوم ، مری اور دو شہ رگیں کاٹنے سے ذبح ہوگا وجہ پورا خون نکلنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن رافع بن خدیج قال قال النبي الله كل يعنى ما انهر الدم الا السن والظفر (بخاری شریف، باب لایذ کی بانسن و العظم و الظفر ص ٨٢٧ نمبر ٥٥٠٦ ابوداؤد شریف، باب الذبيحه بالمروة ص ٣٣ نمبر (٢٨٢) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر وہ طریقہ جس سے خون خوب نکل جائے اس سے ذبیحہ حلال ہوتا ہے۔ رگیں کٹنے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال ابن جريج عن عطاء ... والذبح قطع الاوداج اور دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس الذكاة في الحلق واللبة (بخاری شریف، باب النحر والذبح ص ٢٢٨ نمبر ٥٥١٠ سفن للبیهقی ، باب الذكاة بما انصر الدم وفری الا وداج، ج تاسع ، ص ٢٧٣ نمبر (١٩١٥) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذبح کرنے کے لئے اور اج کالے اور حلق پر چھری چلائے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حلقوم کاٹے اور جب حلقوم کاٹے گا تو مری بھی کٹے گا تب حلال ہوگا۔ حلقوم : کھانے کی نالی۔ المری : سانس کی نالی۔ ودجان : شہ رگ ، جس سے دل کا خون دماغ تک جاتا ہے اس کو کاٹنے سے پورا خون نکلتا ہے۔
And the veins that are cut in slaughter are four: the trachea (halqum), the esophagus (mari'), and the two jugulars (wadajan). If he cuts them, eating becomes permissible. (26) The principle is that all the blood should flow out of the body, and all the blood flows out by cutting these veins. Therefore, cutting the trachea, esophagus, and two jugulars constitutes slaughter. The proof that all blood flows out is this hadith: from Rafi' ibn Khadij, he said: the Prophet said: 'Eat what makes the blood flow, except the tooth and the nail.' (Bukhari, chapter: do not slaughter with the tooth, bone, and nail, p. 827, no. 5506; Abu Dawud, chapter: slaughter with a stone, p. 33, no. 282) From this hadith it is understood that every method from which blood flows well makes the slaughtered animal halal. The proof for cutting the veins is this athar: Ibn Jurayj from 'Ata said: '...And slaughter is the cutting of the jugulars.' And in another narration: from Ibn Abbas: 'The slaughter is in the throat and the upper chest.' (Bukhari, chapter: nahr and dhabh, p. 228, no. 5510; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: slaughter with what makes blood flow and cutting the jugulars, vol. 9, p. 273, no. 1915) From this athar it is understood that for slaughter, one should run the knife over the jugulars and the throat. And from this it is understood that he cuts the trachea, and when he cuts the trachea, the esophagus is also cut, then it becomes halal. Halqum: the food pipe. Mari': the air pipe. Wadajan: the jugular vein, through which blood from the heart goes to the brain; cutting it causes all blood to flow out.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the four specific veins that must be severed in valid Islamic slaughter. The author lists them: al-halqum (trachea), al-mari' (esophagus), and the two wadajan (jugular veins). Cutting all four makes the meat halal. The underlying principle (asl) is that complete blood drainage is required, and these veins are the channels for blood flow. The proof is a hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that anything that causes blood to flow is acceptable except teeth and nails. This indicates that the primary objective is thorough blood drainage. Additionally, an athar from 'Ata explains that slaughter is specifically the cutting of the jugulars (awdaj), and Ibn Abbas's narration links the location (halq and labbah) with cutting these veins. The commentary clarifies the anatomical terms: halqum is the esophagus (food pipe), mari' is the trachea (windpipe), and wadaj is the jugular vein carrying blood from heart to brain. Cutting all four ensures maximum blood flow.

Key Terms
الحلقوم (al-ḥalqūm): The trachea or windpipe; the air passage from the throat to the lungs.
المرئ (al-marī'): The esophagus; the food pipe leading from the mouth to the stomach.
الودجان (al-wadajān): The two jugular veins; the major veins carrying blood from the head back to the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is essential for valid slaughter?
A) Cutting the trachea only
B) Cutting the trachea and esophagus
C) Cutting the trachea, esophagus, and both jugulars
D) Cutting all major blood vessels

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires cutting four specific veins (trachea, esophagus, both jugulars) in slaughter to ensure complete blood drainage, based on the hadith 'Eat what makes the blood flow' and athar specifying jugulars.
