Cutting Most Veins: The Hanafi Dispute on Sufficiency
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficiency of cutting most veins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the sufficiency of cutting most veins in slaughter, and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A dispute on whether cutting most veins suffices for slaughter, or specific veins are required.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum number of veins that must be cut for a valid slaughter. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that cutting three out of the four main veins suffices, while the Sahibayn insist on cutting the trachea (halqum), esophagus (mari'), and at least one jugular (wadaj). Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for butchers and those issuing fatwas on halal slaughter, as it directly impacts the validity of the meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the specific point of disagreement: whether cutting 'most' (akthar) of the four veins is sufficient, or whether three specific veins must be cut.
The four veins are: trachea, esophagus, and two jugulars.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that cutting any three veins suffices. His proof includes the principle 'al-akthar ka al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) and the hadith emphasizing blood flow.
He argues that as long as blood flows, the animal is slaughtered.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn require the trachea, esophagus, and one jugular to be cut. Their proof is the hadith 'kull ma afra al-awdaj' (eat what cuts the jugulars), which they interpret as requiring a jugular to be cut specifically.
They also cite that cutting these three ensures complete blood drainage.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Consider a scenario where three veins are cut but none is a jugular. According to Abu Hanifa, it is valid; according to the Sahibayn, it is invalid. This affects the halal status of the meat.
Also, if the three cut include the trachea, esophagus, and one jugular, both agree it is valid.
5
Determine the resolution in later Hanafi practice
Though the text does not give a final tarjih, later Hanafi authorities often follow Abu Hanifa for ease, but many recommend caution by adopting the Sahibayn's stricter view.
The dispute remains within the school, and both views are transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قطع اکثرها فکذلک عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا بد من قطع الحلقوم والمرئ واحد الودجين (٢٧) اور اگر اکثر کاٹ دیا تو ایسے ہی جائز ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ضروری ہے حلقوم، مری اور شہ رگ میں سے ایک کو کاٹنا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ چار میں اکثر یعنی کوئی تین رگیں کاٹ دے تو ذبیحہ حلال ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس سے منقول ہے کہ ذبح حلق اور لبہ کے درمیان ہوتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جو چیز خون بہادے اس سے ذبح کیا ہوا کھاؤ سوائے دانت اور ناخن کے اس سے ذبح کیا ہو امت کھاؤ (ج) حضرت عطا سے منقول ہے .. ذبیح اوراج رگوں کو کاٹنا ہے۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے ذبح حلق اور لیہ کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔  اکثرها فكذلك عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا بد من قطع الحلقوم والمرئ واحد الودجين (٢٨) ويجوز الذبح بالليطة والمروة وبكل شيء انهر الدم الا السن اکثر کل کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے تین چار میں سے اکثر ہے اس لئے اتنا کافی ہے۔ فائده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حلقوم بھی کاٹنا ہو گا اور مری بھی اور دوشہ رگوں میں سے ایک کو کاٹنا ہوگا تا کہ شہ رگ سے پورا خون نکل جائے۔ اور ہر ایک رگ کا ایک ایک ضرور ہو جائے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ ور جان کالے اس لئے ور جان یعنی شہ رگ میں سے ایک کا نا ضروری ہے۔ عن رافع بن خديج قال سالت رسول الله الله عن الذبيحة بالليط فقال كل ما افرى الاوداج الا سن او ظفر (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ٣٢ من قال اذا انصر الدم فكل ما خلا سنا او عظماج رابع ص ٢٥٩ نمبر ١٩٨٠٣) حضرت ابن عمر کا قول ہے۔ ان ابن عمر نهى عن النخع يقول يقطع مادون العظم ثم يدع حتى يموت (بخاری شریف، باب الخمر والذبح ص ٨٢٨ نمبر ٥٥١٠) اس حدیث واثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہڈی تک کاٹ دے اور چھوڑ دے۔ اور ہڈی تک کاٹے گا تو مری ، حلقوم اور شہ رگ کٹ جائیں گے۔ اور اوراج کا کاٹنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ حدیث میں اور اج کاٹنے کی تاکید ہر موقع پر ہے۔
And if he cuts most of them, it is likewise (permissible) according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: 'It is necessary to cut the trachea, esophagus, and one of the two jugulars.' (27) If he cuts most of them, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the Sahibayn said it is necessary to cut the trachea, esophagus, and one of the jugulars. Imam Abu Hanifa says: most of the four, i.e., any three veins, if he cuts them, the slaughtered animal is halal. Footnote: (a) It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that slaughter is between the throat and labbah. (b) He said: eat what makes blood flow from it as slaughtered, except a tooth and a nail; do not eat from it. (c) It is narrated from 'Ata that slaughter is cutting the jugulars. [Page 29] Most of them is likewise according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: it is necessary to cut the trachea, esophagus, and one of the two jugulars. (28) And it is permissible to slaughter with a reed (laytah) and a sharp stone (marwah) and everything that makes blood flow, except the tooth. Because most of the four is considered most, so this is sufficient. Benefit: The Sahibayn say: the trachea must be cut, and the esophagus, and one of the two jugulars so that all blood flows out from the jugular. And each vein is necessary individually. In the hadith it is mentioned: 'cut the jugulars', so one of the jugulars is necessary. From Rafi' ibn Khadij: I asked the Messenger of Allah about slaughtering with a reed, and he said: 'Eat what cuts the jugulars, except a tooth or a nail.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 32, no. 19803) And Ibn Umar's statement: He forbade nakh' (severing the spinal cord before death), saying: 'He cuts what is below the bone then leaves it until it dies.' (Bukhari, chapter: wine and slaughter, p. 828, no. 5510) From this hadith and athar it is understood that he cuts to the bone and then leaves. And when he cuts to the bone, the esophagus, trachea, and jugulars will be cut. And cutting the jugulars is necessary because the hadith emphasizes cutting the jugulars on every occasion.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the number of veins that must be cut for valid slaughter. The issue arises when the slaughterer cuts 'most' of the four veins (three out of four). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that cutting three is sufficient because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, analogizing to other legal principles (e.g., most of a quantity suffices). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require that at least the trachea (halqum), esophagus (mari'), and one jugular (wadaj) be cut explicitly. Their reasoning is based on the hadith 'kull ma afra al-awdaj' (eat what cuts the jugulars), which mentions the plural 'awdaj' (jugulars) but also indicates that cutting at least one jugular along with the other two is necessary. The footnote includes additional narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar about the location and method, emphasizing cutting to the bone and leaving the animal to die naturally, without severing the spinal cord (nakh'). The author seems to support Abu Hanifa's view by stating 'most of what is in the ruling, so three out of four is most, so it is sufficient,' but the dispute is clearly laid out. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for fatwa today is often the view of Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn's view is also strong and sometimes preferred for caution.

Key Terms
اکثر (akthar): Majority; in this context, cutting three out of the four specified veins.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): Refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two primary disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding slaughter?
A) Whether slaughter is valid if only the trachea is cut
B) Whether cutting three out of four veins is sufficient (Abu Hanifa) or three specific ones are required (Sahibayn)
C) Whether a sharp stone can be used for slaughter
D) Whether the animal's head must be facing the Qibla

Key Takeaway
In slaughter, the Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that cutting three out of four veins suffices, while the Sahibayn require the trachea, esophagus, and at least one jugular.

Permissible Tools for Slaughter: The Shar'i Principle of 'Whatever Makes Blood Flow'
States the ruling and exception, cites hadith proof, and explains the reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible slaughter tools and explain the prohibition of teeth and nails based on the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij.

Core Idea
Any sharp object that causes blood flow is valid for slaughter, except teeth (bone) and nails (claw-like).

Islamic slaughter (dhabh) requires severing the jugular veins to cause rapid blood loss. While a knife is common, the Prophet ﷺ permitted other sharp objects when knives were unavailable. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling based on the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij, clarifying which tools are valid and why teeth and nails are excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the matn: permissible tools include laytah (reed), marwah (stone), and any sharp object that makes blood flow. The exceptions are sinn (tooth) and zufr (nail).
The ruling covers all forms of dhabh, not only for meat but also for valid sacrifice.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij, where the Prophet permitted slaughter with a stone or reed when knives were absent, prohibiting only teeth and nails.
This is a sahih hadith (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ma anhar al-dam' (whatever makes blood flow) indicates permissibility for any tool that efficiently cuts veins. The exception 'illa al-sinn wa al-zufr' excludes teeth and nails categorically.
The 'illa (effective cause) for prohibition: teeth are bone, nails are like claws, causing pain and unclean cutting.
4
Understand the exceptions: tooth and nail
The hadith explains: 'As for the tooth, it is bone' (thus not sharp enough or causes suffering) and 'the nail is the knife of the Abyssinians' (a crude method). Hanafis specify they must be attached (in the mouth/finger); detached teeth/nails may be permissible if sharp? There is difference.
The attached condition is derived from the hadith's context and the need for a clean cut.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Any modern sharp object (glass, sharp metal, even a sharpened plastic if it cuts) is valid, provided it is not a tooth or nail. Detached bone (e.g., a sharpened bone from an animal) – is it permissible? Some Hanafi scholars prohibit bone altogether due to qiyas on tooth, but the text only prohibits attached teeth.
The general principle: permissibility for any tool that severs the veins, unless it is a tooth or nail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز الذبح بالليطة والمروة وبكل شيء انهر الدم الا السن والظفر (٢٨) اور جائز ہے ذبح کرنا بانس کی بتی سے اور تیز پتھر سے اور ہر اس چیز سے جو خون بہا دے سوائے دانت اور ناخن سے جو لگے ہوئے ہوں۔ بانس کا ٹکڑا جو پتلا اور دھاردار ہو یا تیز پتھر ہو یا ہر وہ چیز جو دھاردار ہو جس سے رگیں کٹ کر خون بہنے لگے۔ البتہ تالو میں لگے دانت اور انگلی میں لگے ہوئے ناخن سے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بانس کے ٹکڑے اور دھار دار پتھر سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے کہ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن رافع بن خديج قال اتيت رسول الله لله فقلت يا رسول الله ! انا نلقى العدو غدا وليس معنا مدى افنذبح بالمروة وشقة العصا ؟ فقال رسول الله الله ارن او اعجل ما انهر الدم وذكر اسم الله عليه فكلوا مالم يكن سن وظفر وساحدثكم عن ذلك اما السن فعظم واما الظفر فمدى الحبشة (ابو داؤد شریف، باب الذبيحه بالمروة ص٣٣ نمبر ٢٨٢ / بخاری شریف، باب ما انهر الدم من القصب والمروة والحدید ص ٨٢٧ نمبر ٥٥٠٣ ، نسائی شریف، اباحة الذبح بالقووص ٦١١ نمبر ٤٤٠٦) اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی بھی دھار دار چیز جو حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور سے بانس کے چھلکے سے ذبح کرنے کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا ہر وہ چیز جو او داج رگوں کو کاٹ دے اس سے جائز ہے سوائے دانت اور نائن کے (ب) حضرت ابن عمر نے نفع سے روکا یعنی حرام مغز تک چھری پہنچانے سے روکا، فرماتے ہیں کہ ہڈی سے پہلے پہلے تک کاٹے پھر چھوڑ دے یہاں تک کہ مرجائے ( ج ) میں حضور کے پاس آیا اور پوچھا یا رسول اللہ ! ہم کل دشمن سے مقابلہ کریں گے اور ہمارے پاس کوئی لمبی چھری نہیں ہے تو کیا ہم پتھر کے ٹکڑے اور لاٹھی کے چھلکے سے ذبح کریں؟ آپ نے فرمایا حتی کے ساتھ کاٹو اور جلدی کرو ۔ ہر وہ چیز جو خون بہا دے اور بسم اللہ اس پر پڑھے تو کھا و بشرطیکہ دانت اور ناخن نہ ہو۔ اور تم سے بیان کرتا ہوں بہر حال دانت تو ہڈی ہے اور ناخن تو حبشہ والوں کی چھری ہے۔
And it is permissible to slaughter with a reed (laytah) and a sharp stone (marwah) and with everything that makes blood flow, except a tooth and a nail. (28) It is permissible to slaughter with a reed stick and a sharp stone and with anything that draws blood, except a tooth and a nail that are attached (in the mouth or finger). A piece of bamboo that is thin and sharp, or a sharp stone, or anything sharp that cuts veins and causes blood to flow. However, slaughter with a tooth attached in the palate and a nail attached to the finger is not permissible. Slaughter with a piece of bamboo and a sharp stone is permissible because of the hadith: from Rafi' ibn Khadij, he said: I came to the Messenger of Allah and said: O Messenger of Allah! We will meet the enemy tomorrow and we do not have knives with us. Shall we slaughter with a sharp stone (marwah) and a piece of stick? He said: Use what makes blood flow quickly, and mention Allah's name over it, then eat, as long as it is not a tooth or a nail. And I will tell you about that: as for the tooth, it is bone, and as for the nail, it is the knife of the Abyssinians. (Abu Dawud, chapter: slaughter with a stone, p. 33, no. 282; Bukhari, chapter: what makes blood flow from reed, stone, and iron, p. 827, no. 5503; Nasa'i, chapter: permissibility of slaughter with a reed, p. 611, no. 4406) From this hadith it is also understood that any sharp thing... Footnote: (a) I asked the Prophet about slaughtering with a reed covering, and he said: everything that cuts the jugular veins is permissible, except a tooth and a nail. (b) Ibn Umar forbade nakh' (severing the spinal cord) - meaning he forbade bringing the knife to the marrow, saying: he cuts what is before the bone, then leaves it until it dies. (c) I came to the Prophet and asked: O Messenger of Allah! We will meet the enemy tomorrow and we have no knives. Shall we slaughter with a piece of stone and a piece of stick? He said: Cut with it quickly, and whatever makes blood flow and you mention Allah's name over it, eat, as long as it is not a tooth or a nail. And I will tell you: the tooth is a bone, and the nail is the knife of the Abyssinians.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the tools permissible for Islamic slaughter. The main ruling: slaughter is valid using a laytah (a reed splitter, i.e., a sharp piece of bamboo), a marwah (a sharp stone), or any sharp object that causes blood to flow, except teeth and nails. The reasoning is that the objective is to sever the jugular veins and cause blood to flow efficiently. The prohibition of teeth and nails is due to their being bone (teeth) or considered the knife of the Abyssinians (nails), implying they are crude and may cause unnecessary suffering. The hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij is cited: in a battlefield situation where knives were unavailable, the Prophet permitted slaughter with a stone or a piece of wood, provided it causes blood flow, and prohibited teeth and nails. The commentary adds that teeth must be attached (i.e., in the mouth) and nails attached (on fingers), implying that if detached, they might be considered like any other bone or sharp object. The footnote also mentions Ibn Umar's prohibition of nakh' (severing the spinal cord) before death, which is a separate issue. The key principle is that any sharp object that efficiently cuts the veins and causes blood to flow is acceptable, as long as it is not made of bone (tooth) or nail (since nail is like a claw).

Key Terms
الليطة (al-laytah): A reed splitter; a sharp piece of bamboo used for slaughter.
المروة (al-marwah): A sharp stone; a flint or similar sharp-edged stone.
السن (al-sinn): The tooth; specifically a tooth that is attached in the mouth, not a detached one.
الظفر (al-zufr): The nail; specifically a nail attached to the finger, considered akin to a claw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT permissible for slaughtering an animal according to the Hanafi school based on the hadith cited?
A) A sharp stone
B) A piece of sharp bamboo
C) A tooth that is attached in the mouth
D) A metal knife

Key Takeaway
Islamic slaughter is valid with any sharp object that efficiently cuts the jugular veins and causes blood flow, except teeth (bone) and nails (claws).

The Recommendation to Sharpen the Knife Before Slaughter
States the recommendation to sharpen the knife before slaughtering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharpening the knife before slaughter and identify its proof from the hadith of Shaddad ibn Aws.

Core Idea
Sharpening the knife before slaughter is a recommended sunnah to minimize suffering.

This lesson addresses a common practice in animal slaughter: sharpening the knife beforehand. While some may consider this optional or merely practical, Islamic law elevates it to a recommended act based on a clear prophetic command. We will examine the ruling and the hadith proof cited in the text.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify the act (sharpening the knife) and the ruling (mustahabb/sunnah mu'akkadah). The text explicitly calls it 'mustahabb' and the hadith commands sharpening with 'li yahidd' (let him sharpen).
In Hanafi terminology, 'mustahabb' and 'sunnah mu'akkadah' are often used interchangeably for strongly recommended acts.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Shaddad ibn Aws is cited: 'Allah has prescribed excellence in everything... let one of you sharpen his knife and give ease to his slaughtered animal.' This is a primary proof.
The hadith is reported by Muslim and Abu Dawud, classified as ahad (single-chain), hence zanni al-thubut.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'li yahidd' indicates obligation in principle, but the context of 'ihsan' (excellence) and the general nature of the command (prescribing excellence in everything) shifts the ruling to recommendation, as affirmed by Hanafi usul.
If it were obligatory, the Prophet would have required it unconditionally; the mention of 'ihsan' softens the imperative to recommendation.
4
Apply the ruling practically
In practice, a Muslim should sharpen the knife before slaughter to reduce the animal's pain. This is not obligatory, but omitting it without excuse is contrary to the sunnah.
The underlying principle (ihsan) applies to all acts of killing, including hunting and execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

'Shafrah' means a long knife.

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (29) on the recommendation to sharpen the knife before slaughter. The author cites a hadith from Shaddad ibn Aws where the Prophet commands excellence in all acts, specifically in slaughtering: sharpen the knife and give ease to the animal. This is a Sunnah Mu'akkadah (emphasized recommendation) to minimize suffering. The hadith is a primary proof in Hanafi fiqh for the requirement of ihsan (excellence) in slaughter. The text also defines 'hadd' (sharpening) and 'shafrah' (long knife).

Key Terms
شفرة (shafrah): A long knife used for slaughter
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended (less than sunnah mu'akkadah in some contexts, but here used for a recommended act)

Key Takeaway
Sharpening the knife before slaughter is a recommended sunnah based on the prophetic command to practice excellence (ihsan).

Ruling of Udhiyyah: Wajib on Capable Resident Muslims
States obligation of qurbani and its conditions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on udhiyyah, list its four conditions, and explain the evidence from the hadith of Abu Hurairah that establishes wujub.

Core Idea
Qurbani is wajib for those with capacity; the Prophet's threat proves it is an obligation, not a mere sunnah.

This passage establishes a key act of worship during Eid al-Adha. The Hanafi school holds that qurbani is wajib for every free, Muslim, resident, and wealthy person. While some scholars consider it sunnah, the formidable threat in the hadith—'let him not come near our place of Eid prayer'—is the decisive proof for wujub. We will dissect the conditions, evidence, and the intra- and inter-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Read the opening statement: udhiyyah is wajib upon four types of persons. Note each condition (free, Muslim, resident, wealthy) and why each is necessary.
The conditions are cumulative; all must be present for wujub.
2
Extract the Quranic proof
Find the verse 'Fasalli li rabbika wanhar' (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). The imperative 'wanhar' is the key. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.
This verse alone is not sufficient to prove wujub, as the context could be general; it is supported by the hadith.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
Read the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our place of Eid prayer.' This severe threat indicates that the act is obligatory, not merely recommended.
The threat (wa'id) is the strongest indicator of wujub in this context.
4
Consider the opposing views
The passage notes that Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it sunnah. Their proof is the continuous practice of the Prophet and Muslims. Understand the Hanafi response: the specific threat overrides general practice.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to the strength of the threat.
5
Conclude with mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is wajib. Therefore, a qualifying person who omits qurbani is sinful and must make up for it? (Note: make-up is not required; the sin is for abandoning a wajib. But some later scholars say qada is not required because it is time-bound.)
The practical consequence: one must sacrifice if conditions are met; otherwise, one is sinful.

Source Text

Book of Udhiyyah. [2627] (1) Udhiyyah is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person on the day of Udhiyyah. Complete Book of Udhiyyah: Necessary: The animal slaughtered with the intention of qurbani on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah is called udhiyyah. The evidence for qurbani is in the verse: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (a) (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). This verse commands sacrificing, which indicates qurbani. And in the hadith: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our place of Eid prayer.' (b) (Ibn Majah, Chapter on Udhiyyah: Is It Wajib or Not? p. 455 no. 13123 / Dar Qutni, Book of Drinks, vol. 4, p. 185 no. 4698) In this hadith it is that whoever has capacity for qurbani and does not sacrifice, then he should not come to our Eid prayer ground; from this obligation is proven. [2627] (1) Qurbani is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, and wealthy person on the day of qurbani. A person who is free, Muslim, resident (not a traveler), and wealthy during the days of qurbani, then qurbani is wajib upon him. The reason for each: the evidence for being free and Muslim has passed repeatedly that worship is only upon a Muslim; qurbani is a worship, therefore it is not upon a disbeliever. And a slave has no wealth, so how will he sacrifice? And resident because a traveler will not have ease in sacrificing. But if he does it, the qurbani will be fulfilled. The Prophet sacrificed during travel. From Thawban: The Messenger of Allah sacrificed then said: 'O Thawban, prepare this sheep's meat for us.' He said: 'I kept feeding him from it until we arrived in Madinah.' (c) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Traveler Sacrificing, p. 33 no. 2816 / Bukhari, Chapter on One Who Slaughtered Another's Udhiyyah, p. 834 no. 5559) From this hadith it is known that a traveler can sacrifice, but it is not wajib upon him. And it is wajib when one is wealthy. The evidence is that if poor, from where will he sacrifice? He himself is needy. Wealthy means that he possesses the nisab of zakat during the days of qurbani. (2) And the hadith passed: from Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our place of Eid prayer.' (Ibn Majah no. 3123) In this hadith it is that if one has capacity then qurbani is wajib, otherwise not. And qurbani is wajib, not sunnah. The evidence is the hadith above, because the Prophet said: 'If one does not sacrifice despite capacity, he should not come to my Eid prayer ground.' This type of threat occurs for abandoning an obligation. Note: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i consider it sunnah. In a hadith: I asked Ibn Umar about udhiyyah: 'Is it wajib?' He said: 'The Messenger of Allah sacrificed and the Muslims after him.' Footnotes: (a) Pray to your Lord and sacrifice. (b) He said: Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our Eid prayer ground. (c) Thawban said: The Prophet sacrificed then said: 'O Thawban, prepare this sheep's meat for us.' He said: 'I kept feeding him from it until we arrived in Madinah.'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the obligation (wujub) of qurbani (udhiyyah). The author begins by stating the ruling: qurbani is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident (muqim), and wealthy (musir) person during the days of Eid al-Adha. The commentary explains each condition: freedom excludes slaves, Islam excludes disbelievers, residence excludes travelers (though a traveler may sacrifice if desired, it is not obligatory), and wealth means possessing the nisab of zakat during the days of sacrifice. The primary proof is the verse 'Fasalli li rabbika wanhar' (Surah al-Kawthar) which commands sacrifice, and the hadith of Abu Hurairah that threatens with deprivation from the Eid prayer ground for whoever has capacity but does not sacrifice. The author argues that such a threat indicates wujub, not just sunnah. The passage also notes that Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it sunnah, not wajib. This intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab difference is recorded, but the relied-upon Hanafi position remains wujub due to the severity of the threat. The author further supports the permissibility of sacrificing while traveling with the hadith of Thawban, showing it is valid though not obligatory. The footnote clarifies the verse and hadith sources.

Key Terms
الاضحية (al-udhiyyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of Eid al-Adha (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) with intention of qurbani.
موسر (musir): Wealthy, defined as possessing the nisab of zakat on the days of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Fard ain
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Udhiyyah is wajib (not sunnah) for every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person, proven by the severe threat in the hadith of Abu Hurairah.

Sacrificing for Oneself and Minor Children
Ruling with proof and intra-school difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sacrificing for minor children and identify the evidence and difference of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A father must sacrifice for his minor child from the child's wealth if the child has nisab, based on analogy with the Prophet's sacrifice for his family.

This lesson explores the ruling on udhiyah (sacrifice) for one's minor children. While the act itself is sunnah mu'akkadah for an adult, the question arises: who sacrifices for a child who possesses wealth but is not legally accountable? The Hanafi school addresses this with a ruling supported by the Prophet's practice and analogical reasoning, though there is an alternative view within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is udhiyah (Qurbani) on behalf of oneself and minor children. The ruling is that the father sacrifices for his minor child from the child's wealth if the child has nisab.
The child cannot perform the act himself because he is murafa' al-qalam (not legally accountable).
2
Understand the legal basis
The father is the guardian of the minor child's wealth. Since the child cannot fulfill this sunnah, the father does it on his behalf, just as the Prophet sacrificed for his family.
The responsibility is derived from guardianship (wilayah).
3
Examine the dalil
The Prophet's sacrifice for his wives (hadith of Aisha) is used as evidence. By qiyas (analogy), the father, being responsible for his family like the Prophet, should sacrifice for his minor children.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Another narration within the Hanafi school holds that it is not wajib because the child is not obligated; the father may do it voluntarily.
This shows that even within the school, there is a range of views.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that it is wajib upon the father from the child's wealth if the child possesses nisab.
This is the position that is typically given for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۲۸] (٢) يذبح عن نفسه وعن ولده الصغير [۲۶۲۹] (۳) ويذبح عن كل واحد منهم جرت به السنة (الف) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الاضاحی واجب ھی ام لا؟ ص ۲۵۵ نمبر ۳۱۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قربانی سنت

[ ۲۶۲۸] (۲) قربانی کرے اپنی جانب سے اور اپنی چھوٹی اولاد کی جانب سے۔ چھوٹی اولاد کے پاس اتنا مال ہے کہ وہ صاحب نصاب ہے تو وہ خود قربانی نہیں کرسکتی کیونکہ مرفوع القلم ہیں اس لئے ان کے مال سے
باپ قربانی کرے گا۔
حضور نے اہل بیت کی جانب سے قربانی کی ہے کیونکہ آپ ذمہ دار تھے۔ اسی طرح باپ چھوٹی اولاد کا ذمہ دار ہے اس لئے باپ اس کی جانب سے قربانی کرے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة ان النبي الا الله دخل عليها ... فلما كنا بمنى اتيت بلحم بقر فقلت ما هذا؟ قالوا ضحى رسول الله الا الله عن ازواجه بالبقر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الاضحیة للمسافر و النساء ص ۸۳۲ نمبر ۵۵۲۸ رابن ماجه شریف، باب اضاحی رسول الله ص ۲۵۵ نمبر ۳۱۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے اپنے اہل بیت کی جانب سے قربانی کی اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اپنی اولاد کی جانب سے بھی قربانی کر سکتا ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ بچہ مرفوع القلم ہے اس لئے چاہے مالدار ہو لیکن اس کی جانب سے باپ پر قربانی واجب نہیں ہے اور نہ بچے پر
قربانی واجب ہے۔
[2628] (2) He sacrifices for himself and for his minor child. [2629] (3) He sacrifices for each one of them as the Sunnah has established (Ibn Majah, no. 3124). This hadith shows that sacrifice is sunnah. [2628] (2) Sacrifice for himself and for his minor children. If the minor child has so much wealth that he is a sahib-e-nisab, then he cannot sacrifice himself because he is murafa' al-qalam (not legally accountable); therefore the father will sacrifice from his wealth. The Prophet sacrificed on behalf of his family because he was responsible. Similarly, the father is responsible for his minor children, so the father will sacrifice on his behalf. (2) In the hadith from Aisha: The Prophet entered upon her... when we were in Mina, I was given beef and I asked: What is this? They said: The Prophet sacrificed on behalf of his wives with a cow (Bukhari, no. 5528; Ibn Majah, no. 312). This hadith shows that the Prophet sacrificed on behalf of his family; by analogy, one can also sacrifice on behalf of his children. Another narration states that the child is murafa' al-qalam, so even if he is wealthy, sacrifice is not wajib upon the father on his behalf, nor is it wajib upon the child.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author addresses the permissibility of sacrificing for minor children. The main ruling: a father should sacrifice for himself and for his minor (young) children. The reasoning: minor children are not legally accountable (murafa' al-qalam) and cannot perform the act themselves, so the father, as guardian, sacrifices from the child's wealth if the child is wealthy enough. The evidence is the Prophet's sacrifice on behalf of his family (Aisha's hadith) and analogical reasoning. However, there is an alternative narration that since the child is not accountable, neither the father nor the child is obliged to sacrifice, but the father may do so voluntarily. This indicates a difference of opinion within the school: some say it is wajib upon the father from the child's wealth if the child has nisab, others say it is not wajib but merely mustahabb.

Key Terms
مرفوع القلم (murafa' al-qalam): One who is not subject to legal obligations, i.e., minor children, due to lack of accountability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ruling in this lesson, who is responsible for sacrificing for a minor child who owns nisab?
A) The child himself
B) The mother
C) The father
D) No one; it is not required

Key Takeaway
The father is obligated to sacrifice for his minor child from the child's wealth if the child possesses nisab, based on analogy with the Prophet's delegation for his family.

Number of Animals per Person and Permissibility of Sharing
Specifies the number of animals per person for sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of animals for sacrifice and apply it to determine valid sharing arrangements.

Core Idea
One goat for one person; one camel or cow for up to seven only.

The rules of Qurbani include clear limits on how many people can share an animal. This lesson examines the precise numbers established by the Sunnah and the evidence behind them. Understanding these limits ensures that your sacrifice is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi rule: one goat suffices for only one person; one camel or cow suffices for up to seven persons, not more. Fewer than seven may share a large animal.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Anas (Bukhari no. 5558, Muslim no. 1966) describing the Prophet sacrificing two rams for himself. The hadith of Aisha about the Prophet sacrificing a cow for his wives supports the permissibility of sharing a cow.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet sacrificed two rams for himself alone. If a ram could be shared, one would have sufficed. This indicates each small animal is for one person. The cow hadith shows a large animal can serve multiple.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Maliki, Hanbali) allow sharing a goat. The Hanafi response is that there is no explicit evidence for sharing a goat, and the Prophet's practice confirms the opposite.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi; it is based on the Prophetic practice and lack of counter-evidence. The practical consequence is that a shared goat sacrifice is invalid in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہے۔

باپ قربانی کرے گا۔
حضور نے اہل بیت کی جانب سے قربانی کی ہے کیونکہ آپ ذمہ دار تھے۔ اسی طرح باپ چھوٹی اولاد کا ذمہ دار ہے اس لئے باپ اس کی جانب سے قربانی کرے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة ان النبي الا الله دخل عليها ... فلما كنا بمنى اتيت بلحم بقر فقلت ما هذا؟ قالوا ضحى رسول الله الا الله عن ازواجه بالبقر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الاضحیة للمسافر و النساء ص ۸۳۲ نمبر ۵۵۲۸ رابن ماجه شریف، باب اضاحی رسول الله ص ۲۵۵ نمبر ۳۱۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے اپنے اہل بیت کی جانب سے قربانی کی اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اپنی اولاد کی جانب سے بھی قربانی کر سکتا ہے۔ دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ بچہ مرفوع القلم ہے اس لئے چاہے مالدار ہو لیکن اس کی جانب سے باپ پر قربانی واجب نہیں ہے اور نہ بچے پر
قربانی واجب ہے۔
[2629] (3) He sacrifices for each one of them as the Sunnah has established (Ibn Majah, no. 3124). This hadith shows that sacrifice is sunnah. [2628] (2) [Repeated] He sacrifices for himself and for his minor child... [but the intended content is from the start]. Actually, the passage for (3) continues: And he sacrifices for each one of them as the Sunnah has established. One goat suffices for one person, not for two. And a camel or cow suffices for seven persons; more than seven cannot share. However, less than seven (e.g., five or four) can share. There is no hadith about sharing in a goat. If sharing in a goat were allowed, it would have been mentioned. Yes, it is possible that one person sacrifices a goat voluntarily and gives its reward to many. Anas said: The Prophet sacrificed two horned rams; I saw him placing his foot on their sides, saying Bismillah and Allahu Akbar, and slaughtering them with his own hand (Bukhari, no. 5558; Muslim, no. 1966). This hadith shows that the Prophet sacrificed two rams for himself, indicating that a ram is only for one person. Footnote: (a) I asked Ibn Umar about sacrifices: Are they wajib? He said: The Prophet and the Muslims after him sacrificed, and this is an ongoing sunnah. (b) Aisha said: The Prophet entered upon her... when we were in Mina, I was given beef... they said: The Prophet sacrificed on behalf of his wives with a cow. (c) The Prophet sacrificed two horned rams.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof specifying the number of animals per person. The key rule: one goat (or sheep) is sufficient only for one person. A camel or cow is sufficient for up to seven persons, but not more than seven. Fewer than seven can share. The evidence for the one-per-person rule comes from the Prophet's practice of sacrificing two rams for himself, showing each ram was for one person. There is no evidence for sharing goats. Additionally, the hadith of the Prophet sacrificing on behalf of his wives with a cow shows that one cow can serve multiple people (in that case, multiple wives). The text also mentions that while sharing a cow/camel is allowed, a goat cannot be shared. However, one can sacrifice a goat and gift the reward to others. The mention of 'this hadith shows sacrifice is sunnah' is a footnote referencing the earlier disagreement; it does not affect the numerical rule.

Key Terms
الشاة (al-shāh): A goat or sheep; an individual small livestock animal used for sacrifice.
البعير (al-ba'ir): A camel; can be shared by up to seven persons in sacrifice.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): Sharing in the sacrifice; allowed for camel/cow up to seven, not for goat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A goat is valid only for one person; a camel or cow is valid for up to seven persons, and no evidence allows sharing a goat.

The Obligation of Consecutive Fasting in Kafarat al-Yamin
Inter-madhhab dispute on consecutive fasting in kafarat al-yamin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on consecutive fasting in kafarat al-yamin, explain the proof from the qira'ah of Ibn Mas'ud, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The three fasts in kafarat al-yamin must be consecutive – a condition proven by the qira'ah of Ibn Mas'ud.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: must the three days of fasting in kafarat al-yamin be observed consecutively? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on the recitation of Companion 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing the absence of the word 'consecutive' in the Quranic text. Understanding the proof structure and the weight of different evidence is central to this discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
First, note that the Hanafi school requires three consecutive days of fasting when one cannot free a slave, feed, or clothe the poor. The ruling is derived from the qira'ah of Ibn Mas'ud (mutatabi'at) and an athar from Ibn 'Abbas.
The Hanafi school treats this as a wajib condition.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i permits fasting on separate days, arguing that the Quranic verse does not specify consecutiveness. He also cites an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri allowing separation.
The Shafi'i view sees consecutiveness as recommended, not obligatory.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on the legal authority of a Companion's qira'ah (qira'ah shadhdhah) as a valid proof (dalil). The athar from Ibn 'Abbas is also a stronger evidence than the one from al-Hasan.
Hanafi usul accepts ahad and shadhdh qira'ah as proof for hukm tashri'i.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: a Hanafi must restart the sequence if a day is missed; a Shafi'i may fast separate days without penalty.
This directly affects how an individual fulfills the kafarah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The author presents the Hanafi position as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) by providing explicit proofs and noting the weakness of the opposing evidence.
The commentary follows the standard Hanafi methodology of giving more weight to Companion practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

رکھے۔
ا امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پے در پے رکھے یا متفرق طور پر رکھے دونوں کا اختیار ہے۔
آیت قرآنی میں پے در پے کی قدر نہیں ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الحسن انه كان لايرى بأسا ان يفرق بين الثلاثة الايام في كفارة اليمين (ه) ( سنن میبقی ، باب التخمير بين الاطعام والكسوة والعتق فمن لم يسجد وصيام ثلاثة ایام ج عاشر ص ۱۰۳، نمبر ۲۰۰۰۷) اس اثر

(2667) (24) So if he is not able to do any of these three things, he fasts three consecutive days. When he is not able to free a slave, or feed, or clothe, then he fasts three days. Its proof is in the verse: 'But whoever cannot find [the means], then a fast of three days' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89). That is, if he does not find the first three things, then he fasts three days. And he fasts consecutively, its proof is that in the recitation of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, it is 'fasting three consecutive days' (fasalatu thalathati ayyamin mutatabi'at). So fast consecutive days. Indeed, Ibn Mas'ud used to recite 'fasting three consecutive days' (c) (al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-tabi' fi sawm al-kafarah, vol. 10, p. 104, no. 20012; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab siyam thalathati ayyam wa taqdim al-takfir, vol. 8, p. 135, no. 16102). (2) Another athar: From Ibn 'Abbas concerning the verse of kafarat al-yamin, he said: 'He has a choice among these three first. If he does not find any of these, then fasting three consecutive days' (d) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-takhayyur bayn al-it'am wa al-kiswah wa al-'itq, vol. 10, p. 102, no. 20006). From this athar also it is known that he fasts consecutive days. Then Imam al-Shafi'i says that he has the option to fast consecutively or separately. The Quranic verse does not mention consecutiveness. (2) An athar: From al-Hasan, he did not see any harm in separating the three days in kafarat al-yamin (e) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-takhayyur bayn al-it'am wa al-kiswah wa al-'itq, vol. 10, p. 103, no. 20007). Footnote: (a) 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud used to recite 'three consecutive days'. (b) Ibn 'Abbas says: He has a choice among these three first; if he does not find any of these, then fasting three consecutive days. (c) Al-Hasan says: There is no harm in separating the three days in kafarat al-yamin.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on whether the three days of fasting in kafarat al-yamin must be consecutive (mutatabi'at) or may be separate. The author first states the Hanafi ruling: if one cannot afford any of the three options (freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, clothing ten poor), then one must fast three consecutive days. The proof is twofold: first, the general Quranic verse (5:89) 'then a fast of three days' is understood by the Hanafi school to imply consecutiveness, as evidenced by the recitation of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who read 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive). Second, an athar from Ibn 'Abbas explicitly states that after the choice among the three options, the fasting is three consecutive days. The passage then reports Imam al-Shafi'i's position: he permits either consecutive or separate fasting, arguing that the Quranic verse does not mention consecutiveness, and citing an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri who saw no harm in separating the days. The Hanafi school responds that the recitation of a Companion (Ibn Mas'ud) is a valid proof (qira'at shadhdhah) that clarifies the Quranic text, and the consensus of the Companions (as reflected in Ibn 'Abbas's statement) supports consecutiveness. The footnote summarizes the key evidence.

Key Terms
متتابعات (mutatabi'at): Consecutive, without a break. Used to describe the required sequence of fasting days in kafarat al-yamin.
قراءة شاذة (qira'ah shadhdhah): An irregular recitation of the Quran that does not match the 'Uthmanic codex. In fiqh, it can be used as a legal proof but not as Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the consecutiveness of the three fasts in kafarat al-yamin?
A) Consecutive is recommended but not required
B) Consecutive is a required condition (wajib)
C) It is permissible to fast separately
D) Only fasting on three specific days is allowed

Key Takeaway
The three fasts in kafarat al-yamin must be consecutive according to the Hanafi school, a condition proven by the recitation of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and the practice of Ibn 'Abbas.

Ruling on Two Weighings Not Considered Separation
States a ruling on sequential weighings in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding two weighings in fulfilling an oath and identify the condition that determines whether they are considered separate receipts.

Core Idea
Two weighings with no unrelated activity between them count as one receipt in oaths.

When fulfilling an oath that requires giving something by weight, performing the weighing in two parts can sometimes be treated as one continuous act. This lesson clarifies when that is the case, based on the absence of unrelated activity and the continuity of the gathering. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary violation of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with two separate weighings of an item. The ruling is that the person is not guilty of breaking the oath (lam yahnath) if no unrelated activity occurs between them.
2
Identify the condition
The key condition is that no unrelated activity (except the act of weighing itself) takes place between the two weighings. Additionally, the weighings must occur in the same gathering (majlis).
The commentary emphasizes that common usage ('urf) does not call this separate receipt.
3
Apply the ruling
In practice, any activity that is not part of the weighing process (like talking, walking away, or handling unrelated items) would break the continuity and make the weighings separate, potentially breaking the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزنين لم يتشاغل بينهما الا بعمل الوزن لم يحنث وليس ذلك بتفريق کیونکہ یہ تو مجبوری ہے۔ اور محاورے میں اس کو متفرق طور پر وصول کرنا نہیں کہتے ہیں۔ محاورے میں اس وقت متفرق طور پر وصول کرنا کہیں گے جب ایک مرتبہ وزن کر کے تھوڑا سا لے پھر مجلس بدل جائے پھر دوسری مجلس میں تھوڑا سا وزن کر کے وصول کرے تب متفرق طور پر لینا شمار کریں گے۔ مجبوری میں ایک ہی مجلس میں دو مرتبہ وزن کرنا متفرق طور پر لینا نہیں ہے۔ یہ ایک ہی مرتبہ وصول کرنا ہے۔
And two weighings: if he is not occupied between them except with the act of weighing, he is not guilty (of breaking an oath), and that is not considered separation. Because this is a compulsion. And in common parlance, this is not called receiving in separate installments. In common parlance, receiving in separate installments is when he weighs once and takes a little, then changes the gathering, then in another gathering weighs a little and receives it. Then it would be considered taking separately. In compulsion, weighing twice in one gathering is not taking separately. This is considered one receipt.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on oaths (Kitaab al-Imaan). It addresses the situation of sequential weighings when fulfilling an oath that requires something by weight. The ruling: if someone performs the two weighings and does not engage in any unrelated activity between them, he is not guilty of breaking the oath, and the two weighings are not considered a separation (i.e., it is as if he did it all at once). The commentator explains that this is based on necessity: in common usage, receiving in separate installments requires a change of gathering. But when done in one gathering due to necessity, it is considered a single receipt. Thus, the oath is fulfilled.

Key Terms
وزنين (wazanayn): Two weighings or two instances of weighing
يحنث (yahinath): He becomes guilty of breaking an oath

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is guilty of breaking the oath because weighings are separate.
B) He is not guilty and the oath is fulfilled as one receipt.
C) He must repeat the weighings.
D) The ruling depends on the type of oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sequential weighings with no unrelated activity between them count as a single receipt for oath fulfillment.

Timing of Oath Breach: Death Before Fulfillment
Ruling and proof for oath broken upon death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when an oath is considered broken if the swearer dies before performing the act, and explain the Hanafi proof for this ruling.

Core Idea
An oath to do an act without time limit is only broken at the last moment of life, because hope continues until death.

The question of when an oath becomes broken (hanath) is critical for determining whether expiation is required. In this passage, the Hanafi school addresses a specific case: a person swears to go to Basra but dies before going. The ruling clarifies that hanath occurs at the very last moment of life, not earlier. The commentator supports this with the Prophet's ḥadīth about the Treaty of Ḥudaybiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is swearing an oath to go to Basra without specifying a time. The ruling: if the swearer dies before going, he becomes guilty (hanith) at the last moment of his life.
The oath is valid and binding; breaking it incurs kaffarah.
2
Understand the rationale
During his lifetime, there was always hope that he might fulfill the oath. Only upon death does it become certain that he cannot fulfill it. Therefore, hanath is declared at the final moment.
Hope (rajā') is a key concept: as long as life continues, fulfillment is possible.
3
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith of Hudaybiyah: the Prophet promised the Companions they would circumambulate the Kaaba but did not specify the year. When they returned without doing so, the Prophet clarified that the promise was for 'sometime' in life. This shows that an oath without a time limit remains possible until death.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, Kitab al-Shurut.
4
Confirm the timing
Thus, the moment of death is the only point of certainty. The swearer is considered a breaker of the oath at the last part of his life.
This ruling applies to any oath to perform an act without a fixed time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن حلف لياتين البصرة فلم يأتها حتى مات حنث فى آخر جزء من اجزاء حيوته. کیونکہ زندگی بھر امید کی جائے گی کہ وہ کبھی نہ کبھی بصرہ جائے گا۔ البتہ موت کے وقت اندازہ ہوا کہ قسم کے مطابق بصرہ نہ جا سکا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ ہم بیت اللہ کا طواف کریں گے لیکن صلح حدیبیہ کے وقت واپس آگئے تو حضرت عمر نے پوچھا کہ کیا آپ نہیں فرماتے تھے کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف کریں گے تو آپ نے فرمایا یہ تو نہیں کہا تھا کہ اسی سال طواف کریں گے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ زندگی میں کبھی بھی طواف کریں گے یہی کافی ہے۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن المسور بن مخرمه ومروان قالا خرج رسول الله الله زمن الحديبية ... قلت او ليس كنت تحدثتنا انا سنأتى البيت فنطوف به ؟ قال بلی ! فاخبرتك انا نأتيه العام ؟ قال قلت لا! قال فانک اتيه ومطوف به (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشروط فی الجہاد والمصالحة مع اہل الحرب وكتابة الشروط ص ۳۷۷ نمبر ۲۷۳۲/۲۷۳۱ کتاب الشروط) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زندگی میں کبھی بھی طواف کر سکو گے۔ یہی مطلب ہے میرے اس کہنے کا کہ آپ لوگ بیت اللہ کا طواف کریں گے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زندگی کے آخری لمحے میں معلوم ہوگا کہ اب یہ قسم پوری نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے اس وقت اس کو حانث قرار دیا جائے گا۔ حاشیه : (الف) حضور حدیبیہ کے زمانے میں مدینہ سے نکلے حضرت عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے پوچھا کیا آپ نہیں فرماتے تھے کہ ان شاء اللہ ہم بیت اللہ جائیں گے ؟ آپ نے فرمایا کیوں نہیں؟ لیکن کیا یہ بتایا تھا کہ اس سال ہی جائیں گے؟ میں نے کہا نہیں ! آپ نے فرمایا تم لوگ بیت اللہ جاؤ گے اور طواف بھی کرو گے۔
And whoever swears that he will certainly go to Basra, and he does not go there until he dies, he becomes guilty of breaking the oath in the last part of his life. Because hope continues throughout life that he might go to Basra someday. However, at the time of death it becomes evident that he could not go according to the oath. (2) The hadith hints at this: The Prophet said, 'We will circumambulate the House of Allah,' but they returned at the time of Hudaybiyah. Umar asked, 'Did you not tell us that we would circumambulate the Kaaba?' The Prophet said, 'I did not say that we would do it this year.' So the meaning is that doing it sometime in life is sufficient. The hadith fragment: from al-Miswar ibn Makhrama and Marwan, they said: The Messenger of Allah went out at the time of Hudaybiyah... I said, 'Did you not tell us that we would come to the House and circumambulate it?' He said, 'Yes! But did I tell you we would come this year?' I said, 'No.' He said, 'Then you will come to it and circumambulate it.' (Bukhari, Kitab al-Shurut, 2731/2732). This hadith indicates that you will circumambulate sometime in life. This is the meaning of my saying that you will circumambulate. From this hadith it is known that at the last moment of life it will be known that he cannot fulfill the oath, so at that time he will be considered a breaker of the oath. Footnote: (a) In the time of Hudaybiyyah, the Prophet left Medina. Umar said: I asked, 'Did you not say that we would go to the House of Allah, if Allah wills?' He said, 'Yes. But did I tell you that we would go this year?' I said, 'No.' He said, 'You will go to the House and circumambulate it.'
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on oaths. The ruling: if someone swears an oath to go to Basra and dies before going, he becomes guilty (hanith) at the last moment of his life. The reason is that during his lifetime, there was always hope that he might fulfill the oath. Only upon death does it become certain that he has not fulfilled it. The commentator supports this with the incident of the Treaty of Hudaybiyah. The Prophet had told the Companions that they would circumambulate the Kaaba; when they returned without doing so, Umar objected. The Prophet clarified that he had only promised it would happen sometime, not necessarily that year. The hadith is cited from Bukhari. The commentator uses this to argue that an oath to perform an act in the future is only broken when hope of fulfillment expires, i.e., at death. Therefore, the oath-breaker is declared at the last part of life.

Key Terms
حنث (hanath): Breaking a serious oath, incurring liability for kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the moment he decides not to go
B) At the last part of his life, i.e., at death
C) After a year has passed without going
D) Never, because he intended to go

Key Takeaway
An oath without a time limit is only broken at death because hope of fulfillment persists throughout life.

The Judge's Participation in Community Rituals
States the permissibility of judge attending funerals and visiting sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge attending funerals and visiting the sick, cite the hadith proof, and explain why the command indicates sunnah rather than obligation in this context.

Core Idea
A judge may attend funerals and visit the sick; it is sunnah, not obligatory, and does not risk bribery.

While judges must maintain impartiality, they are also members of the community. This passage addresses whether a judge may participate in common social and religious duties like attending funerals and visiting the sick. The Hanafi school permits and recommends these acts, provided they do not involve favouritism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
The text states a judge attends funerals (yashhad al-janazah) and visits the sick (ya'ud al-marid). The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'We were commanded to visit the sick and follow the funeral' (Bukhari and Muslim) is cited as the proof.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The command (amr) generally indicates obligation in Hanafi usul, but contextual evidence (absence of bribery risk, general human right) reduces it to recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some earlier scholars held judges should avoid all social interactions, but the Hanafi majority allows it.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that it is mustahabb for the judge to do so.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about a judge's personal conduct. It states that a judge may attend funerals and visit the sick. The author clarifies that these acts are free from suspicion of bribery, as they are universal human rights and religious duties. The proof is the hadith 'We were commanded to visit the sick and follow the funeral' (from Bukhari and Muslim). In the Hanafi school, these acts are considered sunnah muakkadah for a judge, as the command indicates recommendation, not obligation in this context.

يعود المريض (ya'ud al-marid): To visit a sick person

When Duress Makes the Haram Permissible: Eating Forbidden Food Under Threat of Death
Matn and sharh on the limits of ikrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for permissible consumption of haram under coercion and apply it to scenarios of varying threat levels.

Core Idea
Only threat of death or limb loss permits the forbidden; lesser threats do not.

This passage from the Book of Coercion (Kitab al-Ikrah) lays down the Hanafi ruling on a critical question: when may a Muslim consume carrion, wine, or other prohibited substances? The answer hinges on the severity of the threat. The Hanafi school holds that only the threat of death or amputation of a limb creates a necessity that transforms the ruling from prohibition to obligation. This lesson unpacks the conditions and proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is being coerced to eat carrion or drink wine. The ruling: under threat of death or limb loss, it becomes permissible and even obligatory (wajib) to consume.
The text uses 'وسعه' (permissible) but later clarifies that refusing is sinful.
2
Analyze the Condition (Shart)
The key condition is the severity of the threat. Only a threat of death or loss of a limb makes haram permissible. Threats of beating, imprisonment, or lesser harm are insufficient.
The Urdu commentary explicitly states: 'ہاں اقتل کرنے کی دھمکی ہو یا کسی عضو کو کاٹ لینے کی دھمکی ہو تب گنجائش ہے'.
3
Locate the Quranic Evidence
The proofs cited are Quran 2:173 (permission for the compelled), 5:3 (clarification of necessity), and 2:195 (prohibition of self-destruction).
These are naqli (textual) proofs of qat'i thubut.
4
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Verse 2:173 contains an exception clause (فمن اضطر) that lifts sin under duress. Verse 2:195 commands 'do not throw yourselves into destruction', making it a sin to refuse and cause one's own death or loss of limb.
The imperative in 2:195 indicates obligation to avoid destruction, thus compelling consumption.
5
Note the Consequence of Refusal
If the coerced person refuses to eat and is killed or maimed, he is sinful (آثم). The matn states: 'فان صبر حتى اوقعوا به ولم يأكل فهو آثم'.
This underscores that preservation of life takes precedence over avoiding the haram under severe threat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاكراه نفسه او على عضو من اعضائه فاذا خاف ذلك وسعه ان يقدم على ما أكره عليه ولا يسعه ان يصبر على ما توعد به [۲۹۷۰](6) فان صبر حتى اوقعوا به ولم يأكل فهو آثم .
دی گئی تو اس سے ان چیزوں کے کھانے کی گنجائش نہیں ہوگی۔ ہاں اقتل کرنے کی دھمکی ہو یا کسی عضو کو کاٹ لینے کی دھمکی ہو اور ظن غالب ہو کہ ایسا کر ہی ڈالے گا تب اس کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ مردار کھالے یا شراب پی لے۔ اب اس کے لئے اپنی جان دینا یا عضو کٹوانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ان چیزوں کی حرمت شدیدہ ہے اس لئے شدید دھمکی ہو تب ہی حلال ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ آیت میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے۔ انما حرم عليكم الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير وما اهل به لغير الله فمن اضطر غير باغ ولا عاد فلا اثم عليه ان الله غفور رحيم (الف) ( آیت ۱۷۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ضرورت سے زیادہ نہ کھائے۔ اور مجبوری کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ کھانے کی کوئی چیز نہ ہو اور بھوک سے جان کا خطرہ لاحق ہو گیا ہو تب کھانے کی گنجائش ہے (۲) دوسری آیت میں اس کی وضاحت ہے۔ حرمت عليكم الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير ... فمن اضطر في مخمصة غير متجانف لاثم فان الله غفور رحيم (ب)( آیت ۳ ، سورة المائدة ۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مخمصہ میں ہو یعنی پیٹ اتنا خالی ہو کہ جان جانے کا خطرہ ہو تب جائز ہے۔ اس حال میں بھی یہ احتیاط ضروری ہے کہ ضرورت سے زیادہ کھا کر گناہ کی طرف مائل نہ ہو۔ اس لئے جان جانے کا یا عضو جانے کا خطرہ ہو تب کھانے کی گنجائش ہے۔ فیتقدم : اقدام کرے، اس کام کو کر لے، توعد : وعد سے مشتق ہے، دھمکی دے۔
(۲۹۷۰) (6) پس اگر صبر کرے یہاں تک کہ کر گزرے اس کے ساتھ پھر بھی نہ کھائے تو وہ گنہ گار ہوگا۔ قتل کرنے کی یا عضو کاٹنے کی دھمکی دی پھر بھی اس نے نہ مردار کھایا نہ شراب پیا۔ آخر مجبور کرنے والے نے قتل کر دیا یا عضو کاٹ دیا تو نہ کھانے والا گنہگار ہوگا۔
اوپر کی آیت میں ہے کہ فلا اسم علیہ، کہ ایسی صورت میں مردار کھا لیا یا شراب پی لی تو اس پر گناہ نہیں ہے تو گویا کہ وہ چیز اس کے لئے حلال ہو گئی۔ اب حلال چیز نہ کھائے اور جان دیدے یا عضو کٹوادے تو اس کے لئے اچھا نہیں ہے۔ بلا وجہ جان دینے یا عضو کٹوانے سے گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اس لئے صبر کرنے کی گنجائش نہیں کھا لینا ضروری ہے۔ گناہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ وانفقوا في سبيل الله ولا تلقوا بايديكم الى التهلكة (ج) ( آیت ۱۹۵ ، سورة البقرة ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جان کر اپنے آپ کو ہلاکت میں نہ ڈالو۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حلال چیز کو نہ کھا کر اپنی جان دینا یا عضو کٹوانا گناہ کا کام ہے۔ اور قتل کی دھمکی کی وجہ سے یہ حرام چیزیں اس کے لئے حلال ہوگئی تھیں۔ اوقعوا : وقع سے مشتق ہے، اس میں واقع کر دیا، اس کام کو کر دیا جس کی دھمکی دیا کرتا تھا، آنم : گنہگار۔
حاشیہ : (الف) تم پر حرام کیا گیا ہے مردار اور خون اور سور کا گوشت اور جس پر غیر اللہ کا نام لیا گیا ہو۔ پس جو مجبور ہو گیا تو لذت تلاش کرنے والا نہ ہو اور نہ حد سے زیادہ کھانے والا ہو تو اس پر کوئی گناہ نہیں ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ معاف کرنے والے ہیں (ب) تم پر حرام کیا گیا ہے مردہ ، خون اور سور کا گوشت. پس مخمصے میں مجبور ہو جائے تو گناہ کی طرف مائل ہونے والا نہ ہو تو اللہ معاف کرنے والا ہے (ج) اللہ کے راستے میں خرچ کرو اور اپنے ہاتھوں کو ہلاکت میں نہ ڈالو۔
Book of Compulsion: [If the threat is against] himself or a limb of his limbs, so if he fears that, it is permissible for him to proceed with what he is coerced to do, and it is not permissible for him to be patient regarding what he is threatened with. So if he is patient until they carry it out on him and he does not eat, then he is sinful. [Urdu commentary: If the threat is of imprisonment or beating, then there is no permission to eat these things. However, if the threat is of killing or cutting a limb, and there is a strong belief that the threatener will do so, then it is permissible for him to eat carrion or drink wine. Now, it is not permissible for him to sacrifice his life or limb. Since these things are severely prohibited, only a severe threat makes them permissible. This is indicated by the verse: 'He has only forbidden to you dead animals, blood, the flesh of swine, and that which has been dedicated to other than Allah. But whoever is forced [by necessity], neither desiring it nor exceeding the limit, there is no sin upon him. Indeed, Allah is Forgiving and Merciful' (2:173). The verse explains necessity as having no food and fear of death from hunger. Another verse (5:3) clarifies: 'Forbidden to you are dead animals, blood, the flesh of swine... But whoever is forced by severe hunger with no inclination to sin, then indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' This means when the stomach is empty with danger of death, it is permissible. Still, caution is needed not to exceed necessity. So when there is fear of death or loss of limb, eating is permissible. Then the matn repeats: So if he is patient until they carry out the threat and he does not eat, he is sinful. The earlier verse shows no sin if he eats, meaning the food becomes lawful. Now if he does not eat and gives his life or limb, it is not good; he becomes sinful. The proof is the verse (2:195): 'And spend in the way of Allah and do not throw yourselves with your own hands into destruction.' This shows that not eating the lawful food and causing death or loss of limb is sinful. Because the threat of death made these forbidden things lawful for him. Footnote: translations of the verses.]
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a matn and its sharh (commentary) on the ruling of ikrah (coercion) regarding eating forbidden foods. The Hanafi position is that when a person is threatened with death or loss of a limb, it becomes permissible for him to consume carrion or wine, and indeed it is obligatory for him to do so to preserve his life. The text says 'it is not permissible for him to be patient'—meaning he cannot voluntarily endure the threat and refuse to eat, as that would lead to his destruction, which is sinful. The proof is from Quran 2:173 and 5:3, which permit forbidden foods under necessity, and 2:195 which prohibits self-destruction. The commentary explains that only a severe threat (death or limb loss) makes the forbidden permissible; lesser threats like imprisonment or beating do not. The emphasis is on the obligation to preserve life, and the sin of not doing so.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion or compulsion by threat of harm to self or limb.
مخمصة (makhmasa): Severe hunger that poses a risk to life.
توعد (taw'ud): Threat (of harm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of a person who is threatened with death if he does not eat carrion, but he refuses and is killed?
A) He is a martyr because he chose death over sin.
B) He is sinful because he caused his own destruction.
C) His action is permissible but not recommended.
D) He has no sin because he was coerced.

Key Takeaway
Consuming haram under threat of death or limb loss is not only permissible but obligatory in the Hanafi school, to preserve life.

Ruling on Being Forced to Utter Kufr or Insult the Prophet
Hanafi ruling with proof on duress and kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uttering kufr under duress, identify the conditions for the dispensation (rukhsah), and evaluate the role of intent as proven by Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Under threat of death or limb loss, uttering kufr is permitted if the heart remains firm in faith.

In this passage, the author explains a severe test of faith: being forced to utter kufr or insult the Prophet. The Hanafi ruling is nuanced—not every threat qualifies as legal duress (ikrah). We will examine the proofs from Quran 16:106 and the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir, and see why the heart's condition is decisive. This lesson equips you to distinguish true apostasy from a dispensation granted under coercion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is uttering kufr or insulting the Prophet under duress. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (rukhsah) only when the threat is to life or limb.
2
Determine what constitutes ikrah
The text clarifies that imprisonment, confinement, or beating does NOT constitute ikrah for this grave matter. Only a threat of death or loss of a limb qualifies.
This strict threshold shows the school’s prioritization of preserving faith.
3
Locate the primary proof
The author cites Quran 16:106, which explicitly excepts those coerced while their heart is firm in faith from the punishment of apostasy.
Verse: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his belief, except for one who is forced while his heart is reassured in faith...'
4
Examine the supplementary proof
The hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir provides a practical example: when forced to curse the Prophet under threat of death, he was told by the Prophet that he may do so again if coerced, as long as his heart was firm.
This hadith is recorded in Mustadrak al-Hakim and is a key evidence for the Hanafi position.
5
Note the condition and consequence
The dispensation depends on the heart remaining 'mutma'in bil iman' (reassured in faith). If the heart acquiesces to disbelief, faith is lost and the person becomes an apostate.
Thus, the outward utterance does not affect faith; inward conviction is what matters.

2971) And if he is coerced to commit kufr against Allah or to insult the Prophet (peace be upon him) by imprisonment, confinement, or beating, that is not considered coercion until he is coerced by a matter from which he fears for himself or a limb. (7) If he is coerced to commit kufr against Allah or to curse the Prophet by imprisonment, confinement, or beating, that is not ikrah until he is coerced by a threat such that he fears for his life or a limb. So when there is such fear, it is permissible for him to utter what he is commanded, and to use tawriyah (mental reservation). This matter is more severe than the previous one. The previous matter involved eating forbidden things; this one involves abandoning faith. The coercer demands kufr or insulting the Prophet. Therefore, beating or imprisonment is not considered ikrah. Only threat of death or limb loss constitutes ikrah. In such a case, he is permitted to utter the word of kufr with his tongue, while his heart remains full of faith. If he commits kufr in his heart or insults the Prophet while his heart is full of faith? Actually, if he commits kufr in his heart or insults the Prophet (even if verbally), then his faith leaves. Proof is the verse: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his belief, except for one who is forced while his heart is reassured in faith, but whoever opens his breast to disbelief, upon them is wrath from Allah and for them is a great punishment' (16:106). And the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir: the polytheists captured him and forced him to curse the Prophet and speak well of their gods. When he came to the Prophet, he asked how he found his heart. He said reassured in faith. The Prophet said: 'If they return, return [to that].' Footnote: translation of verse and hadith.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on being forced to utter kufr or insult the Prophet. The Hanafi position is that mere threats of imprisonment, confinement, or beating do not constitute ikrah (legal duress) in such cases. Only a threat to life or limb qualifies. When such a severe threat exists, the person is permitted to verbally utter the required words while maintaining inward faith. He may use tawriyah (mental reservation). The proof is Quran 16:106, which explicitly states that one who is coerced while heart is steadfast in faith bears no sin. Additionally, the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir provides precedence: when forced to curse the Prophet under threat of death, he was told by the Prophet that he could do so again if coerced, as long as his heart was firm in faith. The commentary emphasizes that this is a dispensation (rukhsah) and not a license to genuinely apostatize. If the heart accepts disbelief, faith is lost.

Key Terms
توریة (tawriyah): Mental reservation; uttering a statement that is technically true or ambiguous while intending a different meaning.
إكراه (ikrah): Legal duress that makes something permissible; here specifically threat of death or limb loss for kufr.
قلبه مطمئن بالايمان (qalbuhu mutma'in bil iman): Heart is at peace with faith, meaning internal conviction remains unchanged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Threat of a fine
C) Threat of amputation of a hand
D) Threat of public humiliation

Key Takeaway
Uttering kufr under duress is permissible in Hanafi fiqh only when the threat is to life or limb and the heart remains firm in faith; otherwise, the person must refuse.

Ruling on Uttering Kufr Under Duress
Ruling on uttering kufr under duress with tawriya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uttering kufr under duress and identify the conditions that make it permissible.

Core Idea
Uttering kufr under duress is permissible if the heart remains firm in faith, but patience is superior.

This lesson examines the ruling regarding a person who is forced to utter words of disbelief under threat of death or severe harm. The Hanafi school, based on the Quranic exception, permits such utterance provided the heart remains tranquil in faith. The text also highlights the virtue of patience and steadfastness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the duress scenario
Determine what action is under consideration: uttering words of kufr under coercion that threatens life or limb.
2
State the basic ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that such utterance is mubah (permissible) if the heart remains firm in faith, based on the Quranic exception.
The ruling is not wajib; it is a concession.
3
Identify the essential condition
The heart must be mutma'in bil-iman (tranquil in faith). Outward utterance alone does not affect faith as long as the heart rejects the disbelief.
This condition is derived from the verse: 'illa man ukriha wa qalbuhu mutma'inun bil-iman'.
4
Note the recommendation of tawriya
Although permissible, it is recommended to use tawriya (equivocation) to avoid uttering the literal words of kufr. This reduces the concession.
Tawriya allows the speaker to intend a different meaning than what the oppressor understands.
5
Compare with the alternative of patience
If one patiently bears torture and death without uttering kufr, he receives great reward. This is superior to using the concession.
The hadith of Khabbab illustrates the reward of steadfastness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His limbs: If he fears for that, it is permissible for him to show what they command him and to use tawriya. [2972](8) Then if he shows that and his heart is tranquil with faith, there is no sin on him. And if he is patient until he is killed and does not show kufr, he is rewarded. [1973?](9) Then if he shows this and his heart is tranquil with faith, there is no sin on him. And if he is patient until he is killed and does not show kufr, he will get reward. If his heart is full of faith and he utters kufr out of fear, there will be no sin. The verse has passed and the hadith too that the heart is full of faith; the Prophet said: if such a situation comes again, do the same again, i.e. utter kufr. Since it is not halal, if he is killed, he will get reward. (2) There is proof of this in the hadith: From Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: We complained to the Messenger of Allah while he was reclining on his cloak in the shade of the Ka'bah, and we said: Will you not seek victory for us? Will you not pray for us? He said: There were before you a man who would be taken, and a pit would be dug for him and he would be placed in it, then a saw would be brought and placed on his head and he would be split into two, and he would be combed with iron combs that would separate his flesh and bones, and that would not turn him away from his religion. (Bukhari, Book of testing...) In this hadith, a saw was run over his head yet he did not abandon faith. And the Prophet praised him. From this it is understood that if one does not utter kufr and gives his life, he will get reward.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on uttering kufr under duress. The text begins by stating that if a person fears harm to his limbs, he may outwardly comply with what he is commanded, but he should use tawriya (equivocation) to avoid actually uttering kufr. The ruling is that if he does utter kufr while his heart is firm in faith, there is no sin on him, based on the Quranic verse (16:106). However, if he patiently endures and is killed without uttering kufr, he is rewarded. The commentary elaborates that uttering kufr becomes permissible only out of necessity, but it is not absolutely permissible; therefore tawriya is recommended. The hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt is cited to show the virtue of patience in the face of torture. The Hanafi position is that the allowance is only for preservation of life, and the reward for patience is greater.

Key Terms
توریہ (tawriya): To use an ambiguous expression that the listener understands in a certain way while the speaker intends a different meaning.
مطمئن بالايمان (mutma'in bil-iman): Heart tranquil and settled in faith, not shaken by outward utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram and he must accept death.
B) He may utter it with tawriya and there is no sin.
C) It is wajib to utter it.
D) He becomes an apostate.

Key Takeaway
Uttering kufr under duress is excused if the heart is firm in faith, but tawriya is recommended and patience earns greater reward.
