Evidence for the Ruling and the Concept of Tawriya
Evidence from Quran and Sunnah for duress ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the Quranic verse and hadith that support the Hanafi ruling on duress, and explain the legal concept of tawriya.

Core Idea
The Quranic exception (16:106) permits outward kufr under duress, and tawriya allows the believer to comply without actual disbelief.

This lesson delves into the primary evidence for the Hanafi position: the Quranic verse 'except one who is forced while his heart is secure in faith' and the hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt. It also explains tawriya as a means to avoid literal kufr, and how the Hanafi school uses it to preserve both life and faith.

Guided Path
1
Recite and analyze Quran 16:106
Read the verse and identify the exception: 'illa man ukriha wa qalbuhu mutma'inun bil-iman'. Note that the verse condemns those who voluntarily disbelieve after faith.
2
Identify the exception clause as the proof
Understand that the exception (istithna) indicates that forced utterance with inner faith does not incur sin. This is the primary textual evidence for the Hanafi ruling.
The exception qualifies the general prohibition of kufr.
3
Examine the hadith of Khabbab and its implication
The hadith describes companions who endured torture without renouncing Islam. The Prophet praised their steadfastness. This hadith shows the superiority of patience, but does not negate the concession.
The hadith is used to encourage patience, not to forbid the concession.
4
Define tawriya and its application in duress
Tawriya is a verbal stratagem where the speaker uses an ambiguous expression that can be interpreted differently than what the oppressor intends.
The Hanafi school recommends tawriya to minimize the apparent kufr while preserving the literal intent of protecting faith.
5
Note the difference between outward action and inner faith
The ruling highlights that outward utterances under duress do not affect the essence of faith as long as the heart remains certain.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position on the integrity of iman.

His limbs: If he fears for that, it is permissible for him to show what they command him and to use tawriya. [2972](8) Then if he shows that and his heart is tranquil with faith, there is no sin on him. And if he is patient until he is killed and does not show kufr, he is rewarded. [1973?](9) Then if he shows this and his heart is tranquil with faith, there is no sin on him. And if he is patient until he is killed and does not show kufr, he will get reward. If his heart is full of faith and he utters kufr out of fear, there will be no sin. The verse has passed and the hadith too that the heart is full of faith; the Prophet said: if such a situation comes again, do the same again, i.e. utter kufr. And in the verse: except those who are forced and their hearts are tranquil with faith. From this it is understood that there is no sin. And if he does not utter kufr and is killed, he will get reward, he will not be sinful. (1) Even with this threat, uttering kufr is not made halal; that is why he said: use tawriya. Since it is not halal, if he is killed, he will get reward. (2) There is proof of this in the hadith: From Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: We complained to the Messenger of Allah while he was reclining on his cloak in the shade of the Ka'bah, and we said: Will you not seek victory for us? Will you not pray for us? He said: There were before you a man who would be taken, and a pit would be dug for him and he would be placed in it, then a saw would be brought and placed on his head and he would be split into two, and he would be combed with iron combs that would separate his flesh and bones, and that would not turn him away from his religion. (Bukhari, Book of testing...) In this hadith, a saw was run over his head yet he did not abandon faith. And the Prophet praised him. From this it is understood that if one does not utter kufr and gives his life, he will get reward.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on uttering kufr under duress. The text begins by stating that if a person fears harm to his limbs, he may outwardly comply with what he is commanded, but he should use tawriya (equivocation) to avoid actually uttering kufr. The ruling is that if he does utter kufr while his heart is firm in faith, there is no sin on him, based on the Quranic verse (16:106). However, if he patiently endures and is killed without uttering kufr, he is rewarded. The commentary elaborates that uttering kufr becomes permissible only out of necessity, but it is not absolutely permissible; therefore tawriya is recommended. The hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt is cited to show the virtue of patience in the face of torture. The Hanafi position is that the allowance is only for preservation of life, and the reward for patience is greater.

Key Terms
توریہ (tawriya): To use an ambiguous expression that the listener understands in a certain way while the speaker intends a different meaning.
مطمئن بالايمان (mutma'in bil-iman): Heart tranquil and settled in faith, not shaken by outward utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Quranic exception and prophetic practice confirm that outward kufr under duress is excused, and tawriya is a legitimate legal stratagem.

Calling the Enemy to Islam Before Combat
Ruling with proof on da'wah before combat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on da'wah before combat, derive the ruling from the hadith proofs, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Before the sword, the call — da'wah is wajib before combat in Hanafi siyar.

The purpose of jihad is to open hearts to Islam, not to shed blood. This passage lays out the prophetic protocol: invite the enemy to Islam, offer jizyah if they refuse, and only fight as a last resort. We will examine the proofs and the Hanafi position on this foundational rule of Islamic warfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific action being ruled upon? The passage rules on the obligation of da'wah (invitation to Islam) before initiating combat against non-Muslims in dar al-harb.
The ruling level is wajib, not fard, because the proofs are from ahad hadith (zanni thubut).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary proofs cited: the hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah (three options: Islam, jizyah, war) and the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight the people until they say La ilaha illallah'.
Both hadith are classified as Sunnah ahad (zanni thubut) but are considered reliable in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each dalil indicate obligation? The imperative 'fad'uhum' (invite them) in the first hadith indicates obligation; the sequential nature shows fighting is contingent on rejection. The phrase 'hata yaqulu' (until they say) implies fighting stops upon conversion.
Hanafi usul holds al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarina (context) to the contrary.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require da'wah if the enemy has already been reached by the message of Islam. The Hanafi view insists on da'wah regardless of prior exposure.
This ikhtilaf stems from different understandings of the prophetic practice and the basis of obligation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) because the hadith of Buraydah explicitly commands da'wah without exception. The later Hanafi masters including Al-Marghinani confirm this.
The ruling is from zahir al-riwayah, the core corpus of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[۲۹۸۴] (۵) واذا دخل المسلمون دار الحرب فحاصروا مدينة او حصنا دعوهم الى
تفرغانه في افواه القوم ثم ترجعان فتملآنها ثم تجيئان فتفرغانه في افواه القوم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب غز والنساء وقتالهن مع الرجال، ص ۴۰۳، نمبر ۲۸۸۰ / مسلم شریف، باب غزوۃ النساء مع الرجال، ص ۱۱۶، نمبر ۱۸۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنگ احد میں حضرت عائشہ اور ام سلیم جہاد میں شریک ہوئیں اور صحابہ کی تیمارداری کی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہنگامی حالات میں عورتوں پر بھی جہاد فرض ہو جاتا ہے۔

صلى الله
حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال ما قاتل رسول الله لا لا لا له قوما حتى دعاهم ( ب ) (مستدرک حاکم، کتاب الایمان، ج اول، ص ۶۱ نمبر ۳۷ / مسند احمد ، باب مسند ابن عباس ، ج اول ص ۱۳۹۰ نمبر ۲۱۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ کی ہمیشہ یہ عادت رہی ہے کہ قتال سے پہلے ان کو اسلام کی دعوت دیتے تھے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں تفصیل ہے جس کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن سليمان بن بريده عن ابيه قال كان رسول الله الا الله اذا امر اميرا على جيش ... واذا لقيت عدوك من المشركين فادعهم الى ثلاث خصال او خلال فايتهن ما اجابوك فاقبل منهم وكف عنهم ثم ادعهم الى الاسلام فان اجابوك فاقبل منهم وكف عنهم... فان هم ابوا فسلهم الجزية فان هم اجابوك فاقبل منهم وكف عنهم، فان هم ابوا فاستعن بالله وقاتلهم (ج) (مسلم شریف ، باب تامیر الامام الامراء علی البحوث و وصیتة اياهم بآداب الغزو وغيرها، ج۲، ص۸۲ نمبر ۳۱ ۷ ارابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی دعاء المشرکین میں ۱۳۶۱، نمبر ۲۶۱۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ پہلے کفار کو اسلام کی دعوت دو۔ نہ مانے تب جزیہ کی پیشکش کرو ۔ اس کو نہ مانے تب قتال کرو۔ اسلام قبول کرلے تو قتال سے رک جائے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ عن انس بن مالك قال قال رسول الله امرت ان اقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا اله الا الله. فاذا قالوها وصلوا صلاتنا واستقبلوا قبلتنا وذبحوا ذبيحتنا
حاشیہ: (الف) جنگ احد کے دن لوگ شکست کھا کر حضور سے پیچھے پیچھے رہ گئے تو حضرت عائشہ اور ام سلیم کو دیکھا کہ وہ کپڑا چڑھائی ہوئی تھیں اور مشکیزے سے زخمیوں کو پانی ڈال رہی تھیں۔ لوگوں نے کہا مشکیزہ اپنے کندھوں پر لارہی تھیں پھر قوم کے منہ میں ڈالتی تھیں۔ پھر واپس بھر کر لاتی تھیں اور قوم کے منہ میں ڈالتی تھیں (ب) حضور نے اسلام کی دعوت دیئے بغیر کسی قوم سے جنگ نہیں کی (ج) آپ جب کسی کو شکر پر امیر بناتے تو فرماتے جب تم مشرک دشمنوں سے مقابلے کے لئے آؤ تو ان کو تین باتوں کی طرف بلاؤ۔ جس بات کو بھی پسند کر لے تو ان سے قبول کر لو۔ اور ان سے جنگ روک لو۔ پھر ان کو اسلام لانے کی دعوت دو پس اگر اس کو پسند کر لے تو ان سے قبول کر لو اور جنگ روک دو۔ اور اگر انکار کر دے تو ان سے جزیہ مانگو، پس اگر اس کو پسند کرے تو ان سے قبول کر لو اور جنگ روک دو۔ اور اگر اس سے بھی انکار کر دے تو اللہ سے مدد مانگو اور ان سے قتال کرو۔
[2984] (5) And when the Muslims enter the Abode of War and besiege a city or a fort, they should call them to... [footnote: they used to fill water skins and pour water into the mouths of the people, then return and fill them and come and pour into their mouths] (a) (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on Ghazwah women and their fighting with men, p. 403, no. 2880 / Sahih Muslim, chapter on women's participation in jihad, p. 116, no. 1811) In this hadith, that in the Battle of Uhud, Aisha and Umm Sulaym participated in jihad and tended to the Companions. From this it is known that in emergency situations, jihad becomes obligatory upon women as well. [2983] (5) If Muslims enter the Abode of War and besiege a city or fort, they should invite them to Islam. Then if they accept, they should refrain from killing them. The purpose of fighting against disbelievers is to make them Muslims. Therefore if they become Muslims before fighting, what need is there for fighting? Hence before starting war, they should invite them to embrace Islam. Hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah never fought a people without inviting them (b) (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab al-Iman, vol. 1, p. 61, no. 37 / Musnad Ahmad, Musnad Ibn Abbas, vol. 1, p. 1390, no. 2106). From this hadith it is known that his constant practice was to invite them to Islam before fighting. (2) Another hadith with details: Sulayman ibn Buraydah from his father said: The Messenger of Allah, when he appointed a commander over an army... and when you meet your enemy from the polytheists, invite them to three things or qualities; whichever they respond to, accept from them and refrain from them. Then invite them to Islam; if they respond, accept from them and refrain from them... if they refuse, demand jizyah from them; if they respond, accept from them and refrain from them; if they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them (c) (Sahih Muslim, chapter on the Imam appointing commanders over expeditions and his advice to them regarding the etiquette of warfare, etc., vol. 2, p. 82, no. 317 / Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on inviting the polytheists, p. 1361, no. 2612). In this hadith also, first invite the disbelievers to Islam. If they don't accept, then offer jizyah. If they don't accept that, then fight. If they accept Islam, then stop fighting. Also evidence is the hadith: Anas ibn Malik said: The Messenger of Allah said: I have been commanded to fight the people until they say 'La ilaha illallah'. So when they say it, pray our prayer, face our qiblah, and slaughter our slaughter. Footnote: (a) On the day of Uhud, the people were defeated and remained behind the Prophet, so Aisha and Umm Sulaym were seen with their clothes lifted, pouring water from water skins onto the wounded. The people said: They were carrying water skins on their shoulders, then they poured into the mouths of the people, then returned and filled them and came and poured into their mouths. (b) The Prophet never fought any people without inviting them to Islam. (c) When he appointed a commander over an army, he would say: When you come before your polytheist enemies, invite them to three things. Whatever they agree to, accept from them and stop fighting. Then invite them to Islam; if they accept, accept from them and stop fighting. If they refuse, demand jizyah; if they accept, accept from them and stop fighting. If they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation to invite the enemy to Islam before initiating combat. The commentator explains that the purpose of jihad is da'wah (invitation to Islam), not mere killing. Therefore, before any military action, Muslims must invite the besieged people to embrace Islam. If they accept, fighting becomes impermissible. The proof is derived from multiple hadith: (1) Ibn Abbas reports the Prophet never fought without prior invitation. (2) The detailed hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah outlines three sequential options: Islam, jizyah, then war. (3) The famous hadith 'I have been commanded to fight the people until they say La ilaha illallah' indicates that upon utterance of the shahada, fighting ceases. A footnote also notes that in emergencies (like the Battle of Uhud), women's participation in jihad becomes obligatory, as Aisha and Umm Sulaym tended the wounded. This shows that jihad in defense can be fard ayn on women when needed.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): A territory under non-Muslim rule where the laws of Islam are not enforced, and where Muslims are permitted to conduct jihad.
دعوة (da'wah): Invitation to embrace Islam, given before initiating combat against non-Muslims.
جهاد (jihad): Warfare against non-Muslims to establish the supremacy of Islam, with the ultimate aim of da'wah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi siyar, da'wah before combat is wajib; the sequence is invite to Islam, then jizyah, then war.

Da'wah Before Jihad: The Obligation of Invitation
States ruling on necessity of inviting before fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that inviting non-Muslims to Islam is wajib before initiating hostilities and identify the hadith evidence supporting this.

Core Idea
Before jihad, invitation is obligatory — the Prophet never fought without da'wah.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling of Islamic warfare: that da'wah must precede combat. The passage establishes that fighting those who have never heard the call of Islam is impermissible without first issuing an invitation. We will explore the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the legal reasoning behind this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the legal status of fighting those who have not received da'wah. The passage says it is not permissible until they are invited.
The ruling is a prohibition (haram) of fighting without da'wah; the da'wah itself is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: from Sulayman ibn Burayda commanding invitation, and from Ibn 'Abbas stating the Prophet never fought without inviting.
Both are ahad hadith, but their meaning is clear and supported by the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ادعهم' in the first hadith indicates obligation per the Hanafi principle that al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
No contextual evidence to shift the imperative from obligation to recommendation.
4
Understand the wisdom
The author explains that da'wah clarifies that jihad is for spreading Islam, not for material gain.
This addresses a potential misconception about the motives of jihad.
5
Note the consensus
This ruling is agreed upon across madhhabs (muttafaq alayh).
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded.

ولا يجوز ان يقاتل من لم تبلغه دعوة الاسلام الا بعد ان يدعوهم [2986] (۷) اور نہیں جائز ہے کہ قتال کرے اس سے جس کو اسلام کی دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو مگر یہ کہ اس کو دعوت دے۔ جن کفار کو اسلام کی دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو ان کو دعوت دیئے بغیر قتال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ حضور جب تک دعوت نہ دے لیتے کفار سے قتال شروع نہ کرتے۔ اس لئے قتال سے پہلے دعوت دینا ضروری ہے تا کہ ان کو بھی پتا چل جائے کہ ہم اسلام کو عام کرنے کے لئے جہاد کر رہے ہیں۔ مال لوٹنے اور لوگوں کو غلام باندی بنانے کے لئے جہاد نہیں کر رہے ہیں (۲) او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن سليمان بن بـريـدة عن ابيه ... ثم ادعهم الى الاسلام فان اجابوک فاقبل منهم وكف عنهم (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب تا میر الامام الامراء علی البحوث، ج ۲، ص۸۲ نمبر ۳۱ ۷ ارابوداؤد شریف، باب فی دعاء المشرکین، ص ۱۳۶۱ نمبر۲۶۱۲) (۳) ایک اور حدیث گزری۔ عن ابن عباس قال ما قاتل رسول الله له قوما حتى دعاهم صلى الله عليه (ب) (مستدرک حاکم، کتاب الایمان ، ج اول ص ۶۱ نمبر ۳۷ رمسند احمد، باب مسند عبداللہ ابن عباس ، ج اول ص ۱۳۹۰، نمبر ۲۱۰۶)
It is not permissible to fight one who has not been reached by the call of Islam except after inviting them. [2986] (7) And it is not permissible to fight someone to whom the call of Islam has not reached, unless you give him da'wah. To fight those disbelievers who have not received the call of Islam without giving da'wah is not permissible. The hadith has passed earlier that the Prophet (SAW) would not begin fighting until he gave da'wah. Therefore, giving da'wah before fighting is necessary so that they also know that we are doing jihad to spread Islam, not to loot wealth and enslave people. (2) The hadith has passed earlier from Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father: '...then invite them to Islam; if they accept, accept from them and refrain from them.' (Muslim, Bab Ta'mir al-Imam al-Umara' 'ala al-Bu'uth, vol. 2, p. 82, no. 31; Abu Dawud, Bab Fi Du'a' al-Mushrikin, p. 1361, no. 2612) (3) Another hadith passed: from Ibn 'Abbas (RA) who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (SAW) never fought a people until he invited them.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab al-Iman, vol. 1, p. 61, no. 37; Musnad Ahmad, Bab Musnad 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, vol. 1, p. 1390, no. 2106)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. It states that it is not permissible to initiate combat against any group of disbelievers until they have been invited to accept Islam. The author emphasizes that this is obligatory, not optional. He supports this with two hadith: one from Sulayman ibn Burayda commanding invitation before fighting, and another from Ibn 'Abbas stating that the Prophet never fought without prior invitation. The wisdom given is to clarify that jihad is for the propagation of Islam, not for material gain.

Key Terms
دعوة الاسلام (da'wat al-Islam): The call or invitation to accept Islam as a religion.

C) They must be attacked immediately.
D) They must be warned of military action only.

Key Takeaway
Invitation (da'wah) to Islam is a wajib condition before initiating jihad against those who have not received the message.

Invitation Recommended for Those Already Called
States that inviting those already reached is mustahabb, not wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on re-inviting those who have already received the call to Islam and demonstrate the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
For those already reached by Islam, a second invitation before fighting is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory (wajib).

This lesson addresses a key question in the ethics of da'wah: when is it obligatory to invite before fighting? The Hanafi school distinguishes between those who have never heard the message and those who have. For the latter, a fresh invitation is recommended but not required. The evidence comes from the Prophet's campaign against Banu al-Mustaliq, where he attacked without a new da'wah.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (inviting those already called before fighting) and its hukm: mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
The text explicitly says 'مستحب' and 'واجب نہیں'.
2
Identify the proof
Locate the dalil: the hadith of Banu al-Mustaliq in Sahih al-Bukhari.
The hadith describes a night attack without prior da'wah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's omission of a fresh invitation indicates that for those already reached, it is not compulsory. The absence of a known prior da'wah to Banu al-Mustaliq is understood as the call having reached them earlier.
The attack at night (while they were inattentive) shows they were not given a new warning.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
Some scholars consider it wajib, but the Hanafi position is mustahabb, supported by this practice.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is mustahabb.
This is from zahir al-riwayah.

ويستحب ان يدعو من بلغته الدعوة الى الاسلام ولا يجب ذلك. [2987] (۸) اور مستحب ہے کہ جس کو دعوت پہنچی ہو اس کو بھی دعوت دے اسلام کی لیکن واجب نہیں ہے۔ جن کو اسلام کی دعوت پہنچ چکی ہو مستحب ہے کہ قتال سے پہلے ان کو دوبارہ دعوت دے۔ لیکن چونکہ دعوت پہنچ چکی ہے اس لئے دوبارہ دعوت دینا واجب نہیں ہے، مستحب ہے۔ اوپر کی احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دعوت دے۔ اور ایک اور حدیث میں ہے کہ بنی مصطلق پر رات میں حملہ کیا جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ ان کو قال سے پہلے اسلام کی دعوت نہیں دی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جن کو دعوت پہنچ چکی ہو اس کو دوبارہ دعوت دینا واجب نہیں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ کتبت الى نافع فكتب الى ان النبى الله الله اغار على بني المصطلق وهم غارون وانعامهم تسقى على الماء فقتل مقاتلتهم وسبى ذراريهم واصاب يو منذ جويرية (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من ملک من العرب رقیقا فوهب و جامع وفدی و سبی
And it is recommended that he invite the one to whom the call has reached to Islam, and that is not obligatory. [2987] (8) And it is mustahabb that whoever has been reached by the call, he should also invite him to Islam, but it is not wajib. For those who have already received the call of Islam, it is mustahabb to give them da'wah again before fighting. But because the da'wah has reached, giving da'wah again is not wajib, it is mustahabb. From the hadith above, we know to give da'wah. And in another hadith, it says that the Prophet attacked Banu al-Mustaliq at night, meaning he did not give them da'wah of Islam before fighting. This indicates that for those already reached, giving da'wah again is not wajib. The hadith is: 'I wrote to Nafi', and he wrote to me that the Prophet (SAW) raided Banu al-Mustaliq while they were inattentive and their cattle were watering at the spring; he killed their fighters and captured their children, and on that day he captured Juwayriyyah.' (Bukhari, Bab man malaka min al-'arab raqiqan fawahaba wa jama'a wa fada wa saba)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof distinguishing between those who have never been invited and those who have. For the latter, a repetition of the invitation before fighting is mustahabb (recommended) but not wajib (obligatory). The author uses the incident of Banu al-Mustaliq as evidence: the Prophet attacked them at night without a fresh invitation, implying that their previous exposure to the call sufficed. The ruling applies to those who have already heard the message of Islam.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended action; doing it earns reward, not doing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is mustahabb.
C) It is haram.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
For those already reached by the call of Islam, a renewed invitation before fighting is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory (wajib).

Permissible Siege Tactics When Enemy Refuses
Lists permissible siege tactics with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using siege tactics like mangonels, burning, and flooding when the enemy refuses Islam and jizya, and cite the supporting hadith proofs.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, all necessary force is permissible when the enemy refuses both da'wah and jizya.

This passage outlines the permissible military actions after the enemy rejects the call to Islam and the offer of jizya. It lists several tactics – from mangonels to flooding – and supports each with a specific hadith from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing the Hanafi principle that the end of establishing justice permits the means of force, within the bounds of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using siege tactics such as mangonels, burning, and flooding after the enemy refuses da'wah and jizya. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
The ruling is not obligatory but allowed under necessity.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda commanding to fight. Additional actions are proven by specific ahadith: Ta'if (mangonels), Banu al-Nadir (burning and cutting trees), and Badr (water tactics).
Each tactic has its own evidence from the Prophet's sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'قاتلهم' indicates permissibility. The specific actions are derived from the Prophet's practice (fi'l), which serves as a proof for the permissibility of those tactics.
The command to fight is general; the prophet's actions specify the means.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict cutting trees and burning based on the principle of preserving property. Hanafi differs because the Prophet explicitly did so and the Qur'an (59:5) confirmed it.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate and leads to practical differences.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi; later Hanafi authorities uphold the permissibility based on necessity and the primary texts. The majority of Hanafi fatwa follows this view.
The ruling is well-established within the madhhab.

If they refuse, they seek help from Allah against them and fight them, and they set up mangonels against them, and burn them, and release water upon them, and cut their trees, and destroy their crops. [2988] (9) So if they refuse, then seeking help from Allah, fight them. And set up mangonels on them, and burn them, and release water upon them, and cut their trees, and ruin their fields. If they also refuse to give jizya, then war will be waged against them. There are various forms of war that were prevalent at that time. For example, set up mangonels on them, set their houses on fire, pour hot water on them so that they die or are forced to surrender. Cut their trees. And ruin their fields so that they are compelled. Fight on refusal of jizya; its proof has passed in the hadith above. From Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father: '...if they refuse, then seek help from Allah and fight them.' (Muslim, Bab Ta'mir al-Imam, vol. 2, p. 82, no. 73; Abu Dawud, Bab Fi Du'a' al-Mushrikin, p. 1361, no. 2612) From this hadith, it is known that if they are not ready to give jizya, then take Allah's name and begin fighting. For this, use mangonels or atomic bombs of that time; its proof is this hadith: From Abu 'Ubayd that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) besieged the people of Ta'if and set up mangonels against them for seventeen days. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Qat' al-Shajar, vol. 9, p. 144, no. 18120) From this hadith, it is known to set up mangonels. The hadith on burning is: From Ibn 'Umar (RA) that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) burned the date palms of Banu al-Nadir and cut them, and that was al-Buwaira. Then the verse was revealed: 'Whatever you cut down of [their] palm trees or left standing on their trunks, it was by permission of Allah and so that He might disgrace the defiantly disobedient.' (Surah al-Hashr 59:5; Bukhari, Bab Hadith Bani al-Nadhir, p. 574, no. 4031; Muslim, Bab Jawaz Qat' Ashjar al-Kuffar wa Tahriqiha, vol. 2, p. 85, no. 1746) From this hadith, it is known that the houses of disbelievers can be burned, and their trees can be cut if necessity arises. This hadith also provides evidence for cutting trees and ruining crops. Regarding releasing water upon them or blocking their water, there is this hadith: From 'Ali (RA) who said: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) commanded me to spoil the water of the wells of Badr. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Qat' al-Shajar, vol. 9, p. 125, no. 18123) From this hadith, it is known to block the water of the disbelievers, and if necessary, pour hot water on them so that they flee the battlefield.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with multiple proofs. It details the permissible tactics when disbelievers refuse both Islam and jizya. The author lists: seeking Allah's help, using mangonels, burning, flooding, cutting trees, and destroying crops. Each tactic is supported by a specific hadith: the general command to fight from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda; the use of mangonels from the siege of Ta'if; burning and cutting trees from the incident of Banu al-Nadir; and manipulating water from the Battle of Badr. The commentary emphasizes that these are necessary measures to compel the enemy and that jihad is not for worldly gain but to establish the deen. The phrase 'or atomic bombs of that time' shows that the principle allows modern equivalents.

Key Terms
منجنیق (manjaniq): A siege engine for launching projectiles; in modern context, any heavy weapon like cannon or bomb.
جزیہ (jizya): A tax levied on non-Muslims under Islamic rule in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the enemy refuses Islam and jizya, all necessary force, including mangonels, burning, and flooding, is permissible to compel surrender.

Prohibition of Selling or Stockpiling Spoils Before Division
Ruling with proof on spoils before division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling or stockpiling spoils before division and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Selling or stockpiling spoils before division is haram; only immediate consumption as needed is allowed.

This passage addresses the handling of spoils of war (ghanimah) before official distribution. The matn states a clear prohibition: it is not permissible for soldiers to sell any part of the spoils or to accumulate them as personal property. The commentary expands by defining the boundary between permitted immediate use and prohibited trade or hoarding, and provides three hadith proofs that establish the ruling as a major sin akin to treachery (ghulul).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn explicitly forbids two actions: selling any portion of the spoils before division, and taking them as personal property (tamawwul). The ruling is haram.
The commentary specifies that limited immediate consumption is allowed, but any act of trade or stockpiling with intent of ownership is prohibited.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three hadith: (1) The practice of the Companions at Khaybar taking only what sufficed, (2) the explicit prohibition of purchasing spoils before division by Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, and (3) the severe warning against ghulul (misappropriation).
The primary dalil is the hadith of Abu Sa'id: 'نهى رسول الله عن شراء المغانم حتى تقسم' (He forbade the purchase of spoils until they are divided).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, an explicit prohibition (nahy) directed at an act indicates that the act is haram. The hadith's direct command not to purchase (or sell) before division is clear and definitive in meaning.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) in transmission, which makes it zanni in thubut but qati in dalala as the meaning is unambiguous.
4
Note the exception for immediate need
The commentary clarifies that taking food, fodder, or oil for immediate essential use is permissible because it does not amount to tamawwul (taking as property). Any excess must be returned to the spoils pool.
This exception is derived from the practice of the Companions at Khaybar. It is not a contradiction to the prohibition but a limitation of its scope.

It is not permissible for them to sell any of that or to take it as property (for themselves). ... (Urdu explanation) And it is not permissible to sell any of it or store it. Before the distribution of the spoils, one may use as much as needed, but it is not allowed to sell it or store it for oneself. ... From the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: 'I said: Did you take khums from food in the time of the Messenger of Allah? He said: We acquired food on the day of Khaybar, and a man would come and take an amount sufficient for him and then leave.' ... From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade the purchase of spoils until they are divided.' ... From Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'If you find a man who has misappropriated spoils, burn his goods and beat him.'
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states the basic ruling: It is not permissible for the soldiers to sell any part of the spoils before official division, nor to accumulate it as personal property (tamawwul). The commentary expands by explaining that limited use for immediate need is allowed, but selling or stockpiling is prohibited. The proof is provided through three hadith: (1) The practice of the Companions at Khaybar taking only what sufficed, indicating no hoarding; (2) Explicit prohibition of buying/selling spoils before division; (3) Severe warning against misappropriation (ghulul). Together, these establish that pre-division selling or stocking is haram and considered treachery.

Key Terms
يتمولونه (yatamawwalunahu): To take it as personal property/accumulate it for oneself
الغلول (al-ghulul): Misappropriation of spoils before division

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Selling or stockpiling spoils before division is haram, supported by explicit hadith, with only immediate consumption as needed excepted.

What a Converting Harbi Secures: Movable vs. Immovable
Ruling with proof on what a converting harbi secures and the dispute over land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between movable and immovable property of a converting harbi and explain why land becomes fay' upon conquest according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A harbi's conversion secures his life, young children, and movable property, but his land remains subject to being spoils upon conquest.

When an enemy combatant (harbi) embraces Islam during war, his life and certain properties become inviolable. However, the Hanafi school draws a critical distinction between movable and immovable assets. This lesson unpacks that distinction, explaining what is secured and what becomes fay' (spoils), and examines the proof texts that support the Hanafi position against alternate views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Secured Items
From the matn, list what the converting harbi secures: his life, his young children, and all property in his hand or held in trust by a Muslim or dhimmi.
These are considered under his effective possession or dependency.
2
Identify the Items That Become Fay'
Upon Muslim conquest of the territory, his real estate (land), wife, her pregnancy, and his adult children become spoils (fay').
The commentary explains that these are not under his effective control or dependent status.
3
Understand the Rationale
Young children are dependent on the father; movable property is in his hand; but land is immovable and under the authority of dar al-harb. Adult children and the wife are independent or not under his protection after conversion.
This distinction between movable and immovable is key to the Hanafi ruling.
4
Trace the Dispute
Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that land is also secured because it is property, citing the general hadith 'Whoever says La ilaha illa Allah, his life and property are inviolable.' The Hanafi school responds by qualifying that hadith with the practice of the Prophet in the hadith of Sakhr, where only movable property was returned.
The dispute centers on whether the general hadith applies to land in dar al-harb.
5
Apply the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts Abu Hanifa's view that land becomes fay' because it is not effectively in the convert's possession until conquest. The mufta bihi is that land is not secured.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab.

And whoever among them accepts Islam secures by his Islam his life, his young children, and all property that is in his hand or is a trust in the hand of a Muslim or dhimmi. Then if we overcome the land, his real estate is fay', his wife is fay', her pregnancy is fay', and his adult children are fay'... (Urdu explanation) When a harbi becomes Muslim, his life, movable property, and young children become secure, but his land in dar al-harb is not secure; if Muslims conquer the land, it becomes spoils. His wife (if still a harbiyya) becomes spoils, her pregnancy follows her, and his adult children become spoils. Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i hold that land is also secured, but the Hanafi position is that it becomes fay'.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi position on what a converting harbi secures. The matn states: he secures his life, young children, and property in his possession or trust. But upon conquest, his land, wife, pregnancy, and adult children become fay' (spoils). The commentary explains the rationale: young children are dependent, but land is immovable and subject to the authority of dar al-harb. The passage then records an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Muhammad (and Imam Shafi'i) argue that land should also be secured based on the general hadith that Islam protects life and property. However, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) distinguishes between movable and immovable property; land remains subject to the status of dar al-harb and thus becomes fay' upon conquest. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that land is not secured and becomes spoils, as it is not in the convert's actual possession under Islamic authority.

Key Terms
فىء (fay'): Spoils of war taken from the enemy without active fighting (or land conquered) which becomes public treasury
عقار (aqar): Real estate, immovable property (land, buildings)
احرز (ahraza): To secure, protect, make inviolable

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A converting harbi secures his life, dependents, and movable property, but his land becomes fay' upon conquest according to the Hanafi school.

Reinforcements and Booty: When Do They Share?
Ruling on reinforcements sharing booty before it leaves Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reinforcements sharing booty and explain the basis of the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Reinforcements share booty if they arrive before it is moved to Dar al-Islam, even after battle.

This lesson examines a key rule of Islamic military law (siyar): the entitlement of reinforcements to a share of the booty. The Hanafi school holds that as long as the booty remains in Dar al-Harb, any arriving unit joins the army's entitlement. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts this to those who join before the battle ends. We will analyze the evidence behind each position and see how the Hanafis interpret the prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the fiqh ruling on reinforcements joining before booty is moved to Dar al-Islam? State the hukm level (wajib) and its condition.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
What evidence from the Sahaba supports the Hanafi position? Look at the practice of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, and the incident of Ziyad ibn Labid.
3
Analyze the opposing school's proof
How does Imam al-Shafi'i argue from 'Umar's letter to Sa'd? Identify the operative phrase 'before they divide'.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school reconcile the letter with their position? What is the alternative interpretation of 'tiftaqu'?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا لحقهم المدد فى دار الحرب قبل ان يُخرجوا الغنيمة الى دار الاسلام شاركوهم فيها. مصنف کے عبارت میں یہ ہے کہ مال غنیمت دار الاسلام لانے سے پہلے کوئی جماعت مدد کے لئے لشکر کے ساتھ مل جائے تو ان کو حصہ ملے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد ملے تو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ کتب عمر الى سعد يوم القادسية اني قد بعثت اليك اهل الحجاز واهل الشام فمن ادرک منهم القتال قبل ان يتفقوا فاسهم لهم۔ اس میں جنگ ختم ہونے سے پہلے شریک ہونے والے کو حصہ دلوایا۔
And if reinforcements join them in Dar al-Harb before they take the booty to Dar al-Islam, they share in it. In the author's phrase, if a group joins the army for help before bringing the booty to Dar al-Islam, they will get a share. Imam al-Shafi'i says: if they join after the battle has ended, they do not get a share in the booty. His proof is this athar: 'Umar wrote to Sa'd on the day of Qadisiyyah: I have sent to you the people of Hijaz and the people of Syria, so whoever among them reaches the fighting before they divide, allocate a share for them.' In this, a share was given only to the one who joined before the battle ended.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the book of Siyar. The issue is about reinforcements arriving after the battle but before the booty is taken to Islamic territory. The Hanafi position, based on the actions of Abu Bakr (with Ziyad ibn Labid) and 'Umar (with the people of Kufa and Basra), is that as long as the booty has not been brought to Dar al-Islam, the newcomers share equally. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts sharing to those who join before the battle ends, citing the letter of 'Umar to Sa'd. The Hanafi response is that 'Umar's letter can be interpreted as referring to prevention of discord, and the earlier examples show a different practice. The author follows the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
المدد (al-madad): Reinforcements sent to aid an already-existing army.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Booty seized from the enemy in war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if they join before the battle ends.
B) If they join before the booty is taken to Dar al-Islam.
C) If they join before the booty is distributed.
D) They never get a share.

Key Takeaway
Reinforcements share booty if they arrive before it is taken to Dar al-Islam, based on Sahaba practice; the Shafi'i condition of joining before battle is a valid but non-operative view in the Hanafi school.

Market People Have No Share in Booty
Ruling with proof from athar and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the share of market people in booty, identify the dalil from the athar of 'Umar and the hadith of Salamah, and distinguish the basis of the ruling from that of the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Booty is for fighters, not traders: intention and participation determine entitlement.

This passage addresses a common scenario in military campaigns: merchants who accompany the army for trade, not combat. Are they entitled to a share of the booty? The Hanafi school, citing the practice of 'Umar and a hadith of Salamah, firmly rules that they are not—unless they actually fight. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
Recognize that 'ahl suq al-'askar' refers to merchants who set up shops in the army camp for trade. The ruling is clear: they have no right to booty unless they fight.
The exception 'illa an yuqatilu' is crucial.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage cites two proofs: an athar from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab stating that booty is for those who witness the battle, and the hadith of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' who received a share only after fighting.
These are considered strong proofs in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'man shahida al-waq'ah' indicates that witnessing the battle with the intention to fight is the criterion. Traders are present but lack that intention.
Intention (niyyah) is a key element in determining entitlement.
4
Consider the role of intention
The passage emphasizes that market people's purpose is trade, not fighting. Hence they are not considered participants in the battle.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by intentions.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly gives a share to those who provide services. The Hanafi response is that mere service without fighting does not qualify.
This ikhtilaf arises from different interpretations of 'shuhud' and the weight given to niyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حق لاهل سوق العسكر في الغنيمة الا ان يقاتلوا. لشکر کے بازار والوں کو حق نہیں ہے غنیمت میں مگر یہ کہ وہ بھی قتال کریں۔ ان لوگوں کا مقصد قتال کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ تجارت کرنا ہے۔ اثر میں ہے کہ جو لوگ جنگ میں شریک ہوں ان کو حصہ ملے گا اور یہ لوگ نیت کے اعتبار سے جنگ میں شریک نہیں ہیں۔ اثر میں ہے: كتب عمر بن الخطاب ان الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعة. حدیث میں ہے کہ سلمہ بن اکوع اجیر تھے تو حصہ نہیں دیا لیکن جب قتال کیا تو حضور نے گھوڑے سوار کا حصہ دیا۔
And the people of the army's market have no right in the booty unless they fight. The market people of the army have no right in the booty unless they also fight. These people's purpose is not fighting but trade. There is an athar: 'Whoever participates in the battle gets a share, and these people, by intention, are not participants in the battle.' There is an athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: 'Indeed, the booty is for whoever witnesses the battle.' In a hadith, Salamah ibn al-Akwa' was a hired servant, so no share was given, but when he fought, the Prophet gave him the share of a horseman.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage rules that non-combatant traders accompanying the army for commerce do not get any share of the booty. The proof is the general principle that booty is only for those who actually participate in the fighting (شهد الوقعة). The example of Salamah ibn al-Akwa' shows that even a servant gets a share if he fights. The Hanafi school distinguishes between those who join with the intention of fighting and those who join for trade. The latter have no claim.

Key Terms
أهل سوق العسكر (ahl suq al-'askar): Merchants who set up shops in the army camp for trade, not for fighting.

Key Takeaway
Market people get no booty unless they fight; the Hanafi school emphasizes intention and actual combat as the basis for entitlement.

The Binding Aman of a Free Muslim: Ruling, Proof, and Exceptions
Ruling on validity of aman granted by free Muslim individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aman granted by a free Muslim and explain the proofs and the exception of mafsada.

Core Idea
The aman of any free Muslim (man or woman) is binding on all Muslims; violation is haram unless the imam revokes it for corruption.

In Islamic law, granting aman (safe conduct) to a disbeliever is not only an individual act but creates a collective obligation. This passage establishes that any free Muslim—regardless of gender—can grant aman, and that once granted, no Muslim may harm the recipient. However, if the aman involves public harm, the imam has authority to revoke it. We will explore the ruling, its proofs, and the limits of this authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the act being described: granting aman to a disbeliever or a group. Then state the hukm (ruling): it is valid and binding on all Muslims; breaking it is haram.
The term 'correct' (صح) indicates legal validity.
2
Determine who can grant aman
Note the conditions: the grantor must be a free (hurr) Muslim, man or woman. This excludes slaves and non-Muslims. Also note that the grantee can be a single disbeliever, a group, or the people of a fort or city.
The text explicitly includes women, countering restrictions in other schools.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The passage cites both Quran and hadith. The Quranic reference is to those who break covenants (Surah al-Anfal 8:56). The hadith is: 'The protection of Muslims is one; whoever breaks the protection of a Muslim, upon him is like that.' Identify these as the primary proofs.
Wajh al-dalalah: the hadith explicitly states the unity of Muslim pacts, so any Muslim's aman is binding on all.
4
Analyze the exception (istithna')
The text says 'unless there is corruption in it' (الا ان يكون في ذلك مفسدة). This means if the aman was granted for corrupt purposes (e.g., to spy), the imam may revoke it, but not arbitrarily—only through proper process.
The exception is based on public interest (maslaha).
5
Examine cross-madhhab dispute
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not consider a woman's aman valid. The Hanafi school responds by affirming the generality of the hadith, which does not distinguish gender. Note the practical consequence: a woman's aman is operative in Hanafi fiqh.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the bounds of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا امن رجل حر او امرأة حرَّةً كافرا او جماعة او اهل حصن او مدينة صح امـانهـم ولـم يجز لاحد من المسلمين قتلهم الا ان يكون في ذلك مفسدة. آزاد مرد یا آزاد عورت کافر کو یا جماعت کو یا قلعے والے کو یا شہر والے کو امن دے تو سارے مسلمانوں کی جانب سے امن سمجھا جائے گا۔ اب کسی مسلمان کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اسے قتل کرے۔ ہاں اگر امن دینے میں کوئی خرابی ہو تو امام باضابطہ اس کے امن توڑنے کا اعلان کرے۔ آیت ہے: الذين عاهدت منهم ثم ينقضون عهدهم في كل مرة وهم لا يتقون. حدیث میں ہے: وذمة المسلمين واحدة فمن اخفر مسلما فعليه مثل ذلك.
And if a free man or a free woman grants aman to a disbeliever, or a group, or the people of a fort, or a city, their aman is valid. And it is not permissible for any Muslim to kill them unless there is corruption in it. A free man or free woman gives aman to a disbeliever, a group, the people of a fort, or the people of a city; it will be considered aman from all Muslims. Now it is not permissible for any Muslim to kill him. Yes, if there is some flaw in granting aman, the imam may formally revoke the aman. The verse is: 'Those with whom you have made a covenant, then they break their covenant every time, and they do not fear [Allah].' And in the hadith: 'The protection of the Muslims is one, and whoever breaks the protection of a Muslim, upon him is like that.'
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling on aman (safe conduct) granted by a free Muslim individual. The key points: (1) Aman is binding on all Muslims if granted by a free adult Muslim (man or woman) to any disbeliever or group, whether from a fort or city. (2) No Muslim may kill such a person after aman. (3) The exception is if the aman involves some corruption (mafsada), such as harm to Muslims; then the imam may officially revoke the aman, but not arbitrarily. The proof includes the Quranic prohibition of breaking covenants (Surah al-Anfal, 8:56) and the hadith that Muslims are one in their pacts.

Key Terms
الأمان (al-aman): Safe conduct granted to a disbeliever, guaranteeing protection from harm.
حر (hurr): Free person (not a slave) who is legally capable.
مفسدة (mafsada): Corruption or harm that would result from keeping the aman, e.g., espionage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the caliph's aman.
B) Any free Muslim man or woman's aman.
C) Only the commander of the army's aman.
D) Only a man's aman, not a woman's.

Key Takeaway
A free Muslim's aman (man or woman) is binding on all Muslims; violation is haram, and revocation requires the imam's formal action upon corruption.

Validity of a Slave's Grant of Aman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on slave's ability to give aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's aman and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A Muslim slave's aman is valid, even if he never fought — the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the capacity of a slave to grant aman (safe passage) to enemy combatants. While Abu Hanifa conditioned it on participation in battle, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, held it unconditionally valid based on explicit hadith. We will explore the proofs and understand which position is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine what the slave's aman is: valid (sahih) or invalid? The Sahibayn say sahih unconditionally; Abu Hanifa says sahih only if the slave fought.
2
Map the two positions
Clearly state Abu Hanifa's position (participation required) and the Sahibayn's position (unconditional).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Read the hadith cited: 'The protection of Muslims is one; the lowest of them can grant protection' and the hadith of Ali: 'The slave has no share of spoils except a trifle, but his aman is valid.'
These are dalil naqli from sunnah.
4
Understand the practical difference
If a slave who did not fight gives aman, Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn say valid. The mufta bihi follows Sahibayn.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Confirm the relied-upon view
The commentary indicates Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi because of explicit hadith.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في القتال وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى يصح امانه ۳۰۱۷] اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ یہ غلام جنگ میں شریک تھا اس لئے اس کے امان کو مانا۔ اس لئے جنگ میں شریک ہو تو اس کے امان کو مانا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جنگ میں شریک ہو یا نہ ہو اس کے امان کا اعتبار ہے۔ وہ بھی مسلمان ہے اور مسلمان کے امان کا اعتبار ہے۔ اس لئے غلام کے امان کا اعتبار ہوگا، حدیث گزر چکی، ذمة المسلمين واحدة يسعى بها ادناهم مسلم شريف، باب فضل اللي وداعا لانی فيها با بركت ص ٢٤٠ نمبر ١٣٧ (۲) حدیث میں اس کی صراحت المدينة ہے۔ عن علي بن ابي طالب قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ليس للعبد من الغنيمة شيء إلا الثنى المتاع وأمانه جائز إذا هو أعطى القوم الأمان (الف) (سنن البيهقي، باب امان العبد، ج تاسع ص ١٢٠ نمبر ١٨١٧٢، مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ١٣٤٠ في امان المرأة والملوك، ج سادس، ج ٥١٤، نمبر ٣٣٣٨٣) اس حدیث میں صراحت ہے کہ غلام چاہے جنگ میں شریک نہ ہو اس کے امان کا اعتبار ہے۔ اس لئے غلام کے امان کا اعتبار ہو گا (۳) اوپر حضرت عمر کے اثر میں بھی یہی تھا کہ غلام کے امن کا اعتبار ہے۔
Regarding fighting: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: His aman is valid. [Footnote 3017] And the other view is that this slave participated in the war, so his aman is accepted. Therefore, if he participated in war, his aman will be accepted, otherwise not. The Sahibayn say: Whether he participates in war or not, his aman is considered. He is also a Muslim, and the aman of a Muslim is considered. Therefore, the aman of a slave will be considered. The hadith has passed: 'The protection of Muslims is one; the lowest of them can grant protection.' (Muslim, chapter on virtue of...). In the hadith, there is clarity about it: From Ali ibn Abi Talib: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The slave has no share of the spoils except a trifle of goods, but his aman is valid if he gives aman to a people.' (Al-Bayhaqi, Sunan, chapter on aman of slave, vol. 9 p. 120 no. 18172; Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf, 1340 in aman of woman and slaves, vol.6 p.514 no.33383). This hadith explicitly states that even if the slave did not participate in war, his aman is valid. Therefore, the aman of a slave will be considered. (3) Also in the athar of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) above, it was that the aman of a slave is valid.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage begins with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a slave's grant of aman (security) to enemy combatants. The base matn states the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) that a slave's aman is valid. The commentary first presents what appears to be Abu Hanifa's view: that the slave's aman is accepted only if he participated in the actual fighting. The Sahibayn, however, hold that participation is not a condition; the slave is a Muslim, and the general principle is that any Muslim can grant aman, as established by the hadith 'The protection of Muslims is one; the lowest of them can grant protection.' This hadith is cited to support the Sahibayn. Further evidence is provided from a specific hadith narrated by Ali ibn Abi Talib, which explicitly states that a slave has no right to spoils except a small item, but his aman is valid when he gives it. This hadith proves the Sahibayn's position without requiring the slave's combat participation. Finally, the commentary refers to an athar (tradition) of Umar ibn al-Khattab, which also indicates the validity of a slave's aman. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as it is supported by strong textual evidence.

Key Terms
أمان (amān): A grant of security or safe passage given by a Muslim to an enemy combatant, rendering that person's life and property inviolable.
عبد (ʿabd): A male slave who is a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The slave must have participated in combat.
B) The slave must be free.
C) The slave must be a Muslim regardless of combat participation.
D) The slave must be authorized by the Muslim leader.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's position that a Muslim slave's aman is unconditionally valid is the relied-upon view, supported by explicit hadith.

Equality of Horse Breeds and Limit on Multiple Horses
Ruling that all war horses receive equal shares; Imam Abu Yusuf's view on multiple horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that all war horses receive equal shares, and explain Imam Abu Yusuf's position that a fighter only receives shares for two horses even if he brings more.

Core Idea
All war horses are equal; you only get two horse-shares no matter how many horses you bring.

In the distribution of spoils (ghanima), a horseman receives a share for his horse in addition to his own share. But what if the horse is a local pony versus a purebred Arabian? And what if he brings several horses? This lesson from a classical Hanafi text first affirms that all horses fit for war are equal. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf's view that a fighter receives shares for only two horses, supported by a mursal hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states that local ponies (baradhin) and Arabian horses (itaq) are equal in receiving shares. This is the default position.
Proof is an athar from Hasan al-Basri.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf introduces a ruling about multiple horses: the fighter only receives shares for two horses, not for each additional horse.
3
Examine the evidence
The proof is a mursal hadith from Makhul that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: لا سهم من الخيل الا لفرسين 'No share from horses except for two horses, even if one has a thousand.'
This hadith is zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the implication
The default Hanafi view (possibly of Abu Hanifa) might have awarded shares for each horse, but Imam Abu Yusuf's view limits it to two. The text does not state a rebuttal, suggesting his view is preferred or at least transmitted as an acceptable ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi likely follows Imam Abu Yusuf due to the explicit hadith.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a fighter with three horses gets shares for only two horses, plus one share for himself (total three shares). A fighter with one horse gets two shares (one for himself, one for the horse).
Foot soldiers (raajil) get only one share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۳۸](۵۹) والبراذين والعتاق سواء امام ابو يوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کئی گھوڑے لیکر شریک ہوا ہو تو دو گھوڑوں کے حصے ملیں گے۔
ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث مرسل ہے۔ انه سمع مكحولا يرفعه الى النبي الله يقول لا سهم من الخيل الا لفرسين وان كان معه الف فرس، اذا دخل بها ارض العدو (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب السهام لمخيل، ج خامس ص ۱۸۴، نمبر ۱۹۳۱۶ مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، ٠٥ ا فى الرجل يشهد بالفراس لكم يقسم منها ، ج سادس ، ص ۴۹۵، نمبر (۳۳۱۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زیادہ بھی گھوڑے لیکر شریک ہوں تو دو گھوڑے کے حصے ملیں گے۔
افت راجل : پیدل چلنے والا ، رجل سے مشتق ہے۔ [۳۰۳۸ (۵۹) دیسی گھوڑے اور عربی گھوڑے برابر ہیں۔

اثر میں ہے۔ عن الحسن قال البرذون بمنزلة الفرس (ب) (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ۱۰۳ فی البراذین مالها وكيف يقسم لها، ج سادس، ص ۴۹۴، نمبر ۳۳۱۷۶ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب السهام خیل ، ج خامس، ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۹۳۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دیسی گھوڑا اور عربی گھوڑا دونوں کے حصے برابر ہیں۔
[3038](59) And the ponies (Baradhin) and the Arabian horses (Itaq) are equal. Imam Abu Yusuf says: If someone participates with several horses, he will receive the shares of two horses. His proof is this mursal hadith: 'He heard Makhul raising it to the Prophet (ﷺ) saying: There is no share from horses except for two horses, even if he has a thousand horses with him when he enters the enemy's land.' (Source: Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Saham li al-Khayl, vol. 5, p. 184, no. 19316; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-Rajul Yashhad bi al-Faras hal Yaqsimu minha, vol. 6, p. 495, no. 3319). From this hadith it is understood that even if he participates with many horses, he will only get the shares of two horses. Ift Rajil: A walking person, derived from Rajl. [3038](59) Local horses and Arabian horses are equal. The horses that are used in war but are somewhat short in stature are called Baradhin (local horses), and the tall horses are called Itaq (Arabian horses). Since both are horses and both are used in war, their shares are equal; none is less than the other. There is an Athar: From Hasan who said: 'The pony is in the same position as the horse.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-Baradhin ma laha wa kayfa yuqsamu laha, vol. 6, p. 494, no. 33176; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Saham al-Khayl, vol. 5, p. 185, no. 9318). From this Athar it is understood that the shares of both the local horse and the Arabian horse are equal.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling from the matn states that all horses fit for war, whether local ponies (baradhin) or purebred Arabians (itaq), receive equal shares in the spoils (ghanīma). The proof for this is an athar from al-Hasan al-Basrī that a pony is like a horse. The commentary then presents a dispute from Imam Abu Yusuf regarding a fighter who brings multiple horses: he only gets shares for two horses, regardless of the total number. His evidence is a mursal hadīth from Makhul that the Prophet (ﷺ) said there is no share except for two horses, even if one has a thousand. This suggests that the default Hanafi position (possibly of Abu Hanifa) is different—perhaps only one share is given, or shares for each horse. However, the text does not explicitly state the opposing view; it only records Imam Abu Yusuf's position as a transmitted opinion. The vocabulary note 'Ift Rajil' appears to be an entry explaining the word 'raajil' (foot soldier), though it is placed here. The overall lesson affirms equal shares for horses of any breed and establishes a limit for multiple horses.

Key Terms
براذين (baradhin): Local or non-Arabian horses used in war, often shorter in stature.
عتاق (itaq): Purebred Arabian horses, tall and noble, also used in war.
سهم (sahm): Share in the spoils (ghanīma) allocated to a fighter and his horse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One share for each horse
B) Two shares total (for two horses) regardless of the number

D) No shares for horses

Key Takeaway
All war horses are equal in receiving shares, but a fighter only receives shares for two horses, per Imam Abu Yusuf's view upheld by the mursal hadith.

6 min
No Shares for Pack Animals and Mules
Ruling that pack animals and mules do not receive shares in spoils, with Quranic and Athar proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shares for pack animals and mules in spoils and explain the proof from the Quran and Athar.

Core Idea
Only combat horses earn a share in spoils; pack animals and mules do not.

This lesson clarifies which animals qualify for a regulated share (sahm) in the distribution of spoils (ghanimah). The Hanafi school, based on the Quranic command to prepare horses and the practice of the early Muslims, reserves shares exclusively for combat-capable horses. Pack animals and mules, though useful, are not entitled to a formal share but may receive a discretionary reward from the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and the ruling
Name the two animals explicitly mentioned: al-rahila (pack camel) and al-baghl (mule). State the ruling: no formal share (sahm) is given to them.
The ruling is not that they get nothing, but that they do not receive a regulated share.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Read Surah al-Anfal 8:60, which commands preparation of horses (al-khayl) to frighten the enemy. Understand that the specification of horses implies that only horses are considered for shares.
The verse is used as a proof of limitation (mantuq and mafhum).
3
Examine the Athar proof
Review the Athar from Makhul that the early Muslims did not give shares to mules, ponies, or donkeys. This confirms the practice.
The Athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Understand the distinction between formal share and discretionary reward
The text mentions that the imam may give something (yurḍakh) for service. Distinguish between a regulated share (sahm) and a discretionary grant (razkh).
This distinction is important for practical application.
5
Apply the principle to similar cases
Consider other animals like donkeys or non-combat horses. Use the same reasoning: only combat horses get shares.
The principle extends to all non-combat mounts.

Source Text

[۳۰۳۹] (۶۰) ولا يسهم الراحلة ولا بغل.
بوجھ اٹھانے والے اور خچر کے لئے حصے نہیں ہیں۔
اونٹ وغیرہ جس پر بوجھ لے جایا جاتا ہے اس کو خدمت کے عوض میں کچھ دے سکتے ہیں لیکن گھوڑے کی طرح غنیمت میں با ضابطہ حصہ نہیں ہے۔
آیت میں دشمنوں کو ڈرانے کے لئے گھوڑے پالنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ چونکہ پچھلے زمانے میں گھوڑے ہی سے میدان جنگ جیتے تھے اس لئے گھوڑے کے لئے حصہ رکھا باقی جانوروں کے لئے غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں رکھا۔ اس آیت میں اس کی ترغیب ہے۔ واعدوا لهم ما استطعتم من قوة ومن رباط الخيل ترهبون به عدو الله وعدوكم (ج) ( آیت ۶۰ سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں دشمنوں کو ڈرانے کے لئے گھوڑے پالنے کی ترغیب دی گئی ہے اس لئے غنیمت میں اس کا حصہ ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن مكحول قال كانوا لا يسهمون لبغل ولا ليزدون ولا لحمار (و) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۰۴۰ انی البغل ای شی چھو ، ج سادس، ص ۴۹۵، نمبر ۳۳۱۸۹ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نچر، گدھے اور وہ گھوڑے جو جہاد کے لائق نہیں اس کے لئے غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ہے۔ الراحلة : بوجھ لادنے کے اونٹ ، رحل سے مشتق ہے جس پر کجاوه رکھا جائے، بغل : خچر
[3039](60) And no share is given for a pack camel (al-rahila) nor a mule. For pack animals and mules there are no shares. A camel etc. on which loads are carried can be given something in exchange for service, but unlike a horse, there is no regular share in the spoils. In the verse, the command is to raise horses to frighten the enemy. Since in former times the battlefield was won by horses, a share was kept for the horse; for other animals no share in spoils was kept. This verse encourages that: 'And prepare against them whatever you can of power and of tied horses, to frighten thereby the enemy of Allah and your enemy.' (Surah al-Anfal 8:60). In this verse encouragement is given to raise horses to frighten the enemy, therefore there is a share for it in the spoils. There is an Athar: From Makhul who said: 'They would not give a share to a mule, nor to a pony, nor to a donkey.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-Baghl hal yus'him, vol. 6, p. 495, no. 33189). From this Athar it is learned that there is no share in the spoils for a mule, a donkey, and a horse that is not fit for jihad. Al-Rahila: The camel used for carrying loads, derived from Rahl, on which a saddle is placed. Baghl: Mule.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating that pack animals (such as camels used for transport) and mules do not receive a regulated share (sahm) in the spoils. However, the imam may give them something as compensation for service. The proof is twofold: First, the Quranic verse (8:60) specifically mentions horses for frightening the enemy, indicating that horses are the primary combat mounts. Second, an athar from Makhul reports that the early Muslims did not give shares to mules, ponies, or donkeys. The lesson also defines the terms: 'raahila' is a pack camel, 'baghl' is a mule. The overall principle is that only combat-capable horses earn shares; other animals do not.

Key Terms
الراحلة (al-rahila): A pack camel used for carrying loads, not for riding into battle.
بغل (baghl): Mule, offspring of a horse and donkey, used for transport but not for combat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The mule gets a share only if it is used in combat

Key Takeaway
Only horses that are used for combat receive a formal share in spoils; pack animals and mules do not, though they may be compensated at the imam's discretion.

The Share of a Fighter is Fixed at Entry into Dar al-Harb
Ruling that the share is determined by entry status into enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the share of a fighter whose status changes after entering enemy territory and identify the proof from the Athar.

Core Idea
Your share in ghanimah is locked at the moment you enter the battlefield, regardless of later changes.

This lesson addresses a common question: if a fighter enters battle on foot, then acquires a horse, does he qualify for the horseman's extra share? The Hanafi school has a clear answer anchored in administrative practice: the commander's register at entry is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: a horseman whose horse dies, and a foot soldier who later buys a horse. Note the ruling for each.
2
State the ruling
The share is determined by status at entry into dar al-harb: the horseman gets two shares (for himself and his horse), the foot soldier gets one share, and later changes do not affect entitlement.
The commander records status at entry.
3
Analyze the proof
The dalil is a mursal Athar from Sulayman ibn Musa: the imam writes the horseman as a horseman and the foot soldier as a foot soldier. This confirms entry as the reference point.
Mursal hadith is zanni, but relied upon in this context.
4
Understand the rationale
The rule prevents disputes and uncertainty (gharar) in distribution. The initial registration is the basis because it reflects the fighter's intended contribution.
Also practical for the commander.
5
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
This ruling is unanimous within the Hanafi school and generally accepted (muttafaq alayh) across schools for the entry-based criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۴۰) (۶۱) ومن دخل دار الحرب فارسا فنفق فرسه استحق سهم فارس ومن دخل راجلا فاشترى فرسا استحق سهم راجل
یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دارالحرب میں داخل ہوتے وقت گھوڑ سوار تھا تو گھوڑ سوار کا حصہ یعنی دو یا تین حصے ملیں گے ۔ اور اس وقت پیدل داخل ہوا بعد میں گھوڑ ا خریدا تو پیدل کا ہی حصہ ملے گا۔ امیر داخل ہوتے وقت ہی تحقیق کرتا ہے اور رجسٹر لکھتا ہے کہ یہ کیسے داخل ہو رہا ہے ، گھوڑے کے ساتھ یا پیدل۔اس لئے داخل ہوتے وقت ہی کا اعتبار ہو گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن سليمان بن موسى فى الامام اذا ادرب قال يكتب الفارس فارسا والراجل راجلا له (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، ۱۵۵، الفارس متی یکتب فارسا ، ج سادس، ص ۵۲۷، نمبر ۳۳۵۰۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب میں داخل ہونے کے وقت کا اعتبار ہے۔ نفق : ہلاک ہوا، خرچ ہوا۔
[3040](61) And whoever enters Dar al-Harb as a horseman and his horse dies (nafaqa), he is entitled to the share of a horseman; and whoever enters as a foot soldier and later buys a horse, he is entitled to the share of a foot soldier. This issue is based on the principle that at the time of entering Dar al-Harb, if he was a horseman, he will get the share of a horseman, i.e., two or three shares; and if he entered as a foot soldier and later bought a horse, he will only get the share of a foot soldier. The commander investigates at the time of entry and writes a register of how he is entering, with a horse or on foot. Therefore, the consideration is at the time of entry. There is an Athar proving this: From Sulayman ibn Musa regarding the Imam when he enters the war, he said: 'He writes the horseman as a horseman and the foot soldier as a foot soldier for him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 155, al-Faris mata yuktabu farisan, vol. 6, p. 527, no. 33502). From this Athar it is understood that the time of entering Dar al-Harb is what matters. Nafaq: died, spent.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing that the share of a fighter in spoils is determined by his status at the time he enters the enemy territory (dār al-harb). If he enters as a horseman, he gets two shares (one for himself and one for his horse) or three (if the horse gets two? Actually the text says 'two or three shares' but the standard Hanafi position is two shares for a horseman; the 'three' might be a variant or a misunderstanding. The key point: subsequent events like the horse dying or buying a horse later do not change his entitlement. The proof is an athar from Sulayman ibn Musa that the commander records the fighter's status upon entry. The term 'nafaqa' means the horse perished or was lost. The ruling ensures clarity and prevents disputes, reinforcing that the intended contribution at the start is the measure.

Key Terms
فارس (faris): A horseman, one who enters battle riding a horse.
راجل (rajil): A foot soldier, one who fights on foot.
نفق (nafaqa): To die or be lost; here, reference to the horse dying or perishing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The share of a foot soldier
C) Half the share of a horseman
D) No share because he changed status

Key Takeaway
The share in ghanimah is determined at the moment of entering dar al-harb, not by subsequent changes.

No Shares for Slave, Woman, Dhimmi, or Child in Spoils
Ruling and proof on spoils for non-combatants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distributing spoils to non-combatant categories and identify the hadith proof that allows only a discretionary gratuity.

Core Idea
Only free adult Muslim male fighters receive a fixed share; others may only get a discretionary gift.

This passage addresses who is entitled to a formal share (sahm) in war spoils under Hanafi law. While free adult Muslim male combatants receive a regulated portion, slaves, women, dhimmis, and children who assist in the expedition are not entitled to a share. However, the imam may grant them a discretionary gratuity (yurḍakh) as compensation for their support. The ruling is grounded in a hadith from Ibn Abbas, which clearly separates the categories that receive shares from those that only receive a gift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories
List the four categories mentioned: slave (mamluk), woman (imra'a), dhimmi (non-Muslim subject), and child (sabi).
These are typically present in military camps but are not full combatants.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that none of these categories receive a formal share (sahm) in the spoils. Instead, the imam may give them a small discretionary gift (yurḍakh).
The amount is at the imam's discretion per the text.
3
Examine the Exception
The text says 'but they are given something (yurḍakh) according to what the Imam sees fit.' This distinguishes between a regulated share and a voluntary reward.
The word yurḍakh (يرضخ) implies a portion smaller than a formal share.
4
Locate the Dalil
The proof is a hadith where Ibn Abbas replies to Najda: '...there is nothing for them except that they are given a small gift (yuḥadhā).'
The hadith is transmitted by Muslim, Tirmidhi, and al-Darimi.
5
Analyze the Dalil's Implication
The phrase 'ليس لهما شيء' (there is nothing for them) negates a formal share; 'إلا أن يحذيا' (except that they are given a gift) permits a gratuity but confirms no share.
This shows the ruling is based on explicit sunnah.

مال غنیمت میں جس طرح مرد مجاہد کا با ضابطہ حصہ ہوتا ہے اس طرح غلام ، عورت، ذمی اور بچے کا حصہ نہیں ہوگا۔ البتہ خدمت کے مرد ہوتا اور البتہ مطابق امام جو مناسب سمجھے اتنا ان کو دیدے۔

Just as a male fighter has a formal share in the spoils, a slave, woman, dhimmi, and child will not have a share. However, the imam may give them something according to what he deems appropriate. There is a hadith: Najda ibn 'Amir al-Haruri wrote to Ibn 'Abbas asking him about the slave and the woman who attend the spoils: is a share allotted to them? ... 'You write asking me about the woman and the slave attending the spoils: is anything allotted to them? And indeed there is nothing for them except that they are given a small gift (yuḥadhā).' This hadith...
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating that four categories of people who may be present in a military expedition do not receive a regulated share (sahm) in the spoils: slaves, women, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state), and children. However, the imam may give them a discretionary gratuity (yurḍakh or yuḥdhā) for their services, such as nursing, cooking, or other support. The proof is a hadith in which Ibn 'Abbas replies to Najda that these categories receive nothing except a little gift. The term 'yurḍakh' means to give something small, not a formal share. This ruling reflects that shares are reserved for adult free Muslim male combatants who actively fight. Others may assist but do not have a legal entitlement.

Key Terms
مملوك (mamluk): A slave, owned person, not entitled to spoils shares.
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state under protection (dhimma).
يرضخ (yurḍakh): To give a small, discretionary gratuity, not a formal share.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, only adult free Muslim male combatants are entitled to a formal share of spoils; others may receive a discretionary gift but not a share.
