Ruling on Property of a Dhimmi Who Becomes a Harbi
Ruling on debts and trusts of a dhimmi turned harbi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings on debts and trusts of a dhimmi who becomes a harbi when killed versus when he dies naturally, and apply the Hanafi principle of prior possession to determine the status of property.

Core Idea
A slain harbi's property becomes spoils, but debts stay with the creditor due to prior possession.

This passage from Kitab al-Siyar addresses the complex legal status of a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim) who betrays his covenant and becomes a harbi (enemy combatant). The central question is: what happens to his debts and property held in trust by Muslims? The Hanafi school answers by applying the principle of prior possession (sabaqa), supported by authentic hadith. You will learn to distinguish between two scenarios — killed in battle versus natural death — and understand the rationale behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage considers two possibilities: the dhimmi-turned-harbi is killed in battle, or he dies naturally. The ruling on his debts and trust property differs based on his manner of death.
The manner of death determines whether his property becomes spoils (ghanimah) or remains his personal property, passing to his heirs.
2
Extract the ruling for debts when killed
If the harbi is killed, debts he owed to Muslims do not become spoils; they remain with the creditor. The creditor's prior possession of the debt (as a claim) protects it from being seized as ghanimah.
The hadith: 'Whoever precedes to something... it is his' is the proof.
3
Extract the ruling for trust property when killed
Property held in trust for the harbi by a Muslim becomes spoils and is distributed among the mujahidin. Since the trust property is effectively owned by the harbi and no one else has possession of it, it falls under ghanimah.
This is contrasted with the debt: the creditor has possession, so the debt is not spoils.
4
Extract the ruling if the harbi dies naturally
If the dhimmi dies a natural death (without fighting), his debts and trust property go to his heirs. His property never became spoils because he was not killed in battle, and his ownership remained intact.
This scenario shows that the key factor is the manner of death and whether the property was seized by force.
5
Apply the principle of prior possession
The underlying principle is that prior possession (sabaqa) gives ownership. The creditor's possession of the debt protects it; the trust property has no such possessor, so it becomes spoils.
This principle is derived from the hadith of Asma' b. Mudarris and applied consistently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
الدار فقتل سقطت دیونه وصارت الوديعة فينا [ ۳۰۵۳(۷۴) وما اوجف عليه
سے قبضہ ہے اس لئے قرض والے کے پاس ہی رہ جائے گا۔ اس سے واپس لیکر مال غنیمت میں تقسیم نہیں کیا جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابيها اسمر بن مضرس قال اتيت النبي الله فبايعته فقال من سبق الى ما لم يسبقه اليه سلم فهو له (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اقطاع الارضین میں ۷۸ نمبر ۳۰۷۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس کا پہلے قبضہ ہو جائے وہ مال اسی کا ہے۔
اور امانت کا مال کسی کے قبضے میں نہیں ہے وہ تو حقیقت میں حربی ہی کا ہے اس لئے وہ غنیمت میں آکر مجاہدین میں تقسیم ہو گا۔ او پر ابن ابی العقیق والی حدیث میں گزرا کہ عہد توڑنے کی وجہ سے و قتل کیا گیا اور اس کی اولا داور بیوی قید کر لی گئی ۔ عن ابن عمران
النبي الله قاتل اهل خيبر فغلب على الارض والنخل ... فوجدوا المسك فقتل ابن ابی الحقیق وسبى نساء هم وذراريهم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی حکم ارض خیبر، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عہد توڑنے والے کا مال غنیمت ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہودیوں کے ساتھ شرط یہ تھی کہ کوئی چیز چھپائے نہیں۔ اور ابن ابی الحقیق نے حی بن اخطب کا مشک چھپایا اور عہد توڑا اس لئے وہ
قتل کیا گیا۔
اور اگر یہ ذمی جو حر بی بنا تھا خود مرا تو اس کا قرض کا مال اور امانت کا مال اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ میدان میں جنگ کے لئے نہیں آیا یا اس کے ملک پر غلبہ نہیں ہوا تو ا کا مال غنیمت نہیں ہوا بلکہ اس کی ملکیت بحال رہی ۔ اس لئے اس کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو گا۔
اسرو : قید کیا گیا، مشتق ہے امیر سے، فیا : مال غنیمت۔
The Book of Siyar. Regarding the house, if he is killed, his debts are dropped and the trust becomes ours. [ 3053(74) and what is spurred upon] from which possession, therefore it remains with the creditor. It will not be taken back and divided in the spoils. (2) There is a hadith: From Abu Asma' b. Mudarris who said: I came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and pledged allegiance to him. He said: Whoever precedes to something that no one has preceded him to, it is his. (a) (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on granting land, hadith 3071) This hadith indicates that whoever takes possession first owns that property. And the trust property is not in anyone's possession; actually it belongs to the harbi, therefore it will become part of the spoils and be distributed among the mujahidin. Earlier, in the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Haqiq, it passed that due to breaking the treaty he was killed and his children and wife were captured. From Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet, peace be upon him, fought the people of Khaybar and conquered the land and palm trees... then they found musk, so Ibn Abi al-Haqiq was killed and their women and children were captured. (b) (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the ruling of Khaybar land, hadith 3006) This hadith indicates that the property of one who breaks a treaty becomes spoils. Because the condition with the Jews was that they would not hide anything. And Ibn Abi al-Haqiq hid the musk of Hayy b. Akhtab and broke the treaty, so he was killed. And if this dhimmi who had become a harbi dies naturally, then his debt property and trust property will go to his heirs. Because he did not come to the battlefield for war, nor was his land conquered, so his property did not become spoils, but his ownership remained. Therefore, after his death, it will be distributed among his heirs. Asru: captured, derived from amir; fiya: spoils.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the property status of a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state) who becomes a harbi (enemy combatant) by joining the enemy. The passage distinguishes two scenarios: (1) if the dhimmi is killed in battle, and (2) if he dies naturally. For the first scenario: debts owed by the harbi are dropped (do not become spoils) and remain with the creditor because the creditor already possesses them. However, property held in trust (amanah) for him by Muslims is considered his property and since it is in the possession of no one (effectively belonging to the harbi), it becomes part of the ghanimah (war spoils) and is distributed among the mujahidin. The proof is the hadith of Asma' b. Mudarris: prior possession establishes ownership; the creditor already possesses the debt, but the trust property is not possessed by anyone, so it goes to the spoils. A second hadith about Ibn Abi al-Haqiq from Khaybar is cited: the Prophet killed him and enslaved his family because he broke the treaty by hiding musk, indicating that a treaty-breaker's property becomes spoils. For the second scenario: if the dhimmi dies naturally without fighting, his debts and trusts go to his heirs, as his property remained his own. The lexical note explains 'asru' (captured) and 'fiya' (spoils). All rulings are within the Hanafi framework.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): An enemy combatant non-Muslim, as opposed to a dhimmi who has a treaty.
أمانت (amanah): Property held in trust by a Muslim on behalf of another.
غنيمت (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken by force from enemy combatants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dhimmi becomes a harbi, is killed in battle, and had a debt owed to a Muslim, what happens to that debt?
A) It becomes part of the war spoils and is distributed to mujahidin.
B) It is forgiven and the creditor loses the right to claim it.
C) It remains with the creditor because the creditor already possesses the debt.
D) It goes to the harbi's heirs.

Key Takeaway
Prior possession (sabaqa) determines ownership: debt remains with creditor; trust property becomes spoils if the harbi is killed, but goes to heirs if he dies naturally.

Ghanimah and Fay: Definitions and Ruling on Disposal
Definitions and ruling with scriptural proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ghanimah (spoils taken by force) and fay (wealth from peace treaties) and state the Hanafi ruling on the distribution of each.

Core Idea
Spoils taken by force (ghanimah) are divided: one-fifth to the treasury, four-fifths to fighters; wealth obtained peacefully (fay) is entirely for public welfare.

In this passage, the author of Al-Sharh al-Thamiri clarifies two distinct categories of wealth obtained from the enemy: ghanimah, taken through combat, and fay, acquired without fighting through peace treaties. The Hanafi school treats these categories differently, and the passage provides the key rulings along with their scriptural proofs. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of war booty in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Define the two terms
State the definition of ghanimah (spoils taken by force from the enemy during battle) and fay (wealth obtained without fighting, such as through peace treaties). Note the source text's explanation that ghanimah involves 'taking possession by force' while fay results from a peace agreement.
The Arabic root of fay' implies 'return' – wealth that returns to the Muslims without conflict.
2
State the ruling on distribution
For ghanimah: one-fifth (khums) is given to the ruler to spend as Allah commanded, and four-fifths are distributed among the soldiers who participated. For fay: the entire amount is spent on the interests of the Muslims (مصالح المسلمين), similar to kharaj, and no khums is taken.
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) upon the imam to implement.
3
Identify the key difference
The distinction hinges on whether the wealth was obtained by force (عنوة) or by peace (صلح). Ghanimah requires active fighting and possession; fay does not.
The passage cites a report from 'Abd al-Razzaq that emphasizes the two are different.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof for fay
The author cites Surah al-Hashr 59:7, which specifies that fay belongs to Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, and travelers. The phrase 'so that it does not circulate only among the rich' indicates it is not to be divided as spoils but spent broadly.
This verse is the primary textual evidence for the unique treatment of fay.
5
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadith are presented: (1) A hadith from Abu Hurayrah distinguishing towns conquered by Allah and His Messenger (fay) from those conquered by Muslims by force (ghanimah with khums). (2) The peace treaty of Najran where the entire payment was fay, with no khums taken. Both support the distinction.
The hadith from Abi Dawud about Najran shows practical application of the rule.

فرمایا نئی اور نیمت الگ الگ مال ہیں۔ نقیمت اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ مسلمان نے کفار سے قبضے میں لیا۔ اس کا نفس امیر کو دیا جاتا ہے۔ اللہ نے اس کو جیسا حکم دیا وہاں خرچ کرے۔ اور باقی چار ٹس ان لوگوں کے لئے ہے جنہوں نے غنیمت حاصل کی۔ اور فی یہ ہے کہ امام اور کفار کے درمیان صلح کی وجہ سے کفار کی ذات پر، اس کی زمین پر اور اس کی کھیتی پر لازم ہو، جس مال پر بھی صلح ہوئی ہو جس کو مسلمانوں نے بزور طاقت نہ لی ہو اور نہ اس پر قبضہ کیا ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ آپس میں صلح ہوگئی ہو۔ یہ صلح کا مال امام کی ذمہ داری ہے کہ اللہ نے جیسا حکم دیا وہاں خرچ کرے (ب) اللہ نے اپنے رسول کو جو کچھ اہل قری کافی دیا تو وہ اللہ اور رسول آدھار جب میں مسلمان کو ادا کریں گے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, 294: Book of Military Expeditions. That which the Muslims acquire from the property of the people of war without fighting is spent on the interests of the Muslims just as kharaj is spent. [When] the Muslims take possession from the disbelievers, one-fifth thereof goes to the ruler to place where Allah has commanded, and the remaining four-fifths are for those who took the spoils (ghanimah). Fay is whatever results from a peace treaty between the imam and the disbelievers regarding their persons, lands, and crops, and whatever is agreed upon in peace that the Muslims did not take by force, nor take possession of, nor overcome until peace was made between them. He said: That peace treaty is the imam's discretion; he places it where Allah has commanded. (a) (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on Ghanimah and Fay being different, vol. 5, p. 1310, no. 9715) This report explains that ghanimah and fay wealth are different and states that wealth from peace treaties is called fay. Fay is to be spent on the affairs of the Muslims, and its proof is this verse: 'What Allah has bestowed upon His Messenger from the people of the towns belongs to Allah, to the Messenger, to the near of kin, to the orphans, to the needy, and to the traveler, so that it does not circulate only among the rich among you' (b) (Surah al-Hashr 59:7). This verse shows that there is no khums (one-fifth) in it, nor is it distributed among the mujahideen; rather it is spent in the interests of the community. (2) The hadith supports this: From Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whatever town is conquered by Allah and His Messenger belongs to Allah and His Messenger. Whatever town is conquered by the Muslims by force, one-fifth thereof is for Allah and His Messenger, and the remainder is for those who fought for it.' (c) (Sunan al-Sabiqi? [likely al-Bayhaqi], chapter on division of known lands, vol. 9, p. 234, no. 18393) This hadith states that what the mujahideen conquered has four shares for the mujahideen, and what was not conquered by the mujahideen but the enemy made peace out of fear is all for the Muslims and spent in their interests. (3) A hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah made peace with the people of Najran for fay: half in Safar and half in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims. (d) (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on taking jizya, vol. 2, p. 74, no. 3041) This hadith shows that in the peace treaty with Najran, no khums was taken and no distribution to the mujahideen; rather the entire wealth served the Muslims. 'Awf: to race horses; here meaning to collect wealth by racing. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Thawri said: Fay and ghanimah are separate wealth. Ghanimah is what the Muslims took possession from the disbelievers. Its one-fifth is given to the ruler to spend where Allah commanded, and the remaining four parts are for those who obtained ghanimah. Fay is what becomes obligatory upon the disbelievers, their land, and their crops due to a peace treaty between the imam and the disbelievers, over any wealth that a peace treaty was made, which the Muslims did not take by force nor take possession of, until peace was made. This peace treaty wealth is the imam's responsibility to spend where Allah commanded. (b) Allah bestowed upon His Messenger from the people of the towns, so it is for Allah and the Messenger and the near of kin and the orphans and the needy and the traveler so that it does not become a circulating state among the rich. (c) He said: Any town conquered by Allah and His Messenger is for Allah and His Messenger. Any town conquered by the Muslims by force, its one-fifth is for Allah and His Messenger and the remainder is for those who fought there. (d) He made peace with the people of Najran for two thousand halas: half in Safar and half in Rajab, which they would pay to the Muslims.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage defines two types of war booty in Hanafi fiqh: ghanimah (spoils taken by force) and fay (wealth obtained through peace treaties without fighting). The ruling is that ghanimah is divided: one-fifth (khums) is given to the ruler for public welfare, and four-fifths are distributed among the soldiers who participated in the battle. Fay, on the other hand, is entirely placed in the treasury and spent on the general interests of the Muslims, similar to kharaj (land tax). The author provides three proofs: first, the Quranic verse (59:7) which distributes fay among specified categories and explicitly states it should not circulate only among the rich; second, a hadith distinguishing between towns conquered by God and the Prophet (which become fay) versus those conquered by Muslims (which become ghanimah with khums); third, the peace treaty of Najran where the entire payment was fay, not divided among the fighters. The footnote clarifies that according to Sufyan al-Thawri, fay and ghanimah are distinct categories. The annotation also explains the term 'awf as gathering wealth by racing horses, which is a minor philological note.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanīmah): Spoils taken by force from the enemy during battle.
الفئ (al-fay’): Wealth obtained from the enemy without fighting, e.g., through peace treaties.
الخمس (al-khums): The one-fifth share of ghanimah allocated to the ruler for public welfare.
مصالح المسلمين (maṣāliḥ al-muslimīn): The general interests and welfare of the Muslim community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is fay (wealth from peace treaties) to be disposed of?
A) One-fifth to the state, four-fifths to the fighters.
B) Entirely spent on Muslim interests, not distributed among fighters.
C) Given entirely to the imam for his personal use.
D) Divided equally among all adult Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Ghanimah (spoils from fighting) is divided into khums and four-fifths for fighters; fay (wealth from peace) is entirely for public welfare.

Prohibition of Building New Places of Worship for Dhimmis in Dar al-Islam
Ruling with proof from hadith and athar forbidding new places of worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building new churches/synagogues for dhimmis in Dar al-Islam and identify the proof from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
New churches and synagogues cannot be built in Muslim-founded cities to prevent propagation of other religions.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling regarding the status of non-Muslim places of worship in an Islamic state. The prohibition is not arbitrary but based on prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions, aimed at preserving the dominance of Islam. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of religious freedom for dhimmis under classical Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is building a new church (kanīsah) or synagogue (bīʿah) in Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi ruling is that it is not permissible (ja'iz nahi hai).
The ruling applies specifically to new constructions, not to maintenance of existing places.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith narrated by Ibn Abbas: 'La taslahu qiblatan fi ard wahidah wa laysa 'ala al-muslimin jizyah' (No two qiblas are suitable in one land, and there is no jizya upon Muslims).
This hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'qiblatan' (two qiblas) is interpreted as two religions having equal status. The prohibition indicates that Islam should not be brought to parity with other faiths, so building places of worship for other religions is forbidden.
This interpretation is based on the context and the companion's understanding.
4
Examine the supporting athar
Ibn Abbas also said: 'Every city founded by Muslims, no church or synagogue may be built in it, nor may a bell be rung, nor may pork be sold.' This athar specifies the scope: Muslim-founded cities (amsar al-muslimin).
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Note the scope and exceptions
The prohibition applies to cities founded by Muslims. Old places of worship in such cities may be maintained, and cities originally founded by dhimmis may have different rules.
This narrows the application of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۷۶] (۹۷) دارالاسلام میں یہودی اور نصرانی کا نیا عبادت خانہ بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تش دارالاسلام کے شہروں میں یہودی کا اور نصرانی کا نیا عبادت خانہ نہ بنانے دیا جائے۔ اس سے اس کی شوکت بڑھے گی اور دوسرے دین کی اشاعت ہوگی ۔ اس لئے ان کا نیا عبادت خانہ بنانے کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله لا تصلح قبلتان في أرض واحدة وليس على المسلمين جزية (ج) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء لیس علی المسلمین جزیہ ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۶۳۳، کتاب الزکوۃ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذمیوں کو بہت زیادہ اس کے دین کی اشاعت کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور نیا کنیسہ یا بچہ بنانا دین کی اشاعت ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كل مصر مصره المسلمون لا يبنى فيه بيعة ولا كنيسة ولا يضرب فيه بناقوس ولا يباع فيه لحم خنزير (و) (سن للبیہقی ، باب بیشتر علیهم ان لا حد ثوافی امصار المسلمین کنیتہ ولا مجمعالصلو انتم ولاصوت ناقوس ولا حمل خزر مرولا ادخال خنزیر، ج تاسع ص ۱۳۳۹، نمبر ۱۸۷۱۴ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۷۰ ما قالوا فی حدم البيع والكنائز وبيوت النار، ج سادس ص ۴۷۱، نمبر ۳۲۹۷۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس شہر کو مسلمانوں نے بسایا ہے اس میں ذمیوں کا نیا عبادت خانہ نہ بنانے دیا جائے۔ حاشیہ : (ج) آپ نے فرمایا ایک ملک میں دو قبلے نہیں ہو سکتے یعنی اسلام اور عیسائیت نہیں رہ سکتے، اور مسلمان پر جزیہ نہیں ہے (د) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا ہر وہ شہر جس کو مسلمانوں نے بسایا ہے اس میں گر جا اور کنیسہ نہیں بنایا جا سکتا۔ اور نہ اس میں ناقوس بجایا جاسکتا ہے۔ اور نہ اس میں سور کا گوشت بیچا جا سکتا ہے۔
[3076] (97) In Dar al-Islam, building a new place of worship for Jews and Christians is not permissible. In the cities of Dar al-Islam, Jews and Christians should not be allowed to build a new place of worship. Because this would increase their prestige and propagate their religion. Therefore, permission for a new place of worship is not given. There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Two qiblas cannot be in one land, and there is no jizya upon Muslims.' (c) (Tirmidhi, chapter: what has come about no jizya upon Muslims, p. 138, no. 633, Book of Zakat). From this hadith it is understood that dhimmis should not be allowed to propagate their religion excessively. And building a new church or synagogue is propagation of religion, so it is not permitted. (2) There is a narration: from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Every city founded by Muslims, no church or synagogue may be built in it, nor may a bell be rung, nor may pork be sold.' (d) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: imposing conditions upon them that they do not build new churches or places of assembly for prayer or sound bells or carry pigs or introduce pork, vol. 9, p. 1339, no. 18714; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 6, p. 471, no. 32972). From this narration it is understood that in a city founded by Muslims, no new place of worship for dhimmis may be built. Footnote: (c) He said: Two qiblas cannot be in one land, meaning Islam and Christianity cannot coexist, and there is no jizya upon Muslims. (d) Ibn Abbas said: Every city founded by Muslims, no church or synagogue may be built in it, nor may a bell be rung, nor may pork be sold.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof prohibiting the construction of new places of worship for dhimmis in Dar al-Islam. The prohibition is based on the hadith 'Two qiblas cannot be in one land,' which indicates that Islam should not be challenged by the open display of other religions. Additionally, the narration from Ibn Abbas specifies that in Muslim-founded cities, building churches or synagogues, ringing bells, and selling pork are forbidden. The reasoning is to prevent the propagation of disbelief and maintain the dominance of Islam. Note that this does not apply to cities originally founded by dhimmis under Muslim rule, where old places of worship may be maintained.

Key Terms
بيعة (bīʿah): A Jewish place of worship (synagogue)
كنيسة (kanīsah): A Christian place of worship (church)
قبلتان (qiblatān): Two qiblas, referring to two dominant religions with distinct places of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible with permission
B) Prohibited
C) Permitted if no mosque is nearby
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Building new churches and synagogues in Muslim-founded cities is prohibited in the Hanafi school to prevent the propagation of disbelief.

Rebuilding Collapsed Old Places of Worship of Dhimmis
Ruling on rebuilding old dhimmi places of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rebuilding collapsed old places of worship of dhimmis and explain the evidence from the treaty of Najran.

Core Idea
Old non-Muslim places of worship are protected by treaty; rebuilding after collapse is part of that protection.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: if a Jewish or Christian place of worship that existed before Islamic rule collapses due to natural causes, may the dhimmi community rebuild it? The Hanafi school answers in the affirmative, based on the Prophet's treaty with the Christians of Najran. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of protection afforded to non-Muslim religious sites under Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the rebuilding of a collapsed old place of worship belonging to dhimmis. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz).
Note that this only applies to old (pre-existing) places, not new construction.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of the treaty of Najran, where the Prophet made a pact with the Christians of Najran. The key phrase is 'on condition that their churches would not be demolished'.
The treaty is recorded in Abu Dawood and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of demolishing churches implies protection of the existing structure. If a church collapses, rebuilding it is a continuation of that protection, not new construction.
This is an inference from the general condition of non-demolition.
4
Note the limitations
The permission is conditional: the place must be old (established before Islamic rule), it must have collapsed naturally, and the dhimmis must be under a valid treaty of protection.
If the place was built after the Islamic conquest, it may not be rebuilt without permission.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling is based on a hadith (zanni al-thubut wa al-dalalah) and is part of the established Hanafi position. No major intra-madhhab dispute is recorded.
The ruling is considered relied upon (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۷۷] (۹۸) اگر پھر منہدم ہو جائیں پرانی گر جائیں تو دوبارہ بنا سکتے ہیں۔ یہودی یا نصرانی کا پرانا عبادت خانہ گر گیا تو اس کو دوبارہ بنایا جاسکتا ہے۔ جو پہلے سے ہے اس کی حفاظت کی ذمہ داری مسلمانوں پر ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو دوبارہ بنایا جا سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے اہل نجران سے صلح میں یہ بات طے ہوئی تھی کہ گر جائیں نہیں گرائیں گے۔ ان کے راہبوں کو نہیں نکالیں گے۔ اور ان کے دین کے بارے میں فتنے میں نہیں ڈالیں گے۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال صالح رسول الله الله الله اهل نجران على الفي حلة ... على ان لا تهدم لهم بيعة ولا يخرج لهم قس ولا يفتنوا عن دينهم مالم يحدثوا حدثا أو يأكلوا الربا (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اخذ الجزية ، ص۷۴، نمبر ۳۰۴ سفن للمتقی ، باب لا تهدم هم کنیسه ولا بیعته ، ج تاسع، ص ۳۳۹، نمبر ۱۸۷۱۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پرانی عبادت گاہیں بنا سکتے ہیں۔
[3077] (98) If they collapse, the old ones, they fall down, then they can rebuild them. If a Jew or Christian's old place of worship falls down, it can be rebuilt. The responsibility of protecting what already exists is upon the Muslims. Therefore, it can be rebuilt. (2) There is a hadith: In the treaty with the people of Najran, it was agreed that they would not be demolished; their monks would not be expelled; and they would not be tried regarding their religion. The part of the hadith is: from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah made a treaty with the people of Najran for two thousand garments... on condition that their churches would not be demolished, nor their priests expelled, nor would they be tried regarding their religion as long as they do not commit a crime or consume usury (a) (Abu Dawood, chapter on taking jizya, p. 74, no. 304; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: do not demolish their churches or synagogues, vol. 9, p. 339, no. 18715). From this hadith it is understood that they can rebuild old places of worship.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling that old places of worship belonging to dhimmis may be rebuilt if they collapse. The proof is the treaty of the Prophet with the Christians of Najran, which guaranteed the protection of their existing churches. The responsibility of Muslims is to protect what already exists, so rebuilding is allowed. However, this does not permit building new ones, only maintaining old ones.

Key Terms
بيعة (bīʿah): A Jewish place of worship
قس (qiss): A Christian priest or monk
صلح (ṣulḥ): A peace treaty or agreement between Muslims and non-Muslims

Killing an Apostate Before Invitation to Islam
Ruling on killing an apostate before offering Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing an apostate before the invitation to Islam and identify the proofs that establish the apostate's blood as mubah al-dam.

Core Idea
Killing an apostate before da'wah is makruh but carries no penalty — his blood is already permissible.

Islamic law prescribes capital punishment for apostasy, but what if someone kills the apostate before the required invitation to return to Islam? This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri clarifies the Hanafi position: the killer is not liable for qisas or diyah because the apostate's blood is already permissible (mubah al-dam). However, the act of killing without invitation is disliked (makruh) because it bypasses the recommended practice of extending da'wah first. The text presents a series of proofs to establish this ruling, distinguishing between the legal permissibility of killing and the ethical preference for patience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage begins by stating the ruling: if someone kills an apostate before presenting Islam to him, it is makruh (disliked) but no liability (qisas or diyah) falls on the killer. Note that this applies to a private individual, not the state authorities who must follow the proper procedure.
The ruling is specific to the case where invitation has not yet been made.
2
Analyze the proofs: Quranic verse
The author cites Quran 2:217 which states that apostasy nullifies deeds and places the apostate in the rank of disbelievers. This is used as a basis for considering the apostate's blood as permissible, since they are no longer protected by Islam.
The verse is interpreted indirectly — the apostate becomes like a harbi (enemy combatant).
3
Analyze the proofs: Hadith of the Prophet
The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari) is presented as the primary textual evidence for capital punishment of apostates. The absence of any condition for prior invitation in this narration shows that the blood of an apostate is immediately permissible upon apostasy.
Another hadith (Ali and the zindiqs) is also cited but not quoted fully.
4
Analyze the proofs: Practice of the Sahaba
The passage reports two incidents: first, the practice of Mu'adh ibn Jabal who insisted on the immediate execution of an apostate without any mention of invitation; second, the case during Umar's caliphate where a killer was not punished. These show that the Sahaba did not consider invitation as a condition for the permissibility of killing.
These reports serve as supplementary evidence for the Hanafi position.
5
Understand the distinction: legal vs. recommended
The author explains the underlying rationale: presenting Islam to the apostate is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). The killer acted against the recommendation, hence the act is makruh, but since the apostate's blood is already mubah, no criminal liability arises.
This distinguishes between the objective legal status (mubah al-dam) and the subjective ethical praiseworthiness of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب حكم المرتد والمرتدة واستنا تھم ج ۱۰۲۲، نمبر ۶۹۲۳/۶۹۲۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔ [۳۰۸۳) (۱۰۴) پس اگر کسی نے اس کو قتل کر دیا اس پر اسلام پیش کرنے سے پہلے تو یہ مکروہ ہے لیکن قاتل پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔ مرتد پر تین دین اسلام پیش کرنا چاہئے، انکار کرنے پر قتل کرنا چاہئے۔ لیکن اگر اسلام پیش کرنے سے پہلے کسی نے قتل کر دیا تو ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن قاتل سے قصاص تکیہ ڈالا گیا اور فرما یا تشریف رکھئے۔ وہاں ایک آدمی بندھا ہوا تھا، پوچھا یہ کون ہے؟ کہا یہودی تھا پھر اسلام لا یا پھر یہودی ہو گیا۔ کہا تشریف رکھئے ، کہا جب تک اس کو قتل نہیں کریں گے نہیں بیٹھوں گا یہ اللہ اور اس کے رسول کا فیصلہ ہے۔ تین مرتبہ فرمایا۔ پھر حکم دیا پس یہودی قتل کر دیا گیا۔
If a killer kills him before presenting Islam to him, that is disliked for him and there is nothing upon the killer. I am not present, nor did I command it, nor am I pleased with it. From which it is understood that granting a respite of three days is necessary. After three days, the apostate should be killed. There is an indication in the verse: 'And whoever among you turns back from his religion and dies while he is a disbeliever – those have wasted their deeds in this world and the Hereafter, and they are the companions of the Fire; they will abide therein forever' (Al-Baqarah 2:217). This verse indicates that when one apostatizes, all his deeds are wasted and he becomes in the rank of a disbeliever. And it has passed earlier that a harbi (enemy combatant) is one whose blood is permissible, and an apostate is even more severe than a harbi, so his blood is also permissible. (2) In a hadith: 'Ali brought some zindiqs and burned them... because of the saying of the Messenger of Allah: Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' Another narration: Mu'adh said: 'Kill the apostate immediately, or I will not sit down.' The portion of the hadith: From Abu Musa: then Mu'adh ibn Jabal followed him... When he arrived, a cushion was placed for him and he was asked to sit. There was a man tied up. He asked: 'What is this?' It was said: 'He was a Jew, then embraced Islam, then became a Jew.' He said: 'Sit down.' He said: 'I will not sit until he is killed, as the judgment of Allah and His Messenger.' He said it three times, then ordered him to be killed. (Bukhari, bab hukm al-murtadd wa al-murtaddah...). This hadith shows that the apostate is to be killed. [3083(104)] So if someone kills him before presenting Islam to him, it is disliked, but there is nothing upon the killer. For the apostate, Islam should be presented for three days; if he refuses, he should be killed. But if someone kills him before presenting Islam, doing so is disliked. However, qisas will not be taken from the killer, nor will diyah be obligatory. Presenting Islam is mustahabb, and the killer acted contrary to mustahabb, so qisas is not taken from him because the apostate has become one whose blood is permissible. (2) In issue no. 103, the athar of Umar passed, wherein a killer killed before presenting Islam without the command of Amir al-Mu'minin Umar, so Umar did not take qisas from the killer nor did he take diyah; he only expressed regret by saying 'O Allah, I was not present and I did not command.' This shows that qisas will not be taken from the killer. (3) In the hadith of Mu'adh, there is no mention of presenting Islam to the apostate; rather, immediate killing was demanded. This shows that after apostasy, one's blood becomes permissible immediately. (Bukhari, no. 6923) Footnotes: (a) Those among you who apostatize and die as disbelievers... (b) Ali brought some zindiqs and burned them... (c) Mu'adh ibn Jabal came to Abu Musa...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the situation where someone kills an apostate before the obligatory invitation to Islam (da'wah) is made. The first line states the ruling: if a person kills an apostate before presenting Islam to him, it is makruh (disliked) but there is no liability on the killer—neither qisas (retaliation) nor diyah (blood money). The author then explains the reasoning: presenting Islam is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). Since the apostate's blood is already permissible (mubah al-dam) due to apostasy, killing him is legally permitted, albeit contrary to the better practice of inviting him first. The text supports this with several proofs: (1) The Quranic verse 2:217 shows that apostasy nullifies deeds and places one in the category of disbelievers, whose blood may be permissible. (2) The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is cited, as well as the incident of Ali burning zindiqs (heretics). (3) The hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, where he insisted on the immediate execution of a man who had reverted to Judaism without any mention of a prior invitation. (4) The athar (report) of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), where the killer of an apostate was not punished because the apostate's blood was already permissible. The passage also mentions that the apostate should be given a three-day respite to repent, but if killed before that, the killer is not liable. The overall Hanafi position is that killing an apostate is obligatory (wajib) for the state/authorities, but if a private individual kills him without invitation, it is sinful (makruh) but no criminal penalty applies because the apostate is effectively a combatant (harbi) in terms of blood permissibility.

Key Terms
مباح الدم (mubah al-dam): One whose blood is legally permissible to shed without liability
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam and becomes an apostate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone kills an apostate before the invitation to Islam is made, what is the ruling?
A) It is haram and qisas is obligatory
B) It is makruh but no qisas or diyah is due
C) It is permissible and recommended
D) It is wajib and the killer must pay diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the legal permissibility of killing an apostate (blood is mubah) and the ethical preference for inviting him first; killing without invitation is makruh but carries no penalty for the killer.

Female Apostate: Imprisoned Not Killed
Ruling with proof on female apostate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a female apostate and identify the proof (dalil) used to derive it.

Core Idea
A female apostate is imprisoned, not killed — based on the Prophet's prohibition of killing women.

This passage addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the treatment of a female apostate differs from a male. While a male apostate may be executed, a woman is to be imprisoned until she returns to Islam. The ruling is based on an athar from Ibn Abbas and the general principle of not killing women. Understanding this difference highlights how the Hanafi school applies prophetic traditions to specific cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman apostatizing (riddah). The ruling is that she is not killed but imprisoned indefinitely until she repents.
The ruling applies specifically to female apostates; male apostates are treated differently (killed).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar (report) from Ibn Abbas (radiyallahu anhuma) recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
The athar is a qawl sahabi (Companion's statement), which in Hanafi usul is considered a valid source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit words 'la tuqtal' (they are not killed) and 'yuhbasna' (they are imprisoned) directly give the ruling. The imperative 'yujbarn' indicates compulsion to return.
The apparent meaning (zahir) is taken, as there is no contradicting evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools hold that female apostates are killed like males. The Maliki school imprisons and beats but does not kill.
The ikhtilaf stems from different interpretations of the general evidence on apostasy.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the specific athar and the general prohibition of killing women (from hadith), preferring this over analogizing women to men.
The mufta bihi (operative view) is imprisonment, not execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۸۴ (۱۰۵) واما المرأة اذا ارتدت فلا تُقتل ولكن تحبس حتى تسلم [۱۳۰۸۴ (۱۰۵) عورت اگر مرتد ہ ہو جائے تو قتل نہیں کی جائے گی لیکن اسلام لانے تک قید رکھی جائے گی۔ اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لا تقتل النساء اذا ارتددن عن الاسلام ولكن يحبسن ويدعين الى الاسلام ويجبرن عليه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ۳۳ ما قالوانی المرتدة عن الاسلام، ج سادس ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۳۲۷۶۳ سفن للبیہقی ، باب قتل من ارتد عن الاسلام اذا ثبت عليه رجلا كان او امرأة ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۵۳، نمبر ۱۶۸۶۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد ہ عورت قتل نہیں کی جائے گی، بلکہ اس کو تو بہ کرنے تک قید کیا جائے گا۔
As for the woman if she apostatizes, she is not killed but is imprisoned until she accepts Islam. (105) If a woman becomes an apostate, she will not be killed but will be imprisoned until she accepts Islam. There is proof in an athar: From Ibn Abbas: 'Women are not killed when they apostatize from Islam, but they are imprisoned and called to Islam and compelled to it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah... Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) From this athar it is understood that an apostate woman will not be killed, rather she will be imprisoned until she repents.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It distinguishes the treatment of female apostates from male apostates. The primary ruling is that an apostate woman is not executed; rather, she is to be imprisoned indefinitely until she returns to Islam. The proof is an athar (report) from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), which explicitly states that women who apostatize are not killed but are imprisoned and compelled to return to Islam. The Hanafi school adopts this view, relying on the apparent meaning of the hadith and the principle that women are not to be killed in jihad or for apostasy, based on the prohibition of killing women in warfare. The passage also mentions that she is to be called to Islam and even compelled (yujbarn 'alayh), meaning that force may be used to bring her back to Islam, though some scholars interpret this as psychological pressure rather than physical torture. The ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools like the Shafi'i hold that both male and female apostates are to be killed. The authority of the athar is considered strong enough to establish the ruling, and it is part of the accepted tradition.

Key Terms
مرتدة (murtaddah): A female apostate from Islam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a female apostate?
A) She is killed immediately
B) She is imprisoned until she returns to Islam
C) She is exiled
D) She is fined

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that a female apostate is imprisoned, not killed, is derived from a specific athar and the principle of protecting women from execution.

Suspended Ownership of an Apostate's Property
Ruling on the suspended ownership of an apostate's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an apostate's property as suspended (zawal mur'a) and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, applying the ruling to scenarios of repentance and death.

Core Idea
An apostate's property is suspended: restored upon repentance, inherited upon death.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling on the effect of apostasy on property ownership. Unlike immediate confiscation, the Hanafi school treats the removal of ownership as suspended (zawal mur'a), allowing for the possibility of repentance and return of property. We will explore the textual proofs and the practical distinction that arises from this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the passage carefully and identify the exact legal ruling: the apostate's ownership is removed in a suspended manner. Note the condition that if he returns to Islam, his property is restored; if he dies or is executed, it is distributed among Muslim heirs.
The key term is 'zawal mur'a'.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Look at the hadith cited: the Prophet (PBUH) ordered both the execution and the seizure of property of a man who married his stepmother and apostatized. Understand that this indicates the removal of ownership, but the suspension aspect is derived from the possibility of repentance before execution.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the athar of Ali
Consider the athar where Ali (RA) executed an apostate and distributed his property among Muslim heirs. This shows that upon death, ownership is fully removed, but note that the apostate was given a chance to repent first, supporting the suspension idea.
The athar distinguishes between property earned during Islam (inheritance) and during kufr (war booty).
4
Identify the Shafi'i opposition
Understand that the Shafi'i school does not recognize suspension; they hold that the apostate retains ownership until execution. The Hanafi response is that suspension allows for the possibility of repentance, and the hadith shows immediate confiscation upon apostasy (though not final until resolution).
The practical difference (thamarah) is evident only if the apostate repents before execution.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a Muslim who apostatizes and then returns to Islam before any legal action. According to the Hanafi ruling, his property is fully restored. If he dies as an apostate, his Muslim heirs inherit his property (with the distinction for wealth earned during apostasy).
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; in non-Hanafi contexts, different rules may apply.

Source Text

کو بھیجا ہے، ایک آدمی نے اپنی سوتیلی ماں سے شادی کی ہے میں اس کی گردن ماردوں اور اس کا مال لے لوں (ج) حضرت علی کے سامنے مستورد بجلی لایا گیا، وہ اسلام سے مرتد ہو چکا تھا۔ پس اس پر اسلام پیش کیا گیا تو The ownership of the apostate over his property ceases with his apostasy in a suspended manner; if he accepts Islam, his properties return to him. (106) The apostate's ownership will be removed from his property due to apostasy as a suspended removal; so if he accepts Islam, it returns to its state. Because of apostasy, his ownership will be removed. But in such a manner that if he returns to Islam, ownership will be restored. And if he dies (as an apostate), that property will be distributed among his Muslim heirs. There is a hadith: A man married his stepmother and became an apostate; he was ordered to be killed and his property taken. The hadith: From Yazid ibn al-Bara' from his father: My uncle met me while he was carrying a flag. I said: Where are you going? He said: The Messenger of Allah sent me to a man who married his father's wife, to strike his neck and take his property. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, bab mal al-murtadd...; Ibn Majah, bab man tazawwaja imra'ata abihi...) From this hadith it is understood that when one apostatizes, he is killed and his property is taken. (2) An athar: From Ali: Mustawrid al-'Ijli was brought to him; he had apostatized. He presented Islam to him, but he refused. He said: So he killed him and made his inheritance among the Muslim heirs. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) From this athar it is understood that as soon as apostasy occurs, his ownership is removed. However, it will be waited until Islam is presented and he accepts. If he does not accept Islam, ownership is completely removed. And the property earned during Islam will be distributed among Muslim heirs, and property earned during disbelief will be war booty. And if he accepts Islam, his property will be returned to him. If an apostate returns to Islam, his property is returned to him. Footnotes: (a) Ibn Abbas: Women are not killed... (b) My uncle... (c) Ali...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the effect of apostasy on property ownership. The core ruling is that when a person apostatizes, his ownership of property is not immediately and irrevocably removed; rather, it is suspended (zawal mur'a). This means that the ownership is in abeyance: if the apostate returns to Islam, the property reverts to him as if ownership never ceased. If he dies as an apostate (either by execution or natural death), the property is distributed among his Muslim heirs as inheritance. The text provides two proofs: (1) The hadith of the man who married his stepmother, where the Prophet ordered both his execution and the seizure of his property, indicating that apostasy results in loss of property. (2) The athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where he executed an apostate and distributed his property among his Muslim heirs. The passage also makes a distinction: property acquired during the period of Islam goes to Muslim heirs, while property acquired during kufr (i.e., after apostasy) is considered war booty (ghanimah). This reflects the Hanafi view that an apostate's wealth is treated similarly to the wealth of a harbi (enemy combatant) upon his death. However, if he repents, everything is restored. The reasoning is based on the principle that apostasy nullifies the protective covenant of Islam, so the apostate becomes like a harbi in terms of property, but because the apostate may repent, the removal is suspended to allow for return.

Key Terms
زوال مراعى (zawal mur'a): A suspended cessation; ownership is not final until the apostate's status is resolved

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It becomes war booty
B) It is distributed among Muslim heirs
C) It is restored to him
D) It is destroyed

Key Takeaway
An apostate's property is in a state of suspended removal (zawal mur'a) – fully restored if he repents, inherited by Muslim heirs if he dies.

Debts and Transactions of an Apostate
Explaining that apostate's debts are paid from apostasy property and transactions are suspended pending outcome.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the debts and transactions of an apostate and explain why they are suspended.

Core Idea
An apostate's debts are paid from apostasy property; his transactions are suspended pending his return to Islam or death.

When a person leaves Islam, his legal capacity is affected. The Hanafi school teaches that debts incurred during apostasy are distinct from those before, and his transactions are not immediately valid or invalid. Instead, they hang in the balance, awaiting his final state. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and evidence behind this suspension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on debts
The passage states that debts incurred during apostasy are paid from property acquired during apostasy. Note that debts from before apostasy are paid from pre-apostasy wealth.
This separates the two periods.
2
Identify the ruling on transactions
All sales, purchases, and dispositions during apostasy are suspended (mawquf). They become valid if the apostate returns to Islam, but invalid if he dies, is killed, or joins enemy territory.
Suspension is key – not automatic invalidity.
3
Understand the legal status of the apostate
Upon apostasy, the apostate is treated like a dead person in terms of legal capacity. The suspension allows hope for his return, so transactions are held in abeyance.
This is a unique Hanafi position.
4
Examine the primary proof (dalil)
The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari) is cited. The imperative to kill immediately indicates that from the moment of apostasy, the person is legally dead.
Thus, transactions are suspended until the death sentence is carried out or revoked by repentance.
5
Observe the analogical support (athar and qiyas)
An athar about the apostate's wife's waiting period (iddah) shows that marriage is also suspended. This reinforces the general principle of suspension for all transactions.
The school uses analogy from marriage to other contracts.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The debts during his apostasy are paid from what he acquired during apostasy. And whatever he sold, bought, or disposed of from his property during apostasy is suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his contracts are valid; if he dies or is killed or [joins dar al-harb], [the contracts become invalid]. As soon as he becomes an apostate, he is in the status of a dead person. It is only for waiting and hope that the matter is suspended. Its evidence is a hadith: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' And another narration: Mu'adh said, 'I will not sit until he is killed, the judgment of Allah and His Messenger,' three times, and he ordered him to be killed. From this hadith it is understood that as soon as he becomes an apostate, he is in the status of a dead person. Therefore, the debt of Islam is paid from the earnings of Islam, and the debt of apostasy is paid from the earnings of apostasy. [3089 (110)] Whatever he sold, bought, or disposed of in the state of apostasy is all suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his transactions become valid; if he dies, is killed, or flees to dar al-harb, they become invalid. ... (2) There is an indication in the athar: from 'Amir and al-Hakam: concerning a Muslim man who apostatizes and joins enemy territory, his wife observes three menstrual cycles if she menstruates, three months if she does not, and if pregnant, until delivery. His inheritance is divided among his wife and Muslim heirs. Then she may marry; if he returns and repents before her iddah ends, they remain in marriage. From this athar it is understood that the marriage is suspended until the iddah ends. And upon this is qiyas.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first states the ruling: debts incurred during apostasy are paid from property acquired during that same period. Transactions during apostasy are suspended, depending on the final outcome: if the apostate returns to Islam, they become valid; if he dies, is executed, or joins dar al-harb (enemy territory), they become invalid. The commentator explains that upon apostasy, the apostate is legally treated as dead, but the suspension allows hope for his return. The proof is a hadith commanding the killing of apostates, indicating immediate death status. Another athar from 'Amir and al-Hakam regarding the wife's iddah and inheritance shows that marriage is suspended until the iddah ends, analogically to other transactions. Thus, all dealings during apostasy are suspended pending repentance or death.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who has left Islam for another religion or atheism.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended pending a future event (return to Islam or death).
ردة (riddah): Apostasy, the act of leaving Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An apostate's transactions are suspended pending his final state: valid if he returns, invalid if he dies or joins enemy territory.

Female Apostate's Transactions Are Valid
Ruling with rational proof for female apostate's transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a female apostate's transactions and distinguish this ruling from the male apostate's case.

Core Idea
A female apostate's transactions are valid because she must live and support herself.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling specific to female apostates (murtaddah). Unlike a male apostate who may face execution, a female apostate is kept alive in hope of repentance. The Hanafi school logically extends this principle to permit her business dealings, ensuring she can earn a livelihood. This ruling highlights how necessity (darurah) shapes legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a female apostate disposing of her property (tasarruf) during apostasy. The ruling is that her disposition is valid (jā'iz).
This includes buying, selling, and other contracts.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The proof is rational (dalīl aqlī): since she is not killed but kept alive to repent, she must be able to earn a living. Necessity permits otherwise prohibited transactions.
This is an istiḥsān based on need, not a direct textual proof.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalālah)
The ruling stems from the preservation of life (ḥifẓ al-nafs). If she cannot transact, she would face hardship, contradicting the Islamic principle of removing difficulty.
The Hanafi school often uses necessity to override general prohibitions.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Some scholars analogise to a male apostate, whose transactions are suspended. They argue apostasy removes legal capacity. The Hanafis distinguish based on the gender-specific consequence of punishments.
The practical difference: a female apostate can freely transact; a male apostate's transactions are suspended until repentance or execution.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjīḥ
The Hanafi position is relied upon (muftā bihī) because it harmonises the rules of apostasy (preserving her life) with the need to avoid hardship.
Later Hanafi authorities affirm this ruling in al-Fatāwā al-Hindiyyah and other works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرتدة اذا تصرفت في مالها في حال ردّتها جاز تصرفها 
مردہ عورت اپنی ردت کے زمانے میں تصرف کرے تو اس کا تصرف جائز ہے۔ جب مردہ عورت کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ تو بہ کرنے تک زندہ رکھا جائے گا تو ظاہر ہے کہ بیع وشراء کی بھی اجازت ہونی چاہئے ورنہ تو زندگی کیسے گزارے گی۔ اس لئے اس کو اپنے مال میں تصرف کی اجازت ہوگی۔
And the female apostate if she disposes of her property during her apostasy, her disposition is valid. If the female apostate disposes during the time of her apostasy, her disposition is permissible. Since a female apostate is not killed, but kept alive until she repents, it is obvious that she must be allowed to buy and sell; otherwise how would she earn a living? Therefore, she is allowed to dispose of her property.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage gives a specific ruling for a female apostate. Unlike a male apostate who may be executed if he does not repent, a female apostate is only imprisoned and beaten to encourage repentance, but never killed. Therefore, she remains legally alive and must be able to support herself. Consequently, all her business transactions (buying, selling, etc.) during apostasy are valid and not suspended. This is based on necessity and practical need.

Key Terms
مرتدة (murtaddah): A female apostate from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the transactions of a female apostate valid during her apostasy, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because she is not killed, so she needs to earn a living.
B) Because her husband is still Muslim.
C) Because she is allowed to inherit.
D) Because she is considered a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
A female apostate's transactions are valid because she retains legal capacity out of necessity for survival.
